de la cure des emorroydes	of the cure for hemorrhoidsAnd si li fai   .i . cautere sus la tete , et  .i . cautere de costé , et  .ij . cauteres entor la cheville subtilz a tout  .i . cautere clavile subtil ; car li cure est profitans a ceus qui sont desaloiez de lor leu .de la cure des emorroydes
Quant les emorroydes sont ou fondement, ou une ou plusors, et sont ancienes et sont de grosses humors froides et moistes corrumpues, et sont curees si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie, si fai cauteres: .iij. sus l’espine dou dos, celi qui est tout defuers desoz almecdate poc et poc en triangulant, et .i. cautere desoz la boude. ij. dois;	When hemorrhoids are in the rectum, one or more, and are old and consist of thick, cold, moist humors, and are treated as we have described in divisions, but are not helped, then make cauteries: three on the spine of the back, that is, all below the buttocks, little by little, triangulating them; and two cauteries under the tailbone.
et se tu penses que ses estomac soit refroidiez, et li viande ne cuise, et on voit enfler la faice, adonques li faice on .i. grant cautere sus le stomac, si com il est devant dit, et .i. autre sus le foie, et i. autre sus la mice a tout le cautere clavile; et laisse le cautere overt lonc tens. Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you think the stomach is cold, and the food is not digesting, and one sees swelling in the face, then on the face place one large cautery over the stomach, as has been said before, and one over the liver, and one over the navel, with the whole cautery clave; and leave the cautery open for a long time. Afterward treat the area until it is healed.
de la charnositeit qui est nommee «thelul»	of the fleshiness which is named "thelul."
Quant tu copes althelul, si eschaufe le cautere qui semble .i. raseur, et puis le met tout embraseit sus cel althelul copeit; et i laisse tant ta main que li cauteres viegne a la naissance de la voine, de coi li sans cort; fai ceu une fois ou .ij., et s’il i a mout d’althelul, si cauterize chaicun si com nos avons dit; aprés les cure d’oignemens profitans tant qu’il soient sanez; et se tu cauterizes d’un cautere grant sus alchatim, si avra plus grant aide.	When you scrape the "thelul", heat the cautery which resembles a razor, and then place it fully heated on the scraped "thelul"; and hold your hand so that the cauteries reach the source of the vein, from which the blood flows; do this once or twice, and if there is a lot of "thelul," cauterize each one as we have said; afterward treat them with healing ointments until they are healed; and if you cauterize with a large cautery on the scrotum, it will be of greater aid.
de plaie mal curee	of poorly healed wound
Quant li malaides ne puet soffrir tailleure ne overture, que nos raconterons en son leu, si vient teil maladie que ne puet estre sanee fuer que par cautere.	When the patient cannot endure cutting or opening, which we will discuss in its place, then such a disease comes that it cannot be healed except by cautery.
Quant a aucun vient fistule, et est enveillie et giete porriture et moistors corrumpues, si la doies prover a tot une tente subtil, et garde que tu saiches a tot la tente combien elle a de parfont. Aprés eschaufe le cautere qui semble .i. raseur, et le boute en la fistule selonc la quantiteit que li tente i est entrée, et rencomence lou cautere tant que cil cors porris et corrumpus soient ars, une fois, ou .ij. ou .iij., selonc la quantiteit de som besoing; et te warde d’ardre lé nerf qui sunt enqui, et des grans voinnes. se li fistule vait au cors de la vesie et a l’intestine, si te warde de ces leus, et ne faire ceu fuers que en leu charnut, et pense qu’ele n’est mie persans; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez, et se li leus est saielez, et les matieres sont ostees lonc tens, adonc saiches que li leus est sanez entierement; et se les matieres ne sont ostees, saiche que li leus est troez, et corrumpus li os au font; et ensi com un de ces que nos dirons en son leu.	When there is a fistula and it is suppurating and discharging putrid corrupt matter, then you should probe it with a thin wire, and be careful to go as deep as the tent goes. Then heat the cautery like a razor and insert it into the fistula according to how far the tent went in, and repeat the cautery until the pus and corruption are burnt up, once or twice or thrice, according to how much is needed; and be careful not to burn any nerves or major blood vessels. If the fistula goes towards the bladder or intestines, then beware of those places, and do not go near them, but only on the flesh, and think that it is not feeling anything. After that, cleanse the wound until it is healed, and if the wound is suppurating and the matter has been discharged for a long time, then know that the wound is completely healed. But if the matter has not been discharged, know that the wound is through and the bone at the bottom is rotten; and in this way, do as one of those which we will discuss in their place.
de la maladie des reins	of the disease of the kidneys
Quant dolor de froit vient as rains, et de grosse ventositeit, et ne prent talant de femme, adonc covient il que tu li fais cautere sus les rains d’une part et d’autre au cautere clavile que nos avons devant dit; et se nos le cauterizons em mileu, si avra .iij. cauteres en ligne, et se feront plus grant aide.	When cold pain comes with rain and strong winds, and takes hold of a woman, then you must make a cautery on the rains on both sides using the key cautery that we mentioned earlier; and if we cauterize it in the middle, there will be three cauteries in a line, and they will provide greater relief.
de la vessie	of the bladder
Quant li vessie est mole et foible de froit et de moistor, si que li malaides retient l’urine, adonc li fai cautere en la partie defuers sus la vessie, la ou encomencent li poil dou poignil, et .i. a destre et .i. a senestre, et soit chescuns cauteres si lons com li nous d’un poce; et li fais .i. cautere defuers le dos, ou .ij. se tu en as besoing; et soit li cauteres clavile selon la forme devant dite.	When the bladder is soft and weak from cold and moisture, and the patient retains urine due to the condition, then make a cautery on the part above the bladder where the hairs of the pubic region start, with one cautery on the right and one on the left, and let each cautery be as long as the width of two fingers; also, make one cautery below the back, or two if you need them; and use the key cautery as described earlier.
de la marris	of the womb
Quant li marrix est froide et moiste, et ne laisse mie por ceu a concevoir, et les flors sont corrumpues et lor termines tarde; et quant elles vienent, si sent grant dolor: adonques covient il c’on li faice .iij. cauteres entor la boude, si com nos avons dit ou cautere de la vessie, et .ij. cauteres defuers le dos; et soit li cauteres clavile, si com nos avons dit.	When the matrix is cold and moist, and does not permit conception, and the flowers are corrupt and their terms late; and when they come, there is great pain: therefore one must make three cauteries around the womb, as we have said in the cautery for the bladder, and two cauteries on the back; and let the cauteries be of a mild nature, as we have said.
de la hainche	of the hip
Quant les moistors viscouses dessendent a la boiste de la hainche, et por ceste cause si se muet de son leu, et li signes est que li cuisse est plus longe que li autre quant on le mesure ensamble; et est trovez li leus dou departement vuis, si covient que tu cauterizes le malaide sus la boiste de la hainche a .i. cautere semblant au cercle, et seigne devant le leu entor la boiste si com elle torne, si que li boiste soit dedens le cercle; et si soit li cauteres telz com cil dont on a cauterizeit le stomac.	When the viscous humors descend to the box of the hip, and because of this they move out of place, and the sign is that the thigh is longer than the other when one measures them together; and it is found that the place of the dislocation is hollow, then one must cauterize the patient on the box of the hip with 1 cautery resembling a circle, and mark before the location around the box as it turns, so that the box is within the circle; and let the cautery be like that which one uses to cauterize the stomach.
Et se cist cauteres ne t’est presens, se li fai .iij. cauteres de l’olivaire grans, et soit li cauteres ausi parfont com tous li keurs; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if this cautery is not present, make three cauteries of the olive oil large, and let the cautery be as deep as all the scabs; and heal it until it is better.
de la dolor de la hainche	of the pain of the hip
Quant dolor vient en la boiste de la hainche, et c’est de froidor et de moistor, et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en la division et li cure ne vaut, et li maladie est anciene: adonc covient il que tu purges le malaide des grosses humors de pilules fetides, ou autres pilules bones semblans.	When pain occurs in the hip socket, it is caused by cold and moisture, and the patient is cured of what we have said in the division, and the cure does not work, and the disease is old: then you must purge the patient of thick humors with foul-smelling pills, or other good-smelling pills.
Aprés li fai cautere; et li maniere dou cautere si est selonc .ij. manieres: c’est a savoir ensamble medicines ardans, et cautere de feu. Cautere de feu si est selonc mout de manieres, desquelz li uns est telz: que tu cauterize sus la boiste de la hainche .iij. cauteres triangulalz selonc ceste forme, et i fai bone profunditeit et grant, et ait entre chaicun cautere d’espaice la groissece d’un doi, et soit li cauteres olivaire; aucune fois fait on cautere en mileu sus lou chief de la hainche, por coi il en i a .iiij. selonc ceste forme:	Afterwards, he should do cauterization; and the method of cauterization is according to two methods: one is with burning medicines, and the other is fire cauterization. Fire cauterization has many methods, one of which is to cauterize the hip socket in a triangular shape according to this form, and make a deep and large wound, and there should be a distance of a thumb's width between each cauterization. Sometimes a cauterization is done in the middle of the hip joint, so that there are four cauterizations according to this form:
Et se tu vues, si le cauterize au cautere dou cercle que nos avons devant dit en la dislocation de la hainche; mais fai en teil maniere que li cercles conteigne toute la hainche, et tous li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if you want to cauterize with the circular cauterization that we mentioned earlier in the dislocation of the hip; but do it in such a way that the circles contain the entire hip, and all the thickness of the heart is burned.
Et c’est li maniere c’on fait en sciatique, quant li dolor tient en la hainche, et ne parvient mie jusc’a la cuisse ne jusc’a la jambe. Et s’ele vient jusc’a la cuisse et la jambe, se li fai .ij. cauteres lai ou li malaides dit que li dolor li tient, et .i. cautere desus la cheville .iiij. dois, a la partie senestre un poc; et soit li cauteres cutellaire, et soit arse li espesseté dou keur; et se li malaides sent que li dolor s’estende jusc’a dois dou piet ou pres d’enqui, se le cauterize la ou il sent la dolor .iij. poins ou .iiij. au cautere qui est apelez «poins».	And this is the way one proceeds in sciatica when the pain is located in the hip and does not reach the thigh or leg. And if it extends to the thigh and leg, then make .2 cauteries where the patient says that the pain lies, and .1 cautery above the ankle joint of the .4th toe on the left side a little; and let the cauteries be cutaneous, and burn away the thickness of the skin; and if the patient feels that the pain extends to the ball or near there, then cauterize where they feel the pain with .3 or .4 cauteries called "points".
Et se mestiers est, se li en fai plus; et se il seit que li dolor soit desoz le genoil vers la cuisse, se li fais cautere au cautere cutellaire ou circulaire, et te done bien garde en tous tes cauteres que tu n’i lassier mie tant le cautere que tu brules les ners et les grans arteres, et que tu ne faices au malaide plus grant nuisance et contraction.	And if necessary, make more cauteries; and if he feels that the pain is below the knee toward the thigh, then use a cutaneous or circular cautery, and be careful with all your cauteries not to leave the cautery on so long that you burn the nerves and large arteries, and cause the patient greater harm and contraction.
Et je meisme ai veus plusors qui ont fait cautere sus la cheville dou piet, et li lasserent tant que li jambe fut toute enflee, et li piez ausi, et fut perciez et corrumpus toz li piez. Aprés une solution de ventre dont il ot la mort.	And I myself have seen many who made cauteries above the ankle joint of the foot, and left them on so long that the leg was completely swollen, as was the foot, and it became pierced and rotten all over the foot. Afterwards they died from a stomach ailment.
Et se li dolors est en .ij. parties ensamble, fai cautere en l’une et en l’autre, selonc ceste maniere. // Et li saige dirent en la cautere de la hainche, de coi ci est li maniere, fai .i. tel fer et soit au chief ausi gros com uns nauvillon de dacte, ou un poc moins, et soit par entrechetres et soit des l’un entrechetres jusc’a l’autre d’espaice la quantiteit d’un nou de poce; et soient li entrechetres aovers de .ij. pars, et soient aussi comme noez, et i ait .i. mainche de fer bien fait; et c’est li forme:	And if the pain is in two parts together, make cautery in one and the other, according to this manner. // And the wise men said about the cautery of the hip, of which here is the manner, make a piece of iron and let it be at the end as thick as a little finger, or a little less, and let it be between the teeth and let it go from one tooth to another with the space the quantity of a thread of the needle; and let the teeth be above two parts, and let them also be like nails, and let it have a handle of well-made iron; and this is the shape:
Et soit eschaufez tant qu’il soit toz rouges et giete senteles, et puis le mette on sus la boiste de la hainche malaide, et soit tornez sus lou sain costeit; et lou cauterize une fois .i. cautere reont et lou laisse .iij. jors; et puis fai emplaustre de burre, et laisse la plaie aoverte lonc tens; aprés la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	And let it be heated until it is all red and dripping hot, and then place it on the box of the painful hip, and let it be turned onto the healthy side; and cauterize once with one cautery and leave it for 3 days; and then make a poultice of butter, and let the wound remain open for a long time; after the cure of ointment until it is healed.
Albucasim dit que nos usons poc de cest cautere por la paor de son regart, et se voions poc qui en usent; et toutevoie ceu est des boins cauteres, qui le puet soffrir, et lai ou il s’afiert.	Albucasim says that we use little of this cautery because of the fear of its sight, and those who are experienced in it use little; and nevertheless, it is one of the good cauteries which can be endured, and it lies where it occurs.
de la dolor dou dos	of back pain
Quant dolor vient au dos, ou par cheoir ou de percussion ou par trop grant evacuation, ou par semblans de matiere espandue froide, a nule de ces semblances ne vaut cauteres, fuer que a celi qui vient de infusion de froide matiere.	When back pain comes from sitting or impact or from excessive evacuation, or from similar appearances of cold matter, none of these warrant cauterization except that which comes from the diffusion of cold matter.
Il covient c’aprés ceu que li malaides est voidiez de pilules fetides ou d’autres semblans, que on li faice sus lou dos, lai ou li dolor tient, trois lignes signies d’enche, et en chescune ligne .v. cauteres ou plus selonc la vertut et la quantiteit que li malaides puet soffrir; et soit fait li cauteres selonc le cautere qui est apelez «poins»; et se tu vues, fai .iij. cauteres ou .iiij. au cautere clavile moien selonc ceste forme:	It is appropriate, after the patient has voided foul pills or other similar substances, to make three marks on their back where the pain is located, and in each mark, administer .v. cauteries or more depending on the strength and amount that the patient can endure; and the cautery should be performed according to the cautery called 'point'; and if you see fit, perform .iij or .iiij cauteries with the medium-sized cautery instrument according to this form:
Maintes fois vient ceste maladie as petis enfans, et li signes de l’encomencement si est qu’il ont estroite alainne quant il se lievent, et paor; et tu trueves en la derriene espinee dou dos et en nous l’apparance qui vient sus les autres espinees.	This disease often affects young children, and the signs of its onset are that they have a tight, constricted appearance when they wake up, and fear; and you will find it in the last vertebrae of the back and in the appearance that comes over the other vertebrae.
Quant tu vois ceu et tu le vues curer, si le cauterize au cautere de celcle selonc ceste forme.	When you see this and you cure it, then cauterize it with a cautery of salt according to this form.
Si que li cautere porpreigne chescune partie de l’espinee egaument. Et se tu vues, si cauterize entor l’espinee au cautere poignant .ij. lignes ou .iij., et soient li poins pres l’uns de l’autre. Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez selonc ceu que nos avons dit, et warde que tu n’amenistrer cautere en gilbositeit qui soit en spame de nerf.	So that the purple cautery will affect each part of the spine equally. And if you see [the spine], then cauterize around it with a pointed cautery .ij or .iij lines long, and let the points be close to each other. Afterward, cure the area until it is healed according to what we have said, and beware of administering cautery in gangliness that is in the webbing of a nerve.
de la dolor des jointes	of joint pain
Quant dolor de jointes sunt de moistors que sont espandues a chaicun membre dou cors, et quant dolor vient em piez, que li mire apelent «podagre» proprement, et quant elle est de froide cause et cures de medicines ne la puent curer, si est curez par cauteres en teil maniere: fai li mout de cauteres entor la jointure dou piet, et soit li cauteres olivaire selonc ceste forme:	When joint pain is caused by moisture that is spread throughout the body's limbs, and when pain comes in the feet, which the doctors properly call 'podagra', and when it is caused by cold and cannot be cured by medicines, then it is cured by cauteries in such a way: make the mouth of the cautery around the joint of the foot, and let the cautery be olive-colored according to this form:
Et s’il i a besoigne que tu poignes sus la faice dou piet, se li fai cautere a tot le cautere c’on claime «point». Et se les dolors viegnent jusc’a genous et as autres jointures, et ceu avient maintes fois, se li fai cautere sus chaicun genoil .iij. cauteres ou .iiij. de chescunne partie, a tout le cautere olivaire; et se tu as mestier de plus, si en fai plus, mais n’i tenir mie ta main fuers que tant que li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if there is a need for you to touch the face of the foot, then you should cauterize it with the entire cautery that one calls "point". And if pains come up to the knees and other joints, and this happens many times, then cauterize each knee with three or four cauteries on each part, with all the olive-sized cauteries; and if you need more, then do more, but do not hold your hand against it for longer than the thickness of the heart is burned.
Et se les dolors dessendent jusc’a genoil et au dos, se li aministre le cautere que nos avons dit en son chapistre. Et se les dolors sunt as mains, si fai poins entor le foscile .ij. lignes; et s’il remaint point de dolor as dois, si fai poins sus chescune jointe et sus lou poil de la main; et se les dolors vienent jusc’as coutes ou jusc’as espaules, si cauterize chescune partie, et fai boin governement au malaide et penre medicines. Car se tu li fais boin governement et tu purges fleume, si sera saneis a l’aide de Deu.	And if the pains go down to the knee and back, then administer the cautery that we discussed in its chapter. And if the pains are in the hands, then make points around the wrist two lines; and if there remains no pain in the fingers, then make points on each joint and on the hair of the hand; and if the pains come to the elbow or shoulder, then cauterize each part, and provide good treatment for the patient and take medicines. For if you provide good treatment and purge the flux, then he will be healed with God's help.
de la routure dou syfac	from the root of the ulcer
Quant routure vient en angres, et li bouelz dessendent as coions et c’est novelement, si covient que quant tu lou vues curer, qu’il ne menjuce mie celui jor; et qu’il use choses qui laichent lou ventre, si que li fiens dessende de son ventre; aprés le fai seoir sus son dos entre tes mains, et li comande qu’il teigne son alaine tant que li boueil soient repairiet, et les ramoinne a tes dois, et seigne d’enche desoz la routure sus l’os dou poignil, et a tout un signe que soit semblans a la moitiet d’un cercle a desus dou cors; puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When the ulcer comes in the anus, and the bowels descend to the testicles and it is new, then when you see him being cured, he should not defecate that day; and he should use things that loosen the belly so that the farts descend from his belly; after that, let him sit on his back between your hands, and command him to press his anus until the bowels are repaired, and bring them back to your fingers, and sign with chalk underneath the ulcer on the bone of the buttock, and throughout a sign that is similar to half a circle on top of the body; then heat the cautery from which this form comes:
tant qu’il soit blans et qu’il giete senteles. Puis ramoine les bouels a lor leu; et li ministres teigne sa main sus qu’il ne retornent arrier; et oevre bien les cuisses au malaide, et met desoz lui .i. cussin et .i. serjant sus les cuisses, et .i. autre sus lou pis qui li teigne les mains; puis met le cautere sus lou signe a tout ta main, et lou tien droit et lou tien tant que tu ateignes l’os, et se tu ne l’ateins la premiere fois, si le rencomence encor une autre tant que tu viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde subtilment que li boueil ne saille quant tu fais lou cautere; que tu ne le brulasses; et que par ceu li malaides ne muere, ou autre malz.	as long as it is white and bleeding. Then reset the bones to their proper place; and the assistant holds his hand steady so that they do not move back; and work well on the thighs of the patient, and put under him one cushion and one servant on the thighs, and another on the feet who holds his hands; then apply the cautery on the sign all over your hand, and hold it straight and hold it until you reach the bone, and if you do not reach it the first time, do it again another time until you reach the bone; and be careful that the blood does not flow when you are doing the cautery; so that you do not burn him; and so that by this the patient does not die, or suffer some other harm.
Et saiches que quant tu ne viens jusc’a l’os au cautere, tes ovraiges ne vaut rien. Et covient que li cauteres des enfans soit subtilz selonc la mesure d’ous, et des grans gens aussi grans selonc lor mesure; aprés .iij. jors cure lou leu dou cautere de burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’autres oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez, et gise li malaides .xl. jors sus son dos tant que li plaie soit bien soudee; et covient que ses norrissemens soit lassatis longement, si que li boueil ne saillent quant il se preigdra d’aler en chambres.	And you should know that when you do not reach the bone with the cautery, your work is worth nothing. And the cautery of children should be subtle according to the size of their ears, and for large people it should be as large as their ears; after 3 days, cure the site of the cautery with butter until the scorch is removed; then cure it with other ointments until it heals, and let the patient lie on his back for 40 days until the wound is well-closed; and his bandages should be left on for a long time so that the blood does not flow when he tries to move around.
Et aprés .xl. jors, quant il se voudra lever, se li amenistre une faixe bien faite, et la porse .xl. autres jors; et ait boin repos, qu’il se travaille poc et se warde de trop grant repletion de boivre et de mengier, et de trop haut braire; et quant il fait cest enseignement si est sanez entierement. Et je dirai ci aprés la cure de taillier en son chapistre.	And after 40 days, when he wants to get up, if a well-made brace is provided for him, and he wears it for another 40 days; and has good rest, not working too much and taking care to avoid excessive eating and drinking, and shouting too loudly; and if he follows these instructions, he will be completely healed. And I will now describe the treatment for cutting into his shoulder joint.
de la routure dou ventre	of the bowel movement
Quant routures vienent en autres ventres et sont connisans, et tu vues qu’elles ne croissent plus, se li fai .j. cautere dou cautere reont selonc sa quantiteit, et soit ars li tiers dou keur; aprés le cure selonc ceu que nos avons dit; et aucun des anciens ont dit c’on le doit cauterizer au cautere a .iij. angles selonc ceste forme:	When bowel movements come from other stomachs and are known, and you see that they no longer grow, then do .j cautery of the cautery according to its quantity, and let it be burned by the third of the heart; after the cure according to what we have said; and some of the ancients said that one must cauterize with a cautery at 3 angles according to this form:
mais signe premier le leu d’enche et fai une ligne per la largesce desus la routure, et une autre defuers, et main ta main emmi a tout le cautere clavile. Mais li premiers cauteres est plus legiers et muedres.	but first sign the site of entry and draw a line along the width above the bowel movement, and another one from the side, and hold your hand in place throughout the entire cautery. But the first cauteries are lighter and deeper.
de dolor anciene en aucun membre	of old pain in any limb
Quant dolor vient en aucun membre, ou de cheoir ou de ferir, et cele dolor tient lonc tens, et li cure de medicine n’i vaut, adonc covient qu’il soit cauterizeis au cautere qui est apelez «poins», et soit li cauteres selonc la longesce dou membre et la petitece et sa foibleteit et sa vertut et sa location de torcions et de sa dolor. s’il est sanez dou premier cautere, c’est bien; se ceu nom, recomence .i. autre cautere sus celui, car teilz costume est qu’il se doit muer au membre que li est prochiens, por coi il covient que tu faices les cauteres tant que li malaides soit saneis.	When pain comes to any limb, from a fall or injury, and the pain persists for a long time, and medical treatment does not help, then cauterization is required using the cautery known as 'point', and the cautery should be applied according to the length of the limb, its size, weakness, virtue, location of twists and turns, and the intensity of the pain. If it is healed by the first cautery, that's good; if not, apply another cautery on top of the previous one, for such is the custom that it should affect the nearby limb, so you must continue applying cauteries until the patient is healed.
de meselerie	from mixing
Li meseil sont aidiet aucune fois par cautere par grant aide, et meismement li maladie que vient de la putrefaction de fleume et de melancolie. Cant tu la vues cauterizer, pren warde se li maladie est au comencement, et s’ele est curee selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et ne dessent ne ne demoure, et tu doutes que li corruption ne porpreigne tout le malaide, adonques li fai .v. cauteres sus lou chief: .i. emmi le chief a nouf, et l’autre vers lou front a la fin des chevous; et .ij. sus les .ij. cornes, et .i. derrierre sus le haiterel; et i laise tant ta main que li cauteres viegne jusc’a l’os, et tant que les escorces en issent fors si que les vapors des grosses humors s’en puissent issir; et le cauterize sus la mice selonc ce qu’il est devant.	Miasmas are sometimes healed by cautery with great difficulty, especially those illnesses that arise from putrefaction of phlegm and melancholy. When you see such an illness being cauterized, pay attention to whether the disease is in its early stages, and if it is cured according to what we have said in the division, and does not persist or remain, and you doubt that the corruption may spread throughout the body, then perform five cauteries on the head: one at the crown of the head, and another towards the forehead at the front of the hairline; and two on the temples, and one behind on the nape of the neck; and hold your hand in such a way that the cautery reaches the bone, and as long as the skin blisters so that the vapors of the thick humors can come out; and cauterize the mouse according to what it is in front.
Et se li meselerie est partout esparse; et elle pert manifestement, si covient que tu lou cauterizes de ces cauteres que nos avons dit ou chief, et .i. cautere en som lou neis, et .ij. cauteres sus l’espinee dou col, et .vj. cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos, et .i. grant sus la crupie et .i. autre delez, et .ij. sus les .ij. espaules; et .ij. sus les coutes, et .ij. sus les tendrons dou pis, et .i. sus chascune jointe des mains et des piez, et sus les fosses des mains; et te warde des ners que sunt sus lou derrien calcant, que tu ne les bruler; et aucune fois fait om cautere sus l’os dou poignil, et .i. autre sus l’os de l’estomac, et .i. autre sus lou foie.	And if the disease is scattered throughout the body, and it is clearly lost, then you should cauterize her with these cauteries that we have mentioned on the head, and one cautery in the nose, and two cauteries on the spine of the neck, and six cauteries on the spine of the back, and one large one on the groin and another there, and two on the two shoulders; and two on the elbows, and two on the tendons of the feet, and one on each joint of the hands and feet, and on the hollows of the hands; and be careful not to burn the nerves that are on the back of the calf. And sometimes do one cautery on the bone of the arm, and another on the bone of the stomach, and another on the liver.
Et saiches que quant plus i fais de cautere, plus li fais d’aide, et mues li profite; et saiches que li malaides ne sent point de dolor au cautere si com li sain le sentent, por ce que li cors est ja toz corrumpus. Et covient ke li cautere soient grant et petit selonc les membres et les jointures, selonc ceu que vos lou troverez en manieres des fers. Aprés cure lou leu de farine de veces avec miel et autres cures tant qu’il soit saneis.	And you should know that the more cauteries you do, the more it will help, and it will be beneficial; and you should know that the sick person does not feel pain from cautery as a healthy person does, because the body is already entirely corrupted. And you should make the cauteries large and small according to the members and joints, according to how you find them in the methods of the irons. After this, treat the wound with wheat flour mixed with honey and other remedies until it is healed.
de enfleure	of swelling
Quant enfleure vient en aucun membre et est curee par medicines et oiles et emplastres, et il n’est mie sanez, adonques li fai cauteres sus le membre selonc la grandour et la petitece dou membre; et soit li cauteres un poc entrans en l’espés dou keur; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez. Et aucune fois fait on cautere et a la main et au piet et au dos, a l’issue dou nerf que muet le membre, et ensi si est ostee li enfleure; et toutevoie ne s’en entremette nuls s’il n’est conoissans des membres et des issues des ners movans lou cors.	When swelling comes to a limb and is treated with medicines, oils, and plasters, but does not heal, then cauterize the limb according to its size; and let the cautery be slightly warm in the center of the fire; then cure it with ointments until it heals. And sometimes cauterization is done on the hand, foot, back, at the exit of a nerve that paralyzes the limb, and thus the swelling is removed; but no one should attempt this who does not understand the limbs and the exits of the nerves that move the body.
de albaras	of almond milk
Quant li maladie qui est apelee «albaras» est enveillie, et li engien de medicine n’i valent rien, adonques le cauterize d’un cautere un poc parfont, selonc la quantiteit de l’espés dou keur, tant que li blenchour soit ostee, et soit muee sa color; puis le cure de farine de veces et de lentilles avec oile roset et foilles de plantain, et sanc de colon et sanc d’alondre, de chescun une partie; et soit mellez tout ensamble, et soit liiez d’un drapel, et soit aers au leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the disease called "albaras" appears, and medicine does not help, then cauterize it with a slightly deep cautery, according to the thickness of the skin, until the whiteness is removed and the color changed; then cure it with a poultice of linseed and lentil flour, with rose oil, and plantain leaves, and colon blood and almond blood, each ingredient being used in equal parts. Mix everything together and apply it, wrapped in a cloth, to the affected area until it heals.
li cure de chancre par cautere	the cure of cancer by cautery
Quant chancre vient au comencement, et tu lou vues arrester, si le cauterize au cautere qui semble .i. cercle, tout entor au tour dou chancre.  Et toutevoie li saige dirent que on faice cautere ausi au mileu dou chancre; et toutevoie ceu ne me semble mie boin, car je redous que il ne soit ulcerez et corrumpus, et je l’ai ja veut avenir aucune fois; et plus droituriere chose est qu’il soit cauteriés entor, au cautere qui est apelez «circule», si com nos avons dit en mout de cauteres.	When chancre appears at the beginning, and you see it stopping, then cauterize it with a cautery that resembles a circle, all around the edge of the chancre. And yet the wise say that one should also make cauteries in the middle of the chancre; and yet this does not seem good to me, for I fear that it will be ulcerated and corrupted, and I have indeed seen it happen sometimes; and a more certain thing is that it be cauterized around, with the cautery which is called "circular", as we have said in many cauteries.
de l’enfleure qui ne puet meurer	of the swelling that cannot subside
Quant aucuns ait une maladie qui est apelee «adubelati», et elle tarde de meurer ou por la superfluiteit qu’ele fait ou por l’eaige dou malaide quant il est decrepites (c’est a dire trop vielz) et il a poc de sanc, ou por lou tens; et tu la vues haster de meurer: adonques le cauterize entor de mout de petis cauteres en poignant; aprés le laisse ensi. Car elle se hastera de meureir.	When someone has a disease called  "adubelati", and it is slow to heal, either because of the excess fluid it produces, or due to the age of the patient when they are decrepit (that is, very old) and have little blood, or because of the season; and you see it hastening to heal: then cauterize it all around with many small cauteries by pricking; after that, leave it as it is. For it will hasten to heal.
Et se tu la vues percier a tout le cautere, si chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	And if you see it piercing all the way through, then heat the cautery with which it is formed:
Et met ta main en mileu de cele maladie qui est apellee «adubelati» tant que li cauteres ait perciet lou keur, et soit telz li cauteres que li malaides lou sente defuers en teil maniere que li cours de la porriture soit alegis. Aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	And put your hand over the middle of that disease called "adubelati" until the cautery has penetrated the skin, and let the cautery be such that the patient feels it burning in such a way that the course of the pus is relieved. After the cauterization, when it is perfectly healed.
li cure dou feu par fer	the fire cautery by iron
Une autre maniere de maladie i a qui est apelee «corrodens», et n’est autre chose que une mengeson de membre, car ele menjut les membres ausi com li feus les leignes seches. Se tu vois ceste maladie en leu qui puisse soffrir cautere ensamble feu, adonques eschaufe les cauteres clavile mout petit et grant, selonc ceu qu’il covient au leu ou li maladie est; aprés le cauterize de toutes pars tant que tu erraiche toute la corruption, et nen remaigne rien de li, que tout ceu qui est corrumpus ne soit osteit. Et puis le laisse .iij. jors, et met sus les leus cauterizez soffre broiet avec oile tant que les eschaudures dou feu soient ostees, et toute li corruption. Aprés lou cure d’oignemens engendrans char.  Et se tu vois aprés .iij. jors que chars saine ne naisse, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere sus ceu qui est demoreit des leus corrumpus. Et ceste mengeson est aucune fois esteit curee de medicine ague en leu de cautere de feu; mais toutevoie cautere de feu est de plus grant aide, et j’ai ja dit la cure de la medicine ague en la division: pren la quant tu en as mestier.	Another kind of disease is called "corrodens", which is nothing but a corruption of a limb, for it corrodes the limbs just as fire burns dry wood. If you see this disease in a place that can withstand cauterization with fire, then heat the cauteries with a small and large claw, according to what is appropriate for the location of the disease; then cauterize all over until you reach all the corruption, and none of it remains, so that all that is corrupted is removed. And then leave it for three days, and apply ointments to the cauterized areas to soothe the burns and remove all the corruption. After three days, if new healthy flesh has appeared, that is good; but if not, then re-cauterize over the area that remains corrupted. This kind of disease can sometimes be cured with medicine instead of fire cautery; however, fire cautery is generally more effective. I have already described the cure for medicine ague in the section on that topic: use it as needed.
des porrelz qui vienent as piez	of warts that appear on the feet
Mout de fois avient que as piez par defuers naist une maladie qui est apelee «clos» selonc nostre entencion, et est une grosse chose fautree qui blece lou piet. Et li cauteres de ceste maladie si est selonc .ij. manieres. C’est a savoir cautere de feu, et cautere d’aigue chaude. Cautere de feu si est que tu eschaufe .i. cautere cheveit ausi com est une penne de vouteul, et soit fait de boin fer a la mesure qu’il puisse porpenre le clou de toutes pars, et qu’il i ait subtilz marges; aprés le met tout chaut sus lou clou, et torne ta main tot entor le clou tant qu’il viegne au font dou clou; et lou laisse ensi .iij. jors tant qu’il encomence giter porriture; puis li fai un emplaustre de malves savaiges broiies avec seil, et laisse l’emplaustre sus toute la nuit, et li clous cherra et sera desracinez de ses racines. Puis cure le leu d’oignement enjanrant char tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many times it happens that on the feet, from different causes, a disease called 'close' according to our understanding arises, and it is a large, faultily formed thing which breaks the toe. And the cautery for this disease is in two ways: that is, fire cautery, and hot water cautery. Fire cautery is that you heat one cautery as hot as an owl's egg, made of good iron to the measure that it can support the nail all around, and that it has thin edges; then put it all hot on the nail, and turn your hand all around the nail until it reaches the bottom of the nail; and leave it thus for three days until it begins to produce pus; then make a poultice of crushed wild mallows with salt, and leave the poultice on all night, and the nail will fall off and be uprooted from its roots. Then cure the place with ointment until it is healed.
Et s’il sont convertit par defuers lou cors, et maintes fois avient et en mains et em piez, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere d’aigue chaude; et est en teil maniere: pren une cainne d’arain ou de fer, ou une penne de vouteul, et met sus lou clou et l’althelul, c’est asavoir porrelz verrues; et met la cainne sus si qu’ele porpreigne tout entor, puis i met un poc d’awe chaude, et retien bien ta main, et presse ta main en tornant si que li marge de la cainne viegne a la racine dou clou, et puisse trover l’aigue chaude voie parfonde jusc’a la racine; et soffre li malaides un poc la mordication de l’aigue chaude une houre; puis le laisse ensi, et il se derracinera tous a tout ses racines. Ensi fai un aprés autre, tant que tu esraiches toz ces qui sont au cors, puis les cure des oignemens qui engenrent char.	And if they are converted from the body, and many times they appear in the hands and feet, then you must administer hot water cautery; and it is done this way: take a brass or iron rod, or an owl's egg, and put it on the nail and the althelul - that is, warts; and put the rod on so that it wraps all around, then pour a little hot water, and hold your hand firmly and press your hand as you turn so that the edge of the rod reaches the root of the nail and can find the hot water deeply to the root. And let the patient endure the biting of the hot water for a while; then leave it thus, and it will be uprooted from its roots all the way through. Do this one after another until you extract all those in the body, then cure them with ointments that produce flesh.
li cure dou trembler	the cure for trembling
Quant aucuns tremble de froidor de ners, ou de fievre quartaine ou d’autre, si covient que tu li faices .iiij. cauteres ou .iv. sus l’espinee dou dos, .i. cautere entre chescune espinee; et .i. cautere ou pez, et .i. sus l’estomac au cautere olivaire; si laissera lou trembler, et se hastera li santez de la maladie froide.	When someone shakes from coldness of the nerves, or from quartan fever or other, you should make them .iiij. cauteries or .iv. on the spine of the back, .i. cautery between each vertebrae; and .i. cautery on the feet, and .i. on the stomach with an olive-sized cautery; this will stop the shaking and hasten the healing from the cold disease.
des pustules puans	of stinking pustules
Aucune fois apperent par defuers le cors bathes, ou pustules puans, que vienent de grosses matieres corrumpues. si covient au premier quant eles apperent que on faice cautere sus chescun chief de la pustule: un cautere subtil de fust de mirte, de coi li pointe soit emprise au feu, ou de racine de aristologe longe, ou au cautere lenticulaire. Et aucune fois les cauterize on au comencement quant il aperent, selonc ceste maniere, et il ne puent croistre des enqui en avant, mais est desrompue li superfluitez dont il vienent, et sont sanez; mais il covient que ceu soit fait aprés l’evacuation de sanc.	Sometimes they appear on the body as bathes or stinking pustules, which come from thick corrupted matter. One should cauterize them at their appearance, with a small cautery of myrtle wood, whose tip is heated, or of long aristolochia root, or with the lenticular cautery. Sometimes one should cauterize them at the beginning as they appear, in this way, and then they cannot grow further, but the superfluity from which they come is disrupted, and they are healed; but this should be done after blood-letting.
quant li artere est copee	when the artery is cut
Maintes fois avient grans decorremens de sanc de l’artere qui est copee a la plaie que vient au pardefuers, ou a l’incision de l’aposteme, ou au cautere dou membre, et as semblans choses; et est mout grief chose d’estenchier.	There are many times great bleeding from the artery that is cut at the wound that comes to the surface, or with the incision of an abscess, or with the cautery of the limb, and similar things; and it is a very sorrowful thing to stanch.
Et toutevoie quant ceu avient a aucun, si te haste de mettre ton doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne, et l’estrain mout tant que li sans soit apaisiez desoz ton doi, et que goute n’en isse plus; puis met au feu les cauteres olivaire plusors petis et grans tant qu’il soient tuit rouge; puis empren .i., ou grant ou petit selonc la plaie et lou leu en coi li artere est route, et met le cautere sus cele voine ou tu tiens ton doi, et tien le cautere tant sus que li sans soit restainchiez.	And yet when this happens to someone, quickly place your index finger over the wound of the vein and hold it very tightly until the blood is calmed beneath your finger and no drop comes out; then take several small and large olive-wood cauteries and heat them in the fire until they are all red; then take a little salt, either large or small depending on the wound and where the artery is rupture, and place the cautery over that vein where you hold your finger, and keep it there until the bleeding is stopped.
Et s’il saut fuers quant tu lieves ton doi desus la voinne, et li cauteres estint, si pren hastivement .i. autre des cauteres qui sont au feu.	And if it bleeds when you lift your finger from the wound and the cauteries are extinguished, quickly take another one of the cauteries which are in the fire.
Et ne cesser de faire ceu l’un aprés l’autre tant que li sans soit estenchiez; et warde que tu n’ardes lou nerf qui est delez, et que autre malice ne viegne sus lou malaide; et saiches que quant sans decourt de l’artere, c’on ne lou puet mie bien restenchier meismement quant li artere est grans, se ceu n’est par une des .iiij. manieres que nos avons dit: ou par cautere, ou par extraction quant ele n’est mie traite, ou par fort liement de fil, ou par medicines mises sus qui ont pooir de restenchier sanc; et soit liee et estrainte avennament.	And do not cease doing this one after the other until the bleeding is stopped; and beware of damaging the nerve which lies nearby, and that no further harm comes to the patient; and know that when blood flows from an artery, it cannot be stopped well by itself alone if the artery is large, unless by one of four methods we have mentioned: either by cautery or extraction when it is not treated, or by a strong ligature, or by medicines placed on which have power to stop bleeding; and let it be bound and pressed gently.
Qui i amenistrera restenchement de liier estroitement de drapelz ou de metre choses ardans sus, ou autres semblans choses, se n’i profite se poc non.	Whoever administers a tight binding of bandages or places burning things on top, or similar things, will not benefit if only a little.
Et se ce avient a aucun et il n’ait mie mire ne medicine present, si doit mettre son doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne si com nos avons dit, et bien estrendre tant qu’il soit restenchiez desus la plaie et desus la voinne; et ne remuer lou doit, mais lou moille d’awe froide sovent que soit mout froide tant que li sans soit congelez et engrossiez et restenchiez; et faice des enqui en avant ceu dont il a mestier de cauteres et de medicines.	And if this happens to someone and they do not have any medicine available, then they should put their index finger on the wound as we have said, and press firmly both on the wound and the vein; and they should not move it, but moisten it with cold water often so that it is very cold until the blood is congealed and swollen and pressed firm; and they should make inquiries in advance about what cauteries and medicines are needed.
Ci encomence li secons livre des cures de taille	Here begins the second book of wound treatments
Nos vos avons dit ou premier chapistre toute maladie en coi il covient cautere de feu, ou de medicine ardans, et les oquisons et les causes et les estrumens et les formes des cauteres; et ai mis celui chapistre des lou chief jusc’a piez, et je irai en cest chapistre par celi meisme voie por ceu c’on trueve plus legierement ceu c’on voura.	We have told you in the first chapter about all illnesses that require cautery with fire or burning medicines, and their cause, instrument, form of cauteries; and I have placed that chapter from head to foot, and I will go in this chapter by the same path so that one may more easily find what they want.
Et ainsois que je encomence ceu, il covient, chier fil, que vos aprenez que en cest chapistre a plus de peril et de paor que ou premier des cauteres, et por ceu il covient plus grant cautele.	And so that I may begin this, my dear son, you must learn that in this chapter there is more danger and fear than in the first of the cauteries, and because of this greater caution is needed.
Car en l’ovraige de cest chapistre avient maintes fois evacuation de sanc a l’ovrir la voinne, et a l’incision sus aposteme, et as cures des plaies, et a l’estraction des saiettes, et a l’incision sus la piere, et les semblans choses; ou il a doutance et paor, et en vient li mors a plusors.	For in the work of this chapter, there is often the evacuation of blood when opening a vein, and incising an abscess, and in the treatment of wounds, and in the extraction of arrows, and in cutting into stones, and similar things; where there is doubt and fear, and many die.
Et je vos amoneste que vos n’entreprenez folie. Car mout de manieres de gens vienent en cures. si vienent de telz qui s’aïrent si avec lor maladie qu’il muerent legierement por la forsenerie qu’il trueve de sa maladie, et de la grandour de son malice; et de ces doit on avoir paor.	And I warn you not to be foolish. For in many ways people come for cures. Some come from such a distance that they would die easily from the journey, because of the severity of their illness; and from those one must be afraid.
Et de ces i a qui te done son sens, et dit: «atendez, je sui garis»; et li maladie est despitouse. Il ne covient mie que vos vos consentez a ces qui vienent a vos qui ont ceste maniere, mais mettez plus grant cusanson en vostre honor qu’en vostre covoitise, et n’ovrez mie folement mais saigement de ceu dont vos estes certain, et dont vos poez avoir pris et los; et usez de pronostication et de indication en cures de vos malaides a coi salus soit convertie; et ceu vos aidera a aquester bone renommee, et gloire, et memoire de loenge.	And so that I may begin this, my dear son, you must learn that in this chapter there is more danger and fear than in the first of the cauteries, and because of this greater caution is needed. And among these there are some who lose their senses and say, "Wait, I am healed"; and they die from the disease. You must not consent to those who come to you with such behavior, but put more care into your honor than your greed, and do not open foolishly but wisely that of which you are certain and that from which you can take profit and loss; and use prediction and indication in the cures of your illnesses for which salvation is turned towards you. And this will help you to that good reputation, glory, and memory of praise.
Tres chier fil, Nostres Sires vos doint boin entendement et droiture, et se vos vuelle espireir de la sainte inspiration de sa main, amen.	Very dear son, our Lord gives you good understanding and righteousness, and if you want to aspire to the holy inspiration of his hand, amen.
Or je vos ai ordeneit cest chapistre en devisant par chapistres, selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre des cauteres, que je vos ai deviseit des le chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que vos trovez plus legierement ceu dont vos avrez mestier.	Now I have ordered this chapter in a discourse on chapters, according to what it is before the chapter on cauteries, which I have discussed from the head to the feet, so that you can find more easily whatever you need.
dou chief plein d’aigue	from the head full of water
Saiches que ceste maladie vient mout de fois as enfans a l’enfanter, et quant li baille estraint trop fort le chief de l’enfant; et aucune fois vient ceu de cause reponue que on ne seit.	Do you know that this disease often comes to infants during childbirth, and when the birth canal is too narrow for the baby's head; and sometimes it comes from a relaxed birth canal, which no one knows about.
Et je ne vis onques ceste maladie fuers qu’en enfans, et a toz ces que j’ai veus se hastait li mors; et por ceu me semble qu’il me vaut mues lassier l’ovraige en teilz cures.	And I have never seen this disease in anyone but children, and in all those that I have seen, death soon followed; and for this reason it seems better to me to leave the treatment in a few simple remedies.
Et je vis .i. enfant de coi li chiés estoit plains d’aigue, et li chief engroissoit chescun jor tant qu’il ne lou pooit sostenir; et crut tant li moistor qu’il fut mors, et ceste moistor si est assemblee desoz l’os sus lou syphac, entre lou keur et l’os; et li ovraiges si est telz se li moistor est entre lou keur et l’os, et li apostemes est petis, que tu fendes emmi lou chief une fendure large; et soit ausi longe com .ij. nous, tant que li mostor corre; et vez ci la forme dou spatumile:	And I saw a child whose head was swollen with water, and the swelling increased every day until he could no longer bear it; and he died of the moisture, which had gathered under the skull between the brain and the bone; and if the moisture is between the brain and the bone, and the abscess is small, then make a large slit in the head, as long as two fingers, so that the moisture may flow out; and here is the form of the spatumile:
Se li moistor est plus creue, et li aposteme soit plus grans, si fai .ij. fendures en maniere d’une croix, selonc ceste forme:	If the moisture is deeper, and the abscess is larger, make two slits in the shape of a cross, according to this form:
Et se li moistor est desoz l’os, et li signes que tu vois les commissures dou chief overtes de chescune partie, et li aigue saut fuer quant tu la presses de ta main au dedens, et ceu ne t’est mie reponut: si covient que tu fendes enmi lou chief .iij. fendures selonc ceste maniere:	And if the moisture is under the bone, and you see the corners of the head opening in every part, and the water jumps out when you press it with your hand from within, and it does not close up again: then you must make three slits in the head according to this manner:
Et aprés l’incision estrai la moistor toute fuers. Aprés estraint les fendures de drapelz et de poudres, et i met vin et oile, et laisse ensi jusc’a cinquieme jor; puis le deslie, et cure la plaie par tentes et par oignemens, et laisse estraindre le chief egaument, et done mengier au malaide viande seche de poc de moistor tant que li membre soit confortez et sanez.	And after the incision, extract all moisture forcefully. After that, squeeze out the folds of cloth and powder, and apply wine and oil, and leave it thus until the fifth day; then loosen it, and treat the wound with poultices and ointments, and let the head be extracted equally, and give the patient dry meat without any moisture as long as the limb is comforted and healed.
Et une autre maniere d’incision est que tu regardes ou apert li grandor de l’aposteme, et li assemblé de l’aigue; car aucune fois est elle devant; aucune fois derrier; aucune fois en destre; et aucune fois en senestre.	And another way of incision is that you look at where the abscess opens, and the gathering of pus; for sometimes it is in front, sometimes behind, sometimes on the right, and sometimes on the left.
Taille donques lai ou li aposteme apert, et l’emplissement de l’aigue, et lou fent selonc ce que tu en as le pooir; et warde que tu ne coper l’artere; et veigne flun de sanc, si que li malaides muere dou decorrement de sanc et de l’evacuation de moistor.	So cut where the abscess opens and the gathering of pus, and pierce according to what you can; and be careful not to cut the artery, and let blood flow, so that the patient dies from bleeding and the evacuation of moisture.
de reume	from gout
Quant il avient a aucun une maladie qui est apelee «catarre» as eulz ou au pis, et li maladie est anciainne, et li cure de medicine ne profite mie, adonques li derraine cure si est li cauteres avec ceu c’on li copera les .ij. arteres.	When someone suffers from a condition called "cataract" in the eyes or feet, and the disease is old, and medical treatment is ineffective, then the best course of action is cauterization by cutting the two arteries.
Il covient donques, cant tu les vues coper, que li malaides faice rere son chief; aprés li frotte lou leu d’un drapel aspre tant que les arteres aperent, puis estraingne li malaides son col a tout .i. drapel; puis regarde ou li voine bait, et li leus de l’une et de l’autre sont aprés les oreilles, et poc sont reponues; puis signe les leus d’enche, puis cope l’une et l’autre d’un spatumile agut de .ij. pars. tant que li taille veigne jusc’a l’os, et ceu soit par lou large dou chief.	Therefore, when you see them cut, the patient should face away; then rub the area around the arteries with a rough cloth until they appear, then hold the patient's neck firmly with one hand; then look where the vein is, and the places are behind the ears, and they are very sensitive; then sign the places with your finger, then cut both with a sharp spatulum two parts deep so that the vein reaches the bone, and this should be done from the back of the head.
Et se tu vues, boute le spatumile desoz l’artere et la cope au desus, en taillant ausi com .ij. dois au traver.	And if you see it, put the spatulum under the artery and cut it from above, cutting also as deep as two fingers across.
Et quant li voinne est copee, si saut li sans en haut continuelment fuers.	And when the vein is cut, the blood will flow out continuously upward.
Et se li artere n’apert au sentir, si covient que tu mesures la quantiteit de l’espaice de .iij. dois, puis seigne d’enche et fent jusc’a l’os; et ceu qu’il covient dou sanc mettre fuers si est .vj. c/, et par aventure un poc plus ou moins. selonc ce que li malaides puet soffrir, et la repletion de l’artere; puis regarde la plaie: s’il remaint sus l’os point dou syphac, si le cope que apostemes chaus n’i veigne, puis estrain la plaie et lie, et la cure d’oignement tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And if the artery does not open to feeling, then you must measure the quantity of the space of three digits, then cut in and cut just to the bone; and what it is convenient to put out of blood is 6 ounces, and by chance a little more or less according to what the patient can endure, and the fullness of the artery; then regard the wound: if there remains on the bone no dot of pus, so that the hot abscess does not come in, then strain the wound and ligate it, and treat it with ointment until it is healed.
de emigrainne	of emetic
Quant emigrainne anciaine vient, et catarre agut, por les moistors des larmes et les chalors en temples et sode anciene forsenee et semblans choses, et il est medicinez par manieres de cures de medicine et tout ceu ne li profite mie, si estraions les arteres des temples et lou cauterizons, si com nos avons conteit.	When ancient emigrant comes, and catarrh is acute, for the moistors of tears and the chills in temples and ancient soddeness and similar things, and it is medicined by manners of cures of medicine and all that does not benefit him at all, then let us draw out the arteries of the temples and cauterize them, as we have related.
Et li maniere de l’estraction d’elles si est que li malaides faice rere les poilz de ses temples, et entende a l’artere qui apert en la temple, car elle apert bien par son batement, et est poc reponue fuers que en aucuns homes qui sont trop froit; et s’elle est reponue, si estraigne son col li malaides d’aucuns drapelz, puis frote le leu d’aucun aspre drap, et arose le leu d’aigue chaude tant que li artere apere manifestement; puis pren le spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	And the manner of the extraction of them is that the patient pulls back the hair of his temples, and feels the artery which opens in the temple, for it opens well by its beating, and is little relaxed outwards when in some men who are too cold; and if it is relaxed, then the patient strains his neck with some cloth, then rubs the place with some rough cloth, and washes the place with warm water until the artery appears clearly; then take the spatulum made from which there is the form:
puis escorche le cuir legierement tant que tu veignes a l’artere, puis la trai en haut as pinceures, et la depart bien des toiles que sont desoz li de chescune partie; et se li artere est subtilz, si la torne a la pointe de l’uncine, puis la cope de celle partie selonc la quantiteit des .ij. chiés. Car s’elle n’est copee, si ne saut mie li sans dou tout en tout.	then scrape the skin lightly until you reach the artery, then pull it upward with tweezers and loosen it well from the tissues beneath in each part; and if the artery is delicate, return it to the hook of the fingernail, then bandage that part according to the amount of the two fingers. For if it is not bandaged, the blood will not stop flowing at all.
Et trai dou sanc des .vj. c/, jusc’a .iij.; et se li artere est grans, si covient que tu la lies en .ij. leus d’un fil double fort de soie, que porriture n’i veigne devant le soudement de la plaie, et veigne decorremens de sanc; puis cope la superfluiteit qui est entre les .ij. liiens en celle houre meisme, et puis, se tu vues, si lou cauterize dou cautere cutellaire jusc’a l’os tant que li chiés soient copez; et c’est li muedre oevre, se li malaides n’a fievre et il est de chaude complexion.	And draw out the blood from 1/4 to 3/8 of an inch; and if the artery is large, you should tie it in two places with a strong double silk thread so that pus does not come before the wound heals, and bleeding comes slowly; then bandage the excess between the two ties in the same hour, and if you wish, cauterize it with a hot-iron cautery up to the bone so that the shoulder is cut; and this is the best treatment if the patient doesn’t have a fever and is of a hot complexion.
Car li cauteres est aide por finir les moistors: por ceu est il de plus grant aide as moistors.	Because cauterization helps to end moisture; that is why it is more helpful for moisture.
Ou il covient por l’estraction des arteres que om emplisse lou leu de viel coton et mette on sus tentes bien faites; et quant on les desliera, si soit curez de medicines seches que font naistre char, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se sans cort de l’artere tant dis com tu i oevres, si te haste dou coper par cautere, ou tu emple lou leu de vitriole et l’estrain a ta main que li sans soit estainchiez; et se tu n’as ceu present, si met sor le leu ton doit tant que li sans soit congelez, et arose le leu d’aigue froide tant que li sans cesse, et soit estraint si com il covient; et ceu qui est muedre et plus legier en l’estraction de l’artere est que tu cauterizes la voinne de cest cautere trenchant de .ij. pars, mais li trenchant soient bien espés por warder plus longement lor chalor.	Or it is necessary for the extraction of arteries that one fills the place with old cotton and places it on well-made tents; and when they are taken off, cure them with dry medicines that cause pus to form, and with tents, until they are healed; and if there is an artery without a vein as far as you work, hasten to cover by cauterization, or employ vitriol and stretch out your hand so that the blood is stopped; and if you don’t have that at hand, put your finger on the place so that the blood congeals, and moisten the place with cold water until the bleeding stops, and bind it as it should be; and what is better and lighter in the extraction of an artery is to cauterize the vein with this cutting cautery of 2 parts, but let the cutter be well thickened so that its heat lasts longer.
Car quant li estrumens est trop tenves, si tient moins sa chalor.	For when an instrument is too thin, it holds its heat less well.
Et doit avoir entre les .ij. coutelz .i. doit de gros d’espaice, et puis quant tu as signiet d’enche les .ij. leus, et tu mes lou fer ardant sus tant qu’il viegne jusc’a l’os, et cope la voinne en .ij. leus; et soient esloigniet entre les .ij. chiés car il n’est mie soudez de cest cautere dou tout en tout; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And between the two knives there should be a space of a finger's width, and then when you have cut through both sides and placed the hot iron on as far as the bone, and split the vein in two places; and the two parts should be pulled apart so that they are not fused by this cautery all the way through. This is how the cautery tool should be formed:
des larmes	tears
Quant les larmes des eulz sont dessendans des voinnes que sont sus lou test dou chief de fuer, et il ne profite mie cure de medicine c’on i faice, et tu vois la faice dou malaide enrougir, et sent ou front ambulation si com de fremis; et sui oil sont tenve et moiste si que li poil des papieres sont cheut, et sont eschaufees les papieres, et escorchies de l’ardor des larmes, si ait mestier de ceste cure.	When tears are flowing from the eyes which are above the testicles on the head, and medicine does not help, and you see the face of the patient turning red, and there is a beating in his forehead as if from trembling; and if the eyelids are thin and moist so that the hairs have fallen out, and the eyelids are scorched by the heat of the tears, then this treatment is necessary.
Et l’apelerent li ancien «cure contuse», et est que tu faices a rere au malaide qui a ceste maladie les poilz qu’il ait ou front, puis li fai .iij. fendures ou front igalment selonc la longesce dou front; et soit l’une des fendures ausi com .ij. doi tout emmi lou front en avalant aval jusc’a neif, et les autres .ij. as .ij. costelz par desus les papieres, et te garde de l’incision des arteres que sont as .ij. costez par desus les papieres; et aloigne ta main de la continuation des .ij. mandibules, et soit chescune plaie la quantiteit de .iij. dois au traver joins;	And the ancients called it "cure contused," and you should do to the patient who has this disease, let him have hair on his forehead, then make three incisions on the forehead evenly according to the length of the forehead; and one of the incisions as two fingers all over the forehead going down to the nose, and the other two at the two temples above the eyebrows, and beware of cutting into the arteries that are on either side above the eyebrows; and keep your hand away from the continuation of the two jaws, and each wound should be the length of three fingers across joints;
et aies apparillie une piece d’esponge et mout de drapelz ses por essuer lou sanc, puis boute le spatumile agut de .ij. pars de coi ci est li forme:	and have ready a piece of sponge and some cloth to wipe away the blood, then insert the spatulum, cut into two parts from where there is the shape:
des l’incision qui est dever la temple jusc’a la seconde incision; et escorche tout le keur qui est entre les .ij. fendures a tot lou syfac qui est sus l’os, puis fai autreteil des la moiene incision jusc’a l’autre seconde, et puis estrai fuer cest spatumile.	from the incision that is to the temple up to the second incision; and scrape all the skin that is between the two incisions up to the bone, then do likewise from the middle incision up to the other second one, and then remove this spatulum.
si boute en la premiere fendure l’estrument qui est apelez «cultellaire», et est tresbien trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part est souef, ne mie trenchans, et c’est li forme:	then insert into the first incision the instrument that is called  "cultellarius," and it is very sharp on one side, and not at all sharp on the other, and this is its shape:
Et met le costeit taillant vers la char aerse au keur, et lou costeit souef vers l’os, et lou boute tant qu’il veigne a la moiene fendure. Et cope toz les vasselz que dessendent dou chief as eulz tant que l’incision soit continue jusc’a ceu qui apert dou keur, et puis autreteil fai en la moiene fendure jusc’a l’autre defuer; et puis estrai dou sanc igalment, et espresse lou leu por le sanc pris; puis met en chescune fendure une tente de viel coton, et met sus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile et en aisil, et garde que apostemes chaus n’i veigne; et au tier jor deslie lou liien, et i amenistre grant planteit d’aigue tede, puis lou cure d’oignement basilicon avec oile roset, et d’autres cures dont on cure plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And cut the incision towards the chest and the armpit to the heart, and the other incision towards the bone, and bind it tightly until it reaches the middle opening. And tie all the vessels that descend from the head to the eyes until the incision is continuous to what opens near the heart, and then another incision in the middle opening to the other defiant; then draw out the blood equally, and express the site for the extracted blood; then put a tent made of old cotton in each incision, and place moistened cloths in wine and oil and garlic on top, and guard against hot abscesses coming there; and on the third day loosen the bandage, and administer plenty of cold water, then treat it with basilicon ointment with rose oil, and other remedies for wounds, until it is healed.
dou reume des eulz	from the eyes
Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees; et li poil chieent, et ou chief en parfont a dolor ague, et li malaides esternue; adonques saiches par ces accidens que celles matieres et cil catharre ne vient fuer que de maintes voines, et li muedre cure que i est, si est ceste.	When someone has a constant catarrh, and you see the eyes are sunken and small, and the vision weakened, and the eyelids burnt, and the hair falling out, and in the head there is pain, and the patient sneezes; then know by these signs that these matters and this catarrh come from many veins, and the remedy for it is to cure what is inside.
Et est que tu comande au malaide a rere son front, puis fai une grant fendure emmi lou front, et une autre dou large. i. poc. Et comence des la fendure de la temple senestre a la temple destre, et soit li incision jusc’a l’os; et esloigne ta main des ners des temples que muevent au mengier; et quant li os est descovers, si essue tout le sanc a une esponge, et puis desevre entre les .ij. levres de la fendure et i met coton viel, et tentes de lin; puis lie desus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile, et te garde d’aposteme chaut; quant il est ostez, si covient que tu frottes l’os tant que chars i comence a naistre, puis le cure de choses exiccatives, que font enjanrer char.	And you should command the patient to lean back, then make a large slit in the middle of the forehead, and another one from ear to ear. Begin the incision from the left temple to the right, going down to the bone; keep your hand away from the nerves in the temples that control swallowing. When the bone is exposed, wipe away all the blood with a sponge, then separate the two lips of the slit and insert old cotton, and tent with linen; then bind dampened cloths soaked in wine and oil on top, and beware of hot abscesses. When it is healed, you should rub the bone until new flesh begins to grow, then treat it with astringent substances that promote healing.
En teil maniere: pren .ij. parties de flor de froment, et de colofoine .iiij. parties, et en fai emplaustre; et l’aministre en ces plaies por enjanrer char per tout.	In this way: take two parts of wheat-flower and four parts of colophony, make an ointment from it, and administer it to promote healing throughout the wound.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	on earaches
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des .iiij. choses: ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer; ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois; ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	All that falls into the ears is one of four things: either grains or a beast, or stone from a mine, or similar object like iron; or seed, such as peas, beans, and lentils; or flowing liquid, like water and garlic and similar things.
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel. Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction; et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine; et estent l’oreille au desus. Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure; et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	When it falls into the ear, a pebble or some other object that does not adhere to the ear or grow in it, then expose the ear to the sun. If you see the pebble, then distil some violet oil or oil of camphor, and then administer extraction; and make the patient sneeze with a spice, and plug their nostrils when they sneeze, and place pieces of cloth or wool around the ear; and keep the ear elevated. Often it comes out through this treatment; and if it does not come out, then administer extraction with fine tweezers, which are made like this:
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin; se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure; et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne; puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit; et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor; puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	If it comes out with the tweezers, that is good; if not, then administer extraction with a fine needle of small wire; and if it does not come out in this way, then make an iron hook and insert the tip of the hook into the ear canal firmly, and plug the area around the hook with soft wax so that air cannot enter with the hook; then pull it out gently, for often it comes out as we have said. And if it does not come out in such a way, then take some glut and use it to grab birds, and place some instrument that is suitable for this purpose, and put some cotton around it; then press the glut onto the pebble or whatever it is, and pull it out.
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme; et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant; et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche; et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it does not come out with all the things we have said, then be quick to split the ear so that pus and blood comes out, and a spasm; and the manner of the splitting is that you first make the patient fast for three days, and bleed him according to his condition, then make him sit between your hands and turn his ear upwards, and make a small slit in the root of the ear at the fat where it depends; and the slit should be like a crescent moon, so that you can reach the pebble, then remove it according to your ability, and suck on it strongly with your mouth; and treat it until it is healed.
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction; et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre .i. spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	And if it is a grain that is inside and it swells, then administer removal; and if it cannot come out, then administer .i. spatumile with a thin needle according to this form:
et amenistre incision de celui grain. Mais ne faire mie ceu quant tu penses que li grains est moistes por la moistor de l’oreille, tant que tu en aies fait maintes pieces; puis l’estrai as pinceures subtilz et au succier, si com nos avons dit, si que li estractions soit aligie.	and administer an incision on that grain. But do not do this when you think the grains are moist due to moisture in the ear; instead, make many pieces of it and then extract them with thin pincers and a succor, as we have said, so that the extraction is easy.
En l’aigue donques que chiet en l’oreille covient que li malaides use d’esternuement de condisi premiers, et ample l’oreille de viel coton. Et soit gisans sus celle oreille meisme ou li aigue est. s’elle saut fuer per ceu, c’est boin. se ceu non, si prent maintes pieres selonc li longesce de ton doit tenves et legieres, et les eschaufe un poc au feu; et em mette li malaides une ou pertus de son oreille, et saille sus i. de ses piez d’autre part, et fiere d’une autre piere sus la piere qui est en l’oreille; et ne cesse de faire ceu de piere em piere tant que li aigue isse toute fuer, et ensi saut elle toute fuer; et se tu vues, si prent .i. jonc, et boute l’un des chiés en l’oreille, et l’autre chief emprent de feu tant que li plus dou jonc soit ars; puis refai autreteil d’autres jons tant que li aigue isse toute, si com nos avons dit en la piere.	In the case of an earache due to fluid in the ear, the patient should use a mild emetic and pack the affected ear with soft cotton. And they should lie down with the affected ear facing upwards, or if the fluid drains out on its own, all the better. If not, they should take several thin stones according to the size of their finger, heat them slightly in fire, and then insert one end into the ear, and press the other end with another stone; and they should continue doing this with different stones until the fluid drains out completely, as we have said for the stones.
En l’estraction de la beste, s’elle est de petit cors, si com puce et semblans chose, cure la si com nos avons dit en la division; mais s’elle est de grant cors c’on la puisse sentir, si amenistre extraction de pinceures; et c’est li chose plus legiere a oster qui soit en l’oreille.	In the extraction of an object from the ear, if it is a small object such as a flea or similar, treat it as we have said in the previous chapter. But if the object is large enough to be felt, administer extraction with pincers; and this is the easiest method to remove something from the ear.
En l’estraction des vers enjanrez as oreilles, quant tu lou cures si com nos avons dit en la division et ou traitier des distillations, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu regardes l’oreille au soleil: s’il i apert nulz vers, si les trai as pinceures subtilz, et s’il n’aperent, si prent la cainne de coi ci est li forme:	When extracting worms from the ears, if you treat them as we have said in the section on distillations and the treatment does not help, then you should examine the ear in the sun. If any worms appear, then catch them with fine tweezers; if they do not appear, then take the skin of a chicken where the comb is,
Et soit estroite desoz et large desus. Et boute lou plus subtil chief en l’oreille selonc la quantiteit de la soffrance dou malaide, puis succe forment a tot la caine; fai ceu sovent tant que tuit li ver issent.
