Et s’il n’obeissent a issir, si estoupe entor la cainne de coton si com j’ai dit en la piere; et s’il ne saillent fuer si com nos avons dit, si aministre distillations que li ancien ont esprovees en l’ocision des vers, et tu les troveras ou traitier des distillations; et si distille tes oiles et tes medicines en l’oreille a tout cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme si com tu vois:	and tie the narrow end tightly beneath and leave the wide end loose above. Then insert the thinnest end of the chicken skin into the ear according to the amount of suffering from the illness; suck on the chicken skin until all the worms come out. If they do not come out, then stuff cotton around it as I said before for the stone; and if they do not emerge as we have said, administer distillation remedies that ancient healers have proven effective against worms, and you will find these in the section on distillation remedies; also, distill your oils and medicines into the ear through this instrument so that the worms come out as you see:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain estrois desoz a .i. petis pertuis, et desus overs por distiller; et por presser dedens la distillation a .i. estrument d’arain bien fait por ceu, et se tu vues pren .i. raseur et envoloupe entor la pointe avenanment coton; puis i giete ton oile ou ton jus, et ceu que tu vues de tes medicines en la cainne, et li caine soit en l’oreille; puis boute dedens lou raseur a tout lou coton, et presse ta main tempreement tant que li oile soit distilleit ou chevement de l’oreille; et lou sente li malaides dedens, et soit li distillations .i. poc eschaufee au feu ainsois c’on la distille en l’oreille; et garde qu’elle ne soit trop froide, car li medicine ne seroit mie si bone.	And it should be made of silver or bronze with small holes beneath and open above for distillation; and to press the distillation into this instrument use a well-made bronze tool, and if you wish take a razor and wrap cotton around its tip; then pour your oil or juice, and whatever medicines you desire, into the chicken skin, and let the skin be in the ear; then put the razor with all the cotton inside, and press your hand gently so that the oil is distilled into the ear; and the patient will feel it inside, and the distillation should be slightly warm as it is poured into the ear; and take care that it is not too cold, for the medicine will not work as well.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	on the stopping of the ears
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles; et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir; et aucune fois avient .i. poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	No child is born without an opening in their ears; and the same thing happens to men due to the clogging of a wound, or due to pus forming inside the ear, and sometimes this clogging extends deep into the ear, so that one cannot see it; and sometimes there is only a slight blockage, which can be seen easily.
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil; et regarde dedens: se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	When it occurs deeply and cannot be seen, it is a matter of great concern in various situations, and in such a case, one should hold the affected ear towards the sun; and look inside: if you see the membrane becoming apparent, then treat it according to its appearance.
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille; se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	And it should be sharp and pointed in front and behind, so that it does not pierce the ear; if the membrane is due to pus or some other substance inside the ear, then grasp it with a pair of fine forceps and squeeze gently until all the substance is removed.
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren .i. raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille. Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille; puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	And if the membrane is deep within the ear, take a small, fine rasor and heat it slightly in the fire, then place it inside the ear. If the patient feels pain when hearing, pierce gently, and be careful not to damage the nerves of the ear; then insert a tent into the ear according to the size of the opening, and moisten it with Egyptian ointment.
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet; et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Do this each day until the wound is healed, or take a piece of cloth and moisten it in rose water, and powder with vitriol; and if you see swelling in the ear, then you should remove the cloth and replace it with another moistened in cerotum made of rose oil and wax, until the swelling is gone; then heal the wound.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	And if there is bleeding, plunge a sponge and cloth in cold water, and place it on the ear, and use other remedies that stop the bleeding that are used for treating distilleries.
de la char des papieres	of the pulp of papers
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	This althelul comes from papers when they are wet and dry, you should extend them with tweezers and pincers, and the tip of a spatulum from its roots; then put powdered vitriol on the spot.
Et se sans en decort, si le cauterize dou cautere lenticulaire subtil, et li cauterizeir aprés l’incision vaut mues; et maintes fois repairent, cant aucune chose demoure de lor racines; et quant elles sont cauterizees par feu, si sont arses celles racines et ne revienent mie.	And if without skin, then cauterize with a subtle lens-shaped cautery, and the cautery after the incision is valuable; and many times they return, as long as nothing remains of their roots; and when they are cauterized by fire, those roots are burned and do not return.
de la gresle	of hailstones
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz; li ovraiges est telz: pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir; fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope. se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide; et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	Many times they come in papers as things that look like hail in shape and hardness, and this is why this disease is called "hailstone"; it is an assembly of moisture thick on the paper above and below; the work is such: take care if the hailstones move from one side to another, and it's a simple thing to know; then they open the paper slightly, then peel it off gently with tweezers, and cover it. If you can't cover it without piercing the paper, it won't harm the patient; and if the split is large, then they put together with a stitch, and cure it until it is healed; and if it is small, they do not force it, for the ointment will restore it at once and heal the wound.
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre; et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien; et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	And if the hailstone is descending inside the ear towards the upper part, then reverse the paper, and the hailstones are held with tweezers, and covered and pressed from one side to another; and if the paper is separated by the incision, it does no harm; and when the hailstone is covered, wipe away the pus with a clean cloth, and cure the area where the wound is until the patient is healed.
de la graisse des eulz	of the fat of the eyes
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz; et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil. Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	Exinach is a fat that is woven into the papers above, and this happens more to children than to no one, and it is very painful for their eyes, and they get catarrh in the mornings, and cannot look at the light of the sun because their tears hasten to their eyes. And because of this, they lie on their faces and sleep on top of them, and their eyelids become moist, and the swelling and appearance are covered by exinach which appears in the eye. And when you press the area with your fingers, it comes out between them.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain; et puis pren .i. drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li; et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle; puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne; et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach; et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.	And the way to do it is that the sick person puts his head on top of the healthy one; and then take a linen cloth and prepare a tent in the form of a circle according to the quantity that contains exinach from each part, and then put it over him; and press with your fingers on both sides so that the exinach is gathered inside the circle. Then make an incision in the middle of the moist skin with a sharp spatulum, and do not make it larger than the wound made for the vein opening; and in various dispositions, exinach comes out of the slit according to the shape of a piece of white grease.
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars; et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	Then take out the entire piece of cloth with your fingers between your thumb and forefinger, and turn your hand to the right and left so that it is spread out; and be careful not to put anything in the slit, so that you do not come to the spatula all the way to the eye, so that you do not hurt it.
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere; puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	And if the wound does not open at the beginning of the slit, then widen the slit slightly until it opens; then extract as we have said, then moisten cloth in vinegar and water, and apply to the area, and extract with bandages.
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree. Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez. Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if there are such men who grind salt and apply it to draw out the moisture that remains. Then treat the wound until it is healed. And if a hot abscess comes to the site, then treat it with soothing poultices until it is healed.
des poilz des papieres	of the hairs of paper
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz; et est li cure selonc .iiij. manieres: ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	When papers grow hairs of a different nature than usual, and they are enveillit, they harm the eyes and cause various diseases, such as tears, and softening of the paper and albugine, all of which lead to the destruction of the eyes; and there are four ways to treat them: by cauterization with fire, or by medicine applied to the eye, or by incision and stitching, or by caustic substances, depending on what is described in this chapter on cauterization.
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre; s’elle est convertie, c’est boin; se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout .i. fil desus; et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai .i. fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur; puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit; puis estrai .i. fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	It is necessary for you to place the head of the patient in your lap, then turn the paper on his eye to your left hand; if it is turned, that is good; but if not, then put an needle with thread through it from above; and have this close to the margin of the paper where the hairs are growing next to these hairs, and draw the thread across the paper to the top, and turn it over to the razor; then, on the part under the paper, under the hairs, all around, as much as the spatulum covers, from the large eyebrow up to the small one; then pull out the thread, and place a little tent of cotton and linen underneath the paper, and sign a figure of an inch, like the shape of a myrtle twig, and still it is necessary that the figure be according to the quantity you see rising above the paper which is split in two.
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie; puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les .ij. lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit; et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des .ij. angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute; puis assemble les .ij. levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout .i. fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les .ij. sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce; et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a .iij. jors ou .iiij.; puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor;	And if you are dealing with someone who needs a large amount of paper, according to how much the paper has softened, then proceed around the spatulum on the two lines that you have marked, and start from the large eyebrow up to the small one; and let one of the slits be near the natural hairs in the thickness of a hair root, then insert the needle into one of the two corners of the eyelid, and cut it all away; then bring together the two edges with a single stitch of fine woolen thread using an needle, and draw out the blood, and dry up the excess thread above the two eyebrows with any sticky substance if you wish to do so; but if not, then leave the stitch and threads for three or four days; then treat the wound without a stitch using dry, constricting substances, for the paper lifts away from the wound as it heals, but the stitch is harmful (as the ancients say), and this is work without fear;
et si a une autre maniere: et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a .iij. oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	and there is another way: it is to mark the paper with a figure that is like the shape of a myrtle twig, as we have described, with three branches evenly spaced according to its form:
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	then cut away what is on top of the smaller forces evenly according to the form which is here:
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait .i. fil, et la boute emmi la figure; et boute .i. autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment; puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans;	And if you do not have the strength to hold the tweezers, and the thing is not equal, then take a needle or thread, and sew it up according to the shape; and sew another thread next to the large artery, and the second thread next to the small one, and bring the threads together between your fingers evenly; then lift your hand evenly, and lift all the skin above which you have signed, as we have described, then bring the two lips of the wound together by sewing, and cure it until it is healed; and if an abscess comes to your incision, then soothe it with cerot and similar soothing ointment;
et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit: si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision; mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	and sometimes the hair of the paper is turned inside out: so you must use what we have said about the incision; but the sewing in one and the other is more artificial.
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme: et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai .ij. caines par art, et .ij. liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est; et cope as .ij. chiés de .ij. pars ou tu tiens les filz; puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les .ij. cainnes des .ij. parties forment; et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	The cure for warts is according to this form: and it is that you turn the paper inside out and cut it inside according to what I have said, and then make two warts by art, and two subtle threads as long as the paper and the broad scale of the wart; and cut at two heads where you hold the threads; then bring one and the other together subtly over what is on top of the paper of the eye, and strain the two warts from the two parts formed; and leave it thus for several days, and the skin which is strained will die and blacken and fall off, until it falls off by itself.
S’il tarde, si le cope aunes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil; et c’est li forme des .ij. cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	If it is delayed, the cautery will force out pus until it heals; and when the wound is sewn up, and the paper removed, the hairs will no longer grow; and this is the form of the two canes which you shall make according to this figure, and according to this quantity of length and breadth:
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute .i. fil de soie souef et subtil; puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc; puis ordene en la chasse .i. autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil; puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain; et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil; puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a .i. ou .ij. ou .iij. ou plusors; puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	the work is such that you thread a fine needle with a fine silk thread; then bring the shoulders together and tie them up gently, and let the length of the threads be about the size of a palm; then prepare another fine silk thread in the needle, and tie off the ends of the thread; then have the patient place his head on your lap; and be in the sun so that the work is exposed, for it is a subtle and small work, then insert the needle through the paper to the root of the hair, and draw out the hair until it comes out of the paper with the natural hair; then extract your hand until the hairs come out of the paper with the natural hair.
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil; adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus; et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne .i. poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	And if the thread is pulled and the hair does not come out with it, then pull the thread from underneath until the thread comes out of the hole above and you see it with your eye; then pull on the thread and the hair, and close your eye for two or three days, so that the hair regrows in its place and the flesh grows over it again; and if the hair is short, accompany a long hair from the eyebrows, and let it grow with the one you are treating until it is elongated and then release it.
de la porriture de l’oil	of the puffiness of the eye
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de .ij. manieres: l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.  Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	When this disease called "aleacrati" or puffiness occurs in the eye, there are two ways it can happen: one is natural, and the other is unnatural. And it happens suddenly from a wound, or cutting, or cauterization, and from similar things.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent. Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere; mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic; et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	And the method of treatment for this is that you split the swelling and loosen the eyelids, and put in tents of linen, and change them until it is healed; and you must not use anything in its treatment that dries and constricts. For if you do, the disease will return worse than before; but rather use emollient things, such as fenugreek; and rosewater or altered and seeded, and daiquilon melted in one of the oils, and wrap a tent around it, and treat it thus.
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant; et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	And the essence of your treatment is that you take care that it does not swell again according to the form it was before; and these works that we have said are only remedies for this disease, so that it does not return according to the form it was before.
de la char qui vient en l’oil	of the flesh that comes in the eye
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens. Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans; et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait .i. fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en .ij. chiés de la char; puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a .i. spatumile large.	This disease which is underneath and is truly called "axacrati", has natural and accidental causes. The accidental cause comes from wounds and splits and cauteries and similar things; and the way to treat it is that you grab a needle with a double thread, insert it into the flesh, and make it pierce from the left tear duct so that the threads come out on both sides of the flesh; then the flesh will be above all of the needle, and the lump will be as wide as a spathamile.
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin; se ceu non, si pren .i. raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent .ij. fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere; et soient li chiés des .ij. fendures des .ij. angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «.j. griesche»; puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les .ij. parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne; puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the shape of the paper returns as it should be, that is good; if not, then take a razor and put it in the split, and turn the paper over, and make 2 splits along the edge inside the paper; and let the shoulders of the 2 splits be at the 2 angles of the incision you have made, so that when they are assembled, the shape is like that of a letter with the number "1", and then remove that flesh according to how much it has grown underneath, following the paper, then join together the 2 cut parts, and sew them up with a thread of wool; then treat it with the medicines for softening that we have mentioned, and with poultices, until it is healed.
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant; puis desevre entre les .ij. leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit; et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil; et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	And if the disease comes from a split or wound or cautery, then you should make a single split underneath the hairs of the papers, and according to what is said above; then separate between the 2 lips of a poultice, as I have said; and one must do the treatment according to the form of the disease, for it is very diverse in shape, and the wise masters prepare things with all their power so that they make the shape return to its natural form; and the patient himself, according to what he needs of treatment and instruments in various dispositions.
dou soudement de la papiere	from sudden papery
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut; et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil; et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil; et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere; puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef; et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez.	When this sudation occurs in human hands in such a way that the paper above is sodden with the white of the eye, and cannot move or perform its natural functions, then you must push the tip of a razor beneath the paper, and lift it upward; and hold it with tweezers, until you grasp what is hurt in the subtile spatula, which is not too pointed nor too trenchant, so that the patient cannot bear that the too-pointed spatula might pierce the eye; and your incision to peel this union should be light, so that the paper returns according to its natural form; and all this union is healed, and they sometimes make in the eye a salty wash, and lift it with sweet water, and use a collarette; then place between the paper and the eye a tent of linen, and place over the eye wool moistened with egg; and after the third day use the collarette and the soothing things until it is healed.
de l’ungle de l’oil	of the nail of the eye
Saiches que li ungle est selonc .ij. manieres: elle est nervouse et semblans a .i. dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om; et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil.	You know that the nail is in two ways: it is nervy and resembles a .ij. hard syphac, and another which is not nervy, but resembles white congealed moisture; and when touched with iron and pinched with tweezers, it cannot feel anything; and both appearances begin towards the great tear duct, and grow little by little until it covers the entire sight, light, and movement of the eye.
Et li maniere de l’incision si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz; et lieve la papiere a ta main, puis coil l’ungle as pinceures de petite doubleure, et l’estent au desus; puis pren une aguille, et i met .i. poil de cheval, ou de vaiche, ou de buef, et .i. fil fort; et double la pointe de l’aguille un poc et la fiche emmi l’ungle, et la perce a tout l’aguille, et lie l’ungle d’un fil et l’estent au desus, et escorche a tout lou poil le costeit de l’ungle qui enseut la prunele et la soie au poil jusc’au chief, puis cope lou remanant en la racine dou larmier a tout lou spatumile subtil et as petites forces, et laisse la char natureil ou larmier, si que par l’incision ne veigne li cors des larmes acostumeement; et aucune fois s’estent li ungle a l’oncine soulement, et au fil, si com nos avons dit; puis l’escorche on a tout le spatumile souef de coi ci est li forme:	And the manner of the incision is that the patient puts his head in your lap, then you work the eyes; and hold the paper in your hand, then curl the nail with tweezers of small doublets, and place them on top; then take a needle, and put in it one horsehair, or cow's hair, or ox's hair, and a strong thread; and double the point of the needle a little and insert it among the nails, and pierce all the way through the needle, and tie the nail with a thread and place it on top, and scorch all along the hair the edge of the nail which follows the eyelid and the silk to the hair up to the head, then cut off the remaining part at the root of the tear duct all the way to the subtile spatumile and with small forces, and leave the natural flesh or eyelid, so that through the incision does not come the body of the tears accustomed; and sometimes only the nail is placed on the oncine, and with the thread, as we have said; then scorch it all the way along the spatumile:
Et garde que li spatumile ne touche la toile charnue et la rompe, et que li prunele ne soit percie; et aprés l’incision giete en l’oil un poc de seil broiet, et dou coliere fait de litargire, et le laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; puis le cure de ceu qu’il i covient tant qu’il soit sanez. And raise the nail gently, and if you see that it does not diminish and the pus is pressing out, then distil from your mouth into the eye a collar made of litharge and red copper and crushed seal, and stop up the eye until the next day; then recommence the other work according to this same procedure, until it is all removed.

If there is no obstruction in the eye, such as an abscess, then use milk, and first treat the abscess with a hot poultice until it is healed, then recommence the procedure as before, until it is healed.

de la char qui naist sus la prunelle	of the flesh which grows on the eyeball

des voines des eulz	of the eyes
Sebel sont voinnes rouges que sont covertes sus l’oil, et tolent a la veue son ovraige et afoiblissent l’oil toz jors. de la fistule de l’oil	of the eye fistula
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule: quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers.	The "arissati" fistula: when you cure it with cautery and medicine according to what I have said before, and it is not healed, then pierce into the abscess where it must be, and draw out all the moisture until the bone is exposed.

puis le met sus l’os delez lou larmier, et esloigne ta main de l’oil .i. poc, puis torne a tot le foret tant qu’il perce l’os et le sent li malaides par ceu que li vens en ist s’il tient sa main sus son neif; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines seches, si com je t’ai ensigniet, et quant li char naist et endurcist li leus, si vait li matiere au neif; si est plus legiere chose au malaide.	then place it on the bone underneath the fistula, and move your hand away from the eye a little, then return to the needle until it pierces the bone and the patient feels it through the pressure of his blood; then restore the area with dry medications as I have instructed you, and when the flesh hardens and closes over the opening, examine the matter at the fistula; this is a gentler treatment for the patient.

When the eyes are completely open and there is no disturbance to the nose or diminution, you should ligature the patient; then bleed him, then apply cupping glasses or leeches without piercing, to suck out, then place over the eye a poultice made of acacia gum, aloe, incense, and sarcocolla, and then compress the eye with bandages and drapes; the manner of the drapes is that you take quite soft drapes, and double each one in four, and then place one on top of another according to the quantity that the eye requires; then compress from above with a firm bandage, and repeat the cupping without piercing; then remove the cupping glasses and leave the eye compressed day and night, and if the ligature softens, you should compress it strongly; then remove the poultice after a day and a night, and if you see the eye healing, that is good; if not, repeat the poultice, and the drapes, and the poultice, and the cupping until he is healed.
dou derrompement de toile uvee	from the ruptura of a woven cloth

de la bowe de l’oil	of the eye socket
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue; et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus .i. siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de .ij. pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz; puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit; et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit. si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee .i. poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse; et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	This disease, which is called "alcunnati", is nothing but an accumulation of fluid in the eye socket, resembling water but not actually being water. The appearance and treatment of this condition are as follows: have the patient sit upright and still, then hold their head steady with your hands from both sides and move it until you see the fluid rise to your eyes. Then stop and let it settle, ensuring that the light shines through so that the patient can see as usual. If the fluid does not drain and the eye socket remains swollen as described, know that it is an accumulation of water. If the swelling is as we have described, have the patient sit still while you take a sharp needle and pierce the white of the eye where the conjunctiva meets the cornea, allowing the fluid to drain. Then treat the eye with warm honeyed water or water infused with fenugreek and honey until it is healed.
des aigues de l’oil	of the eye's waters

de la char sor le neis	of the heart by the nose
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color. En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil; et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers; puis cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	At times they arise from the nose as varied swellings, some resembling scorpions with many feet; and there are others in which there is a coloured swelling, and a pale sore. For that type of sore which is pale and not swollen, you should have the patient sit between your hands facing the sun; open his nostrils, and pour on the oil from an onycha, and draw it out with the tip of the stethoscalp, as far as you are able to endure it.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout .i. des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien; et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient; et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	And if anything remains that cannot be covered, then open it with one of the subtle instruments lightly, so that nothing remains; and if without you are overwhelmed, or an abscess forms, then lances it as it should be; and if it is a malignant abscess, then hasten to cauterize it until the pus is drained and all the pus is removed, then pour in wine or water.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, acoi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes .i. fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice .i. doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil. Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu .iij. jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	And if the ears are affected and moisture extends to the palate, know that it is healthy; and if moisture does not pierce as it should, know that there is pus in the bone above, so do not use instruments to cut: therefore you must place a thick linen thread in his nostril with your fingers, and have a space of a finger or less between each knot; and let the patient hold the end of the thread in their mouth to the limit of their strength, and pull it through until it comes out through the nose; and many children do this at school, and it is an easy thing for anyone who wants to do it. Then hold the end that comes out through the nostril in one hand, and the other end that comes out through the mouth in the other hand, and move them gently back and forth as you would with a bowstring until you feel that the thread has corrupted the pus; then pull the thread, wipe away the blood, moisten the thread in Egyptian ointment, and reinsert it into the nostril as before. Do this for three days or more, until the ointment corrodes all that remains of the pus; then put a plug of wool in the nostril for several days until it is healed, and if medicine is needed to dry the wound, then use it. This is the form of the instrument used to cleanse the ears, through which oils and medicines are distilled into the nose:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait .i. mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	And it can be made of silver or brass, similar to an open lamp, with a handle, and it should also have a lid; and if you want, make a closed cane, and let the instrument be hollow for cleansing the ears; and it should have a handle at the end for holding it when heating oil or any liquid.
de la char sor le neis	of the heart upon the veins
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	Many times a disease called "tuberculosis" arises in the head of the veins, and it grows and becomes large, so that it is visible to look at; and therefore you should cut it at the beginning, and remove all the pus, then place the hot cautery or medicine upon it; and if one delays cutting it until it has become large, then be wary if it is hard, discolored, and lacking in sensation: do not touch it with iron, for it is an abscess, because when one cuts it at any time, great harm comes to the patient. And if the abscess is due only to pressure, not discoloration, and you see that one can cut it all away, then evacuate the patient and cut it without fear, and cure the area of dry and constricting things.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	when the vein is cut and sewn
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes. Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les .ij. levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les .ij. levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet; et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Know that when a vein is cut and sewn, it profits little in some people. Therefore, whenever this happens to someone, one should look to see if the wound has all its blood; and then join the two lips with a single stitch, and cure it until it is healed. And if the lips are torn on both sides, then one should scrape all the parts of their skin until they heal, then join the two lips with a single stitch, and tighten them, and powder them with dragon's blood powder and ground incense; and place an ointment on the powder, either a strong one or another ointment that promotes healing. Leave it to heal by itself, then cure it with ointment until it is healed.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	The method of sewing is that you use thread: either with needles as we said for sewing the belly, or with thread as I have already told you.
des apostemes des levres	of abscesses on the lips
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	At times there are hard abscesses inside the lips, resembling grains of peas, both smaller and larger; therefore, you should open the lips, and cut on each nodule, and pinch it with tweezers, and scrape away any dry matter until the wound is cleaned out; then apply vitriol powder to the incision, and then use an astringent, and treat the area with poultices until it is healed.
de la char des gencives	of gum disease
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	Many times a growth arises on the gums, which the ancients call 'albulus'; you should hold it with tweezers, cut at its root, and let the blood or pus flow; then place powdered vitriol, or other restraining and drying powders, on the site; if the growth returns after the incision, and this often happens, cut it again and cauterize it; if it does not return after cauterization, and this is the form for treating abscesses.
des sordens	Here is a translation of the provided text:
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	Here is a translation of the provided text:
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	It is necessary when treating a toothache that you delay as little as possible in pulling the tooth, for there should be no excuse not to do so; for it is a very serious matter to delay.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant. Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	Therefore, when the patient is forced to draw breath, you must be certain which tooth is causing the pain. Often, the pain deceives the patient, leading them to believe it is a sound tooth, and they have a healthy tooth pulled; and yet the pain persists as long as the diseased tooth remains, for we have already seen this happen to these patients. And when you are certain which tooth is causing the pain, you must scrape around the tooth all the way to the gum; then open the mouth wide to push back the gum on all sides; then probe the tooth with your fingers or fine tweezers, gently at first until it is well loosened, then grip tightly with the tweezers. Have the patient's head between your knees, and hold it firmly so that it does not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier. Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	Afterwards, pull out the tooth carefully without breaking it, and if it will not come out, take one of these instruments and insert it gently into each side of the tooth, then move it as you did before. And if the tooth is decayed and eaten away, you must fill the holes with lint, and then grip it tightly with tweezers so that it does not break while being pulled; and you must work gently around the gum to loosen the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere. Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	And be careful not to break it, and leave a part of it behind, which often brings greater pain to the patient due to the root remaining in place. And beware of doing as ignorant surgeons do, who, through their haste and arrogance, sometimes break the jaw, and do not heed what we have instructed; they sometimes bring great illness due to the roots left behind, or by breaking the jaw, as we have often seen. Once the tooth is pulled, wash the socket with wine or garlic and salt; and if there is bleeding, which often happens, apply powdered vitriole to the socket; and if that does not work, cauterize it.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The forms of forceps, with which one pulls out teeth first, should have long points and thick handles so that they do not bend when you pull the tooth; and these are the forms:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And they should be made of thick metal so that they do not bend when pulling, and they should be well-made iron, and serrated to hold the gums.
de la racine des dens	from the root of teeth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre .i. jor ou ij., tant que li leus soit amolis, puis i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	When the root remains in place, you should apply wet cotton over the area for a day or two, until the gums are softened. Then, use forceps called "algefri", which resemble a doctor's mouth, and inside them are serrated like a file. This is their shape:
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not want to come out with all these tweezers, you must uncover the skin all around the root, and insert the instrument called "althali", that is, a splint, which has this shape:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	And it should be strong and thick so that it does not break, and if the root jumps out through this, that is good; if not, then you must use all the instruments, of which the forms come later:

et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	and other tools that are in front of teeth, and this instrument which looks like a large pair of tweezers, whose shape is:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	And have this instrument outside so that it cannot be broken, and know that many instruments for teeth are; and also other instruments, which are not counted; and the wise subtle master finds by himself his instrument, according to what his works and the disease show him, because there are many diseases where the ancients did not teach any instrument due to their diversity. And if it doesn't break the cart or other bones, or it protrudes, then he searches for the instruments he needs, which I have told you about, and helps with gestures, of which this is the form:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And let them be thick and well-fitting to hold the bone so that it doesn't slip, but he can hold and remove it; and then restore the place with appropriate medicine. And if there is protrusion in the bone, and it is small, then use this instrument:
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a .i. petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When the tooth appears not according to the natural body, and its shape is ugly, especially in virgin women, then you should know whether the tooth is new after the tooth, and it is not in the right place, and it cannot be filed or ground down. So pull it out; and if there is abscess with the tooth, take this instrument of which the form is like a small beak, and let it be made of iron with a sharp point at its end:
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And push it in and out little by little due to the hardness of the tooth, and so that you do not move the others. And if it is apparent, and can be filed down, then file it with a special file as shown in the form:
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	and is also like the file with which we make needles; and in filing, press gently, day after day, little by little, until it does not move, and then smooth it at the end with a file, and if the tooth is too sharp and cuts the tongue, one should file down the sharpness until it is even so that it doesn't cut the tongue or distort speech.
quant li dent lochent	when the teeth are crooked
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les .ij. dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a .i. ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper. Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des .ij. dens sains, et des .ij. meus, si com tu vois:	When the front teeth are crooked, either from a blow or from falling, and the patient cannot chew without spitting it out, and you have treated them with constricting medicines, but to no avail, then they must be restrained with a gold wire because silver wires turn green and rot, but gold never moves. The wire should be neither too thin nor too thick, depending on the amount of space between the teeth. Then, if you want to straighten the teeth, take the wire and hook it between the two healthy teeth, then place the crooked teeth in between, as many as there are, until you reach the healthy tooth on the other side; then go back to the starting point and pull your hand gently but firmly so that it does not move. The wire should reach all the way to the root of the tooth so that it cannot escape. Then, using tweezers, clasp the wire at one end and bring the two ends together, placing them between the healthy tooth and the crooked tooth so that they do not cut the tongue; then leave it as tight as possible for as long as it can stay, and if it comes undone or the wire breaks, then restrain it with another wire. It will remain like this and serve its purpose forever. This is how you straighten crooked teeth, both the front and back, as you can see in the diagram:
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	And when a tooth is missing, we replace it with a new one, as we have said; but only a wise and experienced person should do this, and sometimes we make a tooth out of cow bone and put it in the place of the defect, restraining it as we have described, and it remains and serves for a long time.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	to cover the thread of the tongue
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder. Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	There are two types of this thread which comes from under the tongue, either as a congenital condition or due to an injury. The treatment is to open the mouth of the patient and lift his head, then loosen the tongue and cover the nerve thread with a wide bandage until the tongue is dislodged from its socket. If there is any swelling or bruising due to an injury, soak the area in hot water, and if bleeding occurs, apply powdered vitriol; if not, cauterize it with a lentigo cautery, which is suitable for this purpose. Then treat it with other remedies until it heals.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see it is red or black or hard, and the patient does not feel any pain, do not touch it, as it is a sore; and if it is inclined to blanching and there is moisture, pierce it with a needle, and drain it from both sides; and if bleeding occurs due to your treatment, apply powdered vitriol until it stops, then return to your treatment until you have removed everything. Then raise the area with garlic and salt, and treat it with other remedies until it heals.
des apostemes de la gorge	Of abscesses in the throat:
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les .ij. amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer. Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez. Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	At times, masses form in the throat called "godath", which are properly called the two almonds. When you treat them as we described in the section on treatment, and they do not heal, be careful: if there are hard abscesses of a small size and light color, do not touch them with iron. And if they are red and the root is large, do not touch them with iron either, so that blood does not flow; but leave them until they burst on their own, or you will burst them; and if they are white in color and the root is thin, have an instrument to pierce them ready, but first check that the abscesses are calm and soothed. Then make the patient sit facing the sun, with his arms raised, and let the servant hold his hands between his own, pressing the tongue under all the instrument, from which this shape comes; it can be made of silver or thin brass like a knife:
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	Then you press the tongue against all this instrument, and you will see the abscess; take a needle and insert it into the almond, and draw it out above as much as you can; then draw some threads from the cloth with it, then cover the instrument with which this shape is made, so that it looks like a hook; and even though the heads are curved, and one towards the other, and they are very sharp, and made of iron or steel:
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you do not have this instrument present, then cover it with tongs, of which this is the shape:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les .ij. amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les .ij. amandres igament.	And let it be cut in one part and left uncut in the other; and when you have lanced one of the tonsils, lance the other in the same manner, and after the incision gargle the patient with hot water, and water and garlic, and if bleeding occurs, gargle with water, or scalded pomegranate peels, or bay leaves, and similar things, until the bleeding stops; then cure it until it is healed; and sometimes other abscesses develop in the throat besides the two tonsils, so lance them in the same way as the two tonsils.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir .i. aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi .i. jor ou .ij. Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis .ij. rains par les .ij. pertuis dou neis. Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un .i. oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	I treated a woman for an abscess that was inside her throat, namely, one abscess of small size; and she had almost completely blocked the throat, so that the woman could not breathe through the passageway which was closed off, nor eat or drink, and would have died within a day or two. And the abscess was already so large that it had forced its way out through both openings of the nose. I promptly inserted an incision into one of the openings, then pulled out a large amount of pus; next, I made another incision in the other opening of the nose, and cleared her mouth and pressed her tongue; afterward, I inserted the incision into the abscess, and lanced some of it, and only a little blood came out; thus the passageway of the throat was opened for the woman, and she began to drink water and then wine, and I continued to lance the abscess for a long time; and the abscess would grow again, filling up the space that I had emptied, until it became very large; so I packed it and cauterized it inside her throat: thus it ceased to grow. And I left those parts, and may God help her after me.
de l’uve	of the grape
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve». Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li. Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide. Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a .i. des .ij. estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des .ij. amandres. Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des .ij. amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee. Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor. Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague. Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	When the eye descends to the pupil and it is swollen and long, it is called "perpendicular"; if it is fat and round, it is called an "eye". When it is cured as we have said in the division, and the cure does not help, and you see that the skin of the aperture is soothed, and it is fine, you should cover it; if it is round and not long, and is blood-colored or fuschia or black, then you should avoid cutting into it, for there is great danger in doing so. Therefore, when you see it, according to its whiteness and length, have the patient sit facing the sun, and press his tongue against the instrument we mentioned earlier; then insert the needle into the eye, pull it downward, and cover it with one of the two instruments I mentioned for the incision on the two almonds. You should not cover more than the superfluity that extends beyond the natural limit, for if you do, it will harm the voice and speech. After the incision, use what we said about the incision on the two almonds, and cure it until it is healed. If the patient fears having it covered, then you should use a cauterization of the tongue without fear. And the way to cauterize is as follows: have the patient place his head on your shoulder, then press his tongue against the instrument we mentioned in the chapter on cauterization, and hold it with a hot iron so that it is not too thick or too thin; then use the shaft of this instrument, which has this shape:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés .iiij. jors ou .v. Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	And it has a handle at its head where the medicine is placed, like the handle of a spoon, and the instrument is applied to the whole medicine on the eye; and the patient should lie on his side so that the saliva and mucus from the medicine flow out of his mouth and do not descend into his throat and windpipe. Then hold your hand over the medicine and press it on the eye for half an hour, until you see it swell and the burning of the medicine is soothed; then take cotton and wrap it around any instrument, moisten the cotton in the medicine, and insert the instrument into the cotton around the eye, so that the cotton adheres to the eye; do this often until the cautery is complete, then leave it to dry for four or five days. If you need to renew the cautery with medicine, do so, and after the cautery, wash the area around the eye with cold water, and treat it with gargles until it is healed.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en .i. pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait .i. estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	This cure is safer than incision or cautery; if it is healed by fumigation in this manner, take calamin, hyssop, oregano, rue, chamomile, avens, and similar herbs, and assemble all or some of them in a pot, and add garlic, and let it boil. The pot should be well glazed with strong clay, and the handle of the instrument should be bent according to this shape:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut. Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	And it can be of silver or bronze, and one of the tools should be placed in the mouth of the patient so that the vapor rises to the eye through the tube, until the eye is mortified; after which he should be treated again frequently, until the eye dries out; and take care not to do this at the beginning of the onset of a hot abscess, for various things can happen then; nor should it be done except during the decline of a hot abscess. And if this instrument is not present, take a tube and put a raw egg yolk inside it, so that the mouth of the patient is not too hot; for the egg yolk will not let the vapor harm the mouth, and it is a salutary treatment together.
