Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou .i. morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge .i. fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren .i. estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	Often a fish bone or spine, or some other thing, gets stuck in the throat; so you should treat what you can see, and press the tongue against the sun with all your instruments, so that you move the object; and if it does not become apparent to you and is lodged in the throat, then you must make the patient vomit so that the food is cooked in the stomach; perhaps the thing will come out through vomiting. Or the patient swallows a piece of sponge, or a piece of navel, or a lettuce root, or a morsel of dry bread; and attach a string to the sponge and then swallow it; and when it reaches the spot, it will get stuck, and then you can pull it out; and if it does not come out through what we have said, then take an instrument of soft lead according to this form:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	And the instrument should be bent at the tip so that it can more easily enter the throat, and have its tip lifted up high; and take care not to touch the epiglottis, or he will vomit everything, nor push the bone inside; and move so that the patient swallows the instrument, so that he can move where the object is stuck; then he swallows it down, or pulls it out with all his strength, equally, until it comes out.
de la sansue de la gorge	of the blood from the throat
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit. Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout .i. petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu. Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine .i. fer chaut, et fai ce sovent. Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor. puis pren plein .i. voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	If the blood is not stopped by medicine, as I said in the division, then examine the throat of the patient facing the sun and press his tongue with the instrument I mentioned. If you see the blood, then draw it out with a small hook or delicate tweezers made for this purpose. If this does not work, take a long needle and insert it into the throat of the patient, then heat the end of the needle and repeat this often. If the patient is suffering from an excess of water, fill a glass with cold water, open his mouth, pour it in without swallowing, and move his hand frequently; as soon as the water touches the blood, it will withdraw.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier. Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes .i. pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	And if it does not withdraw as we have said, then smoke the patient with assafetida using the instrument I described for smoking the throat; do this many times, for it will certainly work. The method of the fumigation is to place burning charcoal in a pot and cover it with a perforated lid, and insert the end of the instrument into the hole. Then pour in your fumigation, and have the patient place the tip of the needle in his mouth and close his mouth so that the smoke does not escape, but reaches the blood; the blood will certainly withdraw now. If it does not, then repeat the fumigation many times. Let the patient suffer thirst, eat salted and sour things, and drink nothing; and then he will certainly urinate.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge; et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier; et vez ci la forme:	And if he does not urinate, then strengthen the body with hot baths and by anointing the body; it is good for him to stay in the sun and eat things that are warm. And if his body is very cold, then bathe his head first so that he does not move, then bathe his limbs; and if he still does not urinate, then bathe him all over, and let him eat and drink warm things. And if it goes as we have said, know that the blood has withdrawn.
li chapistres des apostemes	the chapter on abscesses
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en .ij. manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor. Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors. car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	There are many kinds of abscesses, as the recollections which come to us here and there in this book show, and they differ in their perforation and size. They occur in two ways, according to their appearance and what they contain. The second way is due to their location in the body. For example, an abscess in the head is different from one in the fundament, and an abscess in fleshy tissue is different from one that forms in joints, and each requires a different treatment.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures. Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre. Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	And one should not pierce an abscess unless the bowels are quiet according to their nature; and some abscesses must be pierced when they are ripe, and will not go away on their own accord, such as those that form near joints. For when an abscess forms near a joint, if you leave it until it is pus-filled, the ligaments and nerves of the joint may become corrupted, causing contraction in that limb. If the abscess is near a principal organ, delaying the piercing until it is ripe will harm the principal organ. If it is near the fundament, one should pierce it so that it matures; otherwise, it will form an absess deep inside, which will take a long time to heal. One should not pierce an abscess before its digestion is complete, except for those near the fundament, which may become pus-filled and cause pain.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	And one should know the time for piercing an abscess that is ripe according to its nature, and this occurs when the pain subsides, and the fever lessens, and the swelling and redness decrease, and there is less discharge and pressure from the head of the abscess, along with other signs. One should pierce where the abscess is largest and where there is the most discharge; and the piercing should be done in a vertical direction from the body, especially if the abscess is on the arms or legs, or near joints, affecting nerves and arteries, and in all similar cases where there is no fold.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre. Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit. Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui. Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.  Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme; et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com .i. drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes: et si a de telz que sont fendut en .iij. angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	Here are the translations for the provided text:
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites. Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois. Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite; et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton; et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre; et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor; puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Those without a head, like a superficial abscess, should be pierced directly; and when the abscess is large and has formed a great boil, and you pierce it, do not draw out all the pus in that hour but some of it; then dry the abscess until the next day, then draw out something again from it; do this several times until the pus comes out completely. Do this especially if the patient is weak, or a woman carrying a child, or a small child, or an elderly person. For the pus sometimes jumps out with force when you pierce the boil that they might die from it without your knowing. Therefore, be very careful with this chapter; and when you have pierced your abscess, dry the wound, and if the wound of the abscess is small, apply a tent made of linen or old cotton; but if it is a large abscess with many openings, you should place a tent in each one so that they face each other. And if you have cut into the skin of the abscess and opened it all around, fill it with old cotton or the shavings of unmoistened linen cloth, and leave it for three days; then remove it and treat it with ointment until it heals.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille .i. drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.  Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut; et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit; et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if bleeding occurs during your treatment, apply cold water and ash-water, and soak a cloth in it and place it over the bleeding area repeatedly. And if the bleeding persists, use the remedies and treatments I have described earlier in this book; and if it is winter, and the area is very nervous, you should place moistened tents and cloths soaked in warm wine and oil over the abscess; but if it is summer, and the area is fleshy, you should moisten the cloths with water and oil, or cold wine and oil, for three days as mentioned earlier; then loosen the abscess, dry and treat it as necessary until it heals.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes: or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	And now you must know generally about the treatment of abscesses; I have already told you how one should go about treating abscesses, and now see this chapter.
des soros	of sores
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances. Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz; et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire. Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout .i. estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient. Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc. Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien; puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens; se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit. Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit; puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez. Et se li apostemes tient .i. nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc; et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist; et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés. Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	And now you must know generally about the treatment of abscesses; I have already told you how one should go about treating abscesses, and now see this chapter. And now you must understand the nature of sores that come from the head, which are similar to those found on birds, like the warts on a chicken's leg, and there are many variations. Some are full of pus and blood; others are hard and pebbly in texture, and there is no doubt if the artery does not cause a contrary effect. The treatment for this type of sore is to use an instrument called an 'entromissoire', which will be described later, depending on what it contains. If it contains moisture, then open it from above. And when the moisture has been expelled, peel off the skin that contained it without leaving anything behind; otherwise, it will return as soon as you leave it alone, and you must repeat this process daily until it is completely healed. Then soak cotton in Egyptian ointment, if available; if not, in water and salt, and apply this to the wound, leaving it overnight; and continue this treatment daily until it is completely healed. If the abscess contains a hard lump of grease, treat it according to the method described below, opening it from above; then pierce your fingernails into it, and peel off the entire surface, and apply all your remedies to draw out the pus from under the skin. If the artery causes a contrary effect, then do as I have instructed you after. And so also treat any abscess that is pebbly in texture, cutting and curing it as I have described.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc. Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut .i. apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme; et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier; et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere. En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe; et les cure si com il covient.	And the treatment for a moist and pebbly abscess is easier, as it usually contains less blood. And sometimes there are abscesses on the head that do not contain moisture, and I once encountered such an abscess on the head of an old woman; it was like a hard, rough, white stone, and could not be broken open; had anyone tried to cut into it, they would have caused a wound as if with a stone. With abscesses coming from the head, especially those found on children and at the roots of the ears, the opening should always be at the lowest point to allow the pus to drain out; then treat them as necessary.
des scrophules	of scrofula
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre. Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit; et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes. Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit. en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde; si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les .ij. levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief; et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	Many times this abscess occurs in the neck, and under the armpits, and in the groin, and sometimes elsewhere in the body; they are numerous and intertwined with each other. Each scrofula is properly within its own capsule, as is the case with the tumor and the abscess of the head, as we have said; and there are many varieties of scrofula. There are some that contain moisture, and others that are malignant and resistant to treatment. Therefore, when you see one that is in a healthy condition upon examination, and resembles the color of the rest of the body, and is even all around, and not adherent to the nerves of the neck or the artery or the duct, and is not deep; then you should cut it open from above, and scrape away at each side, and the two lips of the wound will be drawn back, as we have said regarding abscesses in the head; and pull gently, little by little, being careful not to cut into any nerve or vein, and let there be no spasm or twitching so that the hand does not slip, and do not cut too aggressively, but only what is necessary.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie; et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir. Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses; puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde. Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement; puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	And if you cut into the vein or artery and it will not allow you to work, then put some vitriol powder into the wound, or any other powder that stops bleeding, and tie the wound closed; and leave it until the abscess is healed, and the wound softens and begins to discharge. And when the blood has clotted, return to your task, until you have finished; then inquire about whether there are any small scrofula remaining, and cut them out and clean them. And if there is a large vein in the root of the scrofula, then you should not cut that scrofula at its root, but ligature it with a strong double thread, and let it fall away from it without harm; then dress the wound with old cotton soaked in Egyptian ointment, and then treat the wound.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les .ij. levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule. si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit. Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure; et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption; et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you cut away the whole scrofula, then you must bring together the two lips of the wound and stitch them now, so that there is no superfluity remaining due to the size of the scrofula. Then you must attend to covering the root of it, pulling it out and sewing it as we have said. Those scrofulae which hold superfluity, pierce where it appears dead; and pierce it thus, as the one previously mentioned, hanging down, then administer tenting with ointment and similar things, so that it corrupts what is remaining of the corruption; and when the wound is clean, then cure it with ointment interwound with charcoal, until it is healed.
de squinance	of squint
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	The ancient wrote and spoke of the incision of the throat; but I have never seen it done in our land, and this is their written word.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en .ij. amandres.	For those who have squint, the flap of the throat called the 'epiglottis' should be cut; and this is done by those who have hot abscesses in their mouths, throats, or both armpits.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the disease is in the channel of the lung, it is necessary to cover the epiglottis to avoid the loss that comes from strangulation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz .iij. cercles ou .iiij. une petite fendure dou travers, entre les .ij. cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige;	Therefore, when we want to split the epiglottis, we should split it under three circles or four, a small split across, between two circles, or according to the quantity of the split in the larynx, not in the cartilage.
et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	and those places where it is suitable to split the epiglottis so that there is no meat, and the vessels are long from there.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit;	And if the masters are fearful, they should stretch the skin of the throat to the entire larynx, then split the larynx until it reaches the glottis; and avoid the blood vessels, if you see any, and then cover the larynx, as we have said.
et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix;	and is demonstrated by the section of the vein of the finger which leaps out through the place that is broken, and by the failure of the voice;
et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	and leaves the wound open for a space.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the hour has passed for which you doubt strangulation, bring together the two lips of the wound in the heart, and sew it up entirely without the cartilage; then administer remedies that promote scabs, until they are healed.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	Albucasis says to do this only as long as the throat is completely choked, and the patient is judged dead, and the lack of breath continues.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort;	So then cover the epiglottis so that the patient cannot swallow, and he breathes through the wound, and thus is guarded from death.
et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en .iij. jors ou en .iiij.	and for this the ancients commanded to leave the wound open until the maliciousness of the disease had passed, and it passes in three or four days.
Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee;	And then they commanded to sew up the wound and cure it, once it was cured;
et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	and I will tell you what I saw.
Je vis que une damoisele prist .i. coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon;	I saw a young maiden take a knife, and thrust it into her throat, and cut through some of the veins in her neck;
et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	and I was called to heal her, and found her as good as dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I uncovered the wound and found that the blood which had issued from it had not oozed or flowed further than the throat, and the vein had stopped bleeding.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee;	I hurriedly sewed up the wound and healed her so that she recovered.
et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition;	and she had no power over the lady until she was bled, and then she returned to her senses.
por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	That is why I say that one should not be afraid of cutting the epiglottis.
de la grosse gorge	of the large throat
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes;	This abscess is called a "gorge hernia", and it is a large abscess coloured yellow, and it occurs often in women.
et est selonc .ij. manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	and it occurs in two ways: natural and accidental; where the natural has no cause.
Et li accidens est selonc .ij. manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere;	And the accidental occurs in two ways, one of which is like a growth that comes from us, and the other way is like an abscess that comes from an artery;
et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire:	And there is fear in it, and one should not work to make force except in the small one, and test and search at all the openings:
se tu le trueves ausi com .i. nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point;	If you find it as smooth as a nut, and it cannot be cut, then cut it, as one cuts a nut, and treat it throughout its coat, if there is none;
et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	and search thoroughly, and treat it as necessary until it is completely healed.
des nous	of us
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances;	There are many ways of us, which I will tell all the similitudes;
et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	and now it is necessary that I say all the difference between us and issue.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture; adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	I say that discharge is continued fever, as long as the ebullition has not passed and the porridge is complete; then the fever and heat subside.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient .i. syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros;	With the nostril there is no heat or fever or pain, and it contains a pustule, which is its own sack and is according to the color of the body, and begins like a pimple, and becomes large;
et sont selonc ij semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	and they are according to their appearances, either greasy or moist, and very colorful as I have said in the division.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	It is necessary, when you come to the cure of the nose, that you test and inquire first with all the instruments which are called "forceps", according to what its shape will come to in the chapter which follows.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme;	And the method of inquiring into abscesses of the brain is to squeeze at the most moist spot that you find in the abscess, and gradually press your fingers in, as far as you know that the instrument has pierced the membrane, then according to the size of the abscess.
puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	Then pull out the instrument, and take care not to let anything escape.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes;	If the pus flows freely, whatever its colour, they should proceed as I have said for other abscesses.
et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout;	And if no pus comes out after the instrument is inserted, know that it is solid, so they should make a cross-shaped incision and take it out with pincers, and lightly scrape away at each side of the wound to draw out the skin where it lies, so that you draw it out healthy with the nail;
et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	and if you cannot draw it out whole, then draw it out in pieces so that nothing remains.
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois;	For if anything remains, it will return to us many times;
et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez;	and if a little remains and the pain afflicts you, then apply some corrosive powders to the wound, and press on the wound, and apply hot poultices for abscesses, and treat it with other remedies until it is healed;
et se li nous est grans, si cout les .ij. levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	and if the wound is large, then cut the two lips of the wound, and treat what is inside with ointment.
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc; puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	and if the vein beats against you or another, quickly apply ground vitriol and leave it for two or three days until the wound suppurates and the bleeding stops; then return to the cupping as before.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de .iij. manieres: grans et moien et petit; et s’en i a .iij. quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et .i. qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de .iij. manieres: grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule;	Here are the forms of the trocar, which come in three types: large, medium, and small; and there are three squares, called "albaret", and one called "breb", and they come in three sizes: large, medium, and small, for piercing abscesses of fistula.
et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule;	They are like needles used for piercing sorcerers, made of brass, iron, or silver, and the black-tipped ones are best for piercing the tunnels of fistula.
et sont de .iij. manieres: grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	They come in three sizes: large, medium, and small, depending on the size of the opening of the fistula.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci: grans, moiens, et petis; et si a oncines qui ont .ij. corbeures de .iij. manieres ausi;	The shapes of warts are of many kinds, as you can see here: large, medium, and small; and there are warts which have two curves in three ways also.
et si a oncines qui ont .iij. corbeures, et sont ausi de .iij. manieres; et si a oncines qui ont .ij. corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de .iij. manieres; et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	and there are warts with three curves, and they are also of three kinds; and there are warts with two curves, and warts with only one curve, and they are of three kinds; and all these are necessary in their place.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf;	The tips of these which are cut are sharp, and there are some which do not cut except from one side, so that we do not cut the vein or nerve;
et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes;	and these intrusions are the needles used in many ways, so that the patient does not hurt themselves while opening abscesses;
et sont de .iij. manieres: grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois;	and are of three kinds: large, small, and medium, as you can see;
et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus;	and we should not use them except in fleshy parts, such as legs, arms, breasts, and armpits, and similar places;
et aucune fois fait on .i. autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	and sometimes we make another small instrument, like slices of fisticuffs, according to this form, with which one stops the flow of blood;
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	and they put it sometimes in the place that heals by cutting the veins, and the arteries, and sometimes they mend according to this large form;
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme;	Sometimes men's nipples swell when they become corrupt, so that they resemble women's nipples.
et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne b. jusques a .g.:	and remain ugly and swollen; and if anyone wants to cure them, they should follow this procedure from line b to g.:
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee;	then scorch the fat, and apply medicine to the wound in layers, then stitch together the two lips of the wound, and let it heal.
et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en .ij. costelz desus, par .ij. semblans fendures;	and if the nipple sinks in and becomes soft due to its size, as it does in women, then cut it in two at the base, through two similar slits;
de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.;	wherein one is attached to the other at the end of both, so that the larger line contains the smaller according to this form, from this line .b. up to the line .g.
puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les .ij. levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez;	then scrape the skin between the two lips and remove the fat, and administer what we have said about stitching and powders, and what is necessary in the treatment, until it is healed;
et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif;	and if it is not healed, or the incision is not fully made, because the patient will not rest, or due to bleeding, then you should fill the wound with moist cotton in a corrosive ointment;
et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	and let it be until it absorbs the residue and fat, then treat it until it is healed.
des apostemes des asselles	of abscesses of the armpits
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	These abscesses that come from under the armpits are like hard scrofula, and some contain moisture.
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	So those that contain moisture should be cut according to this form, from line b. up to line g.:
Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when all the pus inside the abscess is drained, plug the wound with old cotton, and leave it until the next day. Then remove all the cotton and treat it with an appropriate ointment until it is healed.
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the abscesses are like scrofula, then treat them as we have said for fissures of scrofula, and if the wound is closed, then apply cautery as we have said before.
de la routure de l’artere	from the rupture of an artery
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme;	When an artery is ruptured and the skin above it is sewn up, many times abscesses will occur, as well as swelling in the vein and abscess.
et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont;	And if one knows it is from an artery, then the abscess will be long and deep.
et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens .i. estraignement; et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans;	and when you sense it with your fingers, you will feel .i. dislocation; and when it is in the vein, there is a visible displacement.
et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	and it is foolish to cover this abscess, especially when it is under the armpit and in the groin and neck and many other places, and it is large.
Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc;	Therefore, one should avoid the cure with iron, and in those who are bald, one should also avoid it, as well as in those with inflammation of the artery that makes a hole in the skin of the head.
puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte;	Then perform an incision with a scalpel, and carefully cut the artery away from the membranes, until it is fully exposed.
puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en .ij. leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des .ij. arteres qui sont en temples;	then put a needle underneath it and pierce it all the way to the other side, and constrict the artery with a double thread in two places, according to what I taught you in the extraction of the two arteries that are in the temples;
puis point le leu qui est entre les .ij. liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme;	then probe the place between the two ties with an introducer until the pus comes out and the abscess is drained;
puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient;	then administer the cure that makes the wound clean, until the thread comes out;
puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez;	then cure it with an appropriate ointment until it is healed;
et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir,	and if the abscess is at the base of the vein, you must grasp with your hand as much of the abscess as you can all over the skin,
puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait .i. fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit;	then insert the needle under the area you are holding in your hand and pierce it, and pass through .i. double thread so that you draw it from the other side;
puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de .ij. pars as .ij. chiés dou fil;	then ligature the abscess, as I told you, with either of the two parts of the thread;
et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout .i. fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en .iiij. leus;	and if you doubt that the thread will slip out, insert another needle through all of the thread under the abscess at the incision of the first needle, and tighten the threads in four places;
puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez;	then scrape off the abscess until the surplus comes out, then scrape off the surplus from the heart and leave what is attached.
puis met sus .i. drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	then put on a wet cloth soaked in wine and oil, then administer poultices and ointments until it is healed.
des apostemes des ners	abscesses of the nerves
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	Also, as abscesses come in the artery and vein, they also come to the nerves when they are hurt, or through excessive exertion, and similar things.
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est .i. grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor;	And this happens more often in the shoulders and elbows and everywhere where there are joints, and it is a painful abscess, and its color resembles the color of the body, and it has various dispositions without pain.
et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur;	And when it is pressed firmly, the patient feels pain, and it is not in a deep part of the body but under the skin.
et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer: par aventure i vanroit contraction;	And it is useless to bandage it tightly from all sides, and it neither goes forward nor backward, nor downward nor upward, and one who has a dislocation should not cover it with iron; otherwise, there might be contraction.
et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	And those who have it on the head or forehead, use the spathonile.
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine;	If the abscess is small, hold it with tongs and cut it at its root;
et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it is large, suspend it with a hook and lacerate it, then cut out the bone and sew up the wound, treating it until it is healed.
des grosses boces pendans	large boils hanging
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros; et en i a de petis et de mout grans;	Sometimes they occur in bellies and nowhere else, and it is a disease called "ringworm" because of its resemblance to oats, and its root is subtle, and the scabs are large; and there are both small and very large ones.
et je vis .i. home qui en avoit .ij. ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor.	and I saw .I. man who had .ii. or belly that were more like mushrooms than anything else, and there was no difference in them, and they were white, and had thin roots, and were split open, and moisture ran out of them.
Je les copai et trovai en l’un .xviij. onces pesant, et en l’autre .vj. З., et li ovraiges en l’incision si est que tu regardes se li malaides est moistes, et li color de l’artelul est blainche et moiste et de subtil racine;	I cut them and found one weighing .xviij. ounces and the other .vj. ounces, and their texture was such that if you look at the joint, the disease is moist, and the articular cartilage is white and moist with a fine root;
si le cope au spatumile large, et soient en ta presence li cautere au feu. Car au taillier vient maintes fois trop grans decorremens de sanc, et se li sans te vaint, si te haste donques dou cauterizer;	if the cut is wide, and there are large blood vessels in it, and if the blood flows out, then you must hasten with the cautery;
et se tu vois le malaide espoanteit et paourous de l’incision dou fer, si prent .i. fil de plonc bien fait, et en lie l’artelul si com nos avons dit, et le laisse .ij. jors;	and if you see the patient frightened and fearful of the incision from the iron, then take  .i. well-made thread, tie off the joint as we have said, and leave it for  .ij. days;
et puis le restraint, et ne cesser d’estraindre lou fil de plonc tant qu’il cope l’artelul, et chiece par lui sens travail; et se les racines sont grosses, si a paour au coper meismement por le ventre, mais tu em pues bien coper la moitiet,	and then restrain it, and do not cease to constrict the hair tightly until it slips the joint, and pull gently on it without effort; and if the roots are thick, then there is fear of slipping out the same way through the belly, but you can certainly grip half of it,
puis le cauterize qu’il ne reviegne; puis cure la plaie, et garde que tu ne coper le thelul qui est de fuxe color et de povre sens et de lait regart.	then cauterize it so that it does not return; then cure the wound, and beware of gripping the part which is of a red colour and poor sensation and milk-white appearance.
Car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, et je venrai a la cure de chancre ci aprés.	For this is an encrusted abscess, and I will come to the cure for cancers below.
quant li boude ist fuer	when the boil has burst
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit;	If the appearance of a hernia comes from cauterization of a wound or from a fissure in a syphilitic ulcer, and it is on the abdomen, and some of the intestines protrude out, as happens with other ruptures, or from blood that flows from veins or arteries according to what is mentioned earlier, or from wind.
et se c’est par la routure dou syfac et par l’issue dou bouel, si est li color de l’aposteme semblans a la color dou cors, et est legiere chose sens dolor, et apert de diverse issue.	And if it is from a rupture of the syphilitic ulcer and an opening in the intestines, then the color of the abscess will be similar to the color of the body, and there will be little pain and various openings.
Et se c’est por l’issue de l’intestine, adonques est il plus divers, et quant on le presse a ses dois si se repont, et puis revient, et par aventure si est sarrez, et agrandist mout a l’entree dou bain et por fort travail.	And if it is due to the protrusion of the intestines, then it will be very diverse; and when pressed with the fingers, it retracts, and then returns, and sometimes it is constricted, and it increases in size at the entrance to the bath due to intense exertion.
Et se c’est por moistor, c’est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie; et se c’est por sanc, si apert par ces signes li apostemes gros et dur, et est fichiez selonc une quantiteit;	And if it is due to moisture, then it is a minor issue and opens easily when pressed with the hand, without any constriction; but if it is due to blood, then there are signs of large and hard abscesses, and they are fixed according to a certain amount.
et se c’est por ventositeit, si est souef au tochier, et li ovraiges si est que tu regarde se li apparance est por le sanc de l’artere, ou de la voine, ou ventositeit.	And if it is due to flatulence, then it is swollen in the touch, and the work is that you look to see if the appearance is due to blood from the artery or vein, or flatulence.
Si covient que tu laisses la cure. Car il en a doutance et paor, si com je t’ai dit ou chapistre des apostemes, por l’artere et por la voine.	You should let it be cured. For there is doubt and fear, as I told you in the chapter on abscesses, due to the artery and vein.
Et se li apparance est por l’intestine ou lou boueil, si covient que tu comandes au malaide qu’il teigne son alaine, et soit estendus tout drois, puis seigne d’enche tout entor la boude;	And if the appearance is due to the intestine or bowels, then you should instruct the patient to tighten his belt and hold himself upright, then sign around the belly;
puis le comande a gesir sovin entre tes mains,	then command him to sit between your hands,
puis va entor le leu que tu as signiet a tout le spatumile,	then go around the area you have marked all around the ulcer
puis estent la moitiet de l’aposteme au desus a tout le grant uncine;	then cut the top of the abscess halfway down to the large hook;
puis le lie entor d’un fil fort, ou d’une corde de fort soie fermement, et soit li nous dou liien assolz;	then tie it tightly around with a strong thread or strong silk rope, and let the patient hold the end of the string;
puis oevre la moitiet de l’aposteme estendut sus le liien, et i boute ton doit indice, et quier l’intestine;	then cut the top of the abscess halfway down to the string, and push your index finger into it, and pull out the intestine;
se tu le trueves pris dou liien, si le deslie, et boute l’intestine au defuer dou ventre;	if you find it caught in the bowel, then free it and push the intestine back into the abdomen.
et se tu trueves le boueil, si le prent a l’oncine, et en cope la superfluiteit;	and if they find an obstruction, they grab it at the elbow, cut out the surplus;
et se li artere te fait contraire, ou li voine, si vai belement entor, puis revien a ton ovraige et pren .ij. aguilles, et i boute .ij. fors filz, et boute les .ij. aguilles entor ceu que tu as fait en crois que tu feis percier;	and if the artery makes a counter-clockwise turn, or the vein, then go around it, then return to your work and take two needles, and thread them with two strong threads, and then pierce through what you have done in a cross shape;
puis estrain l’aposteme en .iiij. leus sus les aguilles, et se tu vues, oste les aguilles, et laisse lou leu tant qu’il porrisse, et chiece li char morte par soi;	then pull the abscess out by four inches on the needles, and if you see, remove the needles, and leave it as long as possible, and the dead flesh will come out on its own;
ou tu la cope quant elle iert subtiliie et porrie, puis le cure de ceu qu’il covient, et cheve l’aposteme si com nos avons dit;	where you cup it when it is subtle and tender, then treat it as needed, and lance the abscess as we have said;
et estrai le sanc ou la moistor que tu trueves, puis cure le leu de ceu qu’il couvient, et soude le leu.	and extract the blood or moisture that you find, then treat the area as needed, and close the wound.
dou chancre	from which ulcer
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer; et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement; et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner; ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	We have described in the division of similarities of ulceration, and how one should work with medicines, and how one should avoid the cure of iron; and we speak of ulcer in the genitals, and great caution is required in its cure, and the ancients said that when ulcers are in places where they can be cut, such as ulcers in breasts, and in similar places, then all of it must be removed when it is in the beginning. And when it is large and old, one should not approach it at all, for I have never been able to heal any of them, nor has anyone ever healed them before me.
Et li ovraiges, quant il est en leu ou on le puet oster, si com nos avons dit, est que tu purge aucune fois le malaide de cole noire; puis le fai sainier s’il ait manifeste repletion, puis afaite le malaide .i. boin leu por faire l’ovraige; puis giete tes oncines ou chancre, et le cheve de toutes pars, et l’oste de toutes pars sens rien laissier; et laisse corre le sanc tout fuer, et espreint bien le leu a ta main ou a aucune chose, et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire de l’incision de l’artere ou de la voine, si le cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the work, when it is in a place where it can be removed, as we have said, is that you purge the patient of black bile sometimes; then make him bleed if he has manifest fullness; then open the wound .i. good place to do the work; then cut your oncines or cancer, and the head from all parts, and the bone from all parts without leaving anything; and let the blood flow out completely, and squeeze well the place with your hand or something, and if the bleeding makes you opposite to the incision of the artery or vein, cauterize it until the blood vessels are burned; then cure it with another cure until it is healed.
de ydropisie	of hydropsy
Nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’idropisie, et en queil maniere li assemblee de l’aigue est faite, et les signes de chescune semblance, et la cure qui est faite par medicines, et cele qui est curee par fer: si est eclites soulement; et ne doit on touchier de fer en ces .ij. semblances: c’est a savoir, tympanites et yposarche, car c’est mortelz chose; donques quant tu medicines ceste semblance de ydropisie qui est apelee «eclites» de medicines, et li cure ne profite, si regarde se li malaides est foibles, ou s’il ait autre maladie que ydropisie, si com toust et solution de ventre et semblans choses; si n’i touchier de fer, car il i a doutance; et se tu vois le malaide de fort vertut, et il n’a autre maladie que ydropisie soulement, et il n’est mie trop jones ne trop vielz, si dois ensi ovrer:	We have already spoken of the appearances of hydropsy, and in what manner the gathering of fluid occurs, and the signs of each appearance, and the cure which is made by medicine, and that which is cured by iron; so we will now speak only briefly. And you should not use iron in these two appearances: that is, tympanites and hyposarche, for these are deadly; therefore, when you treat this appearance of hydropsy called 'eclites' with medicine, and the cure does not help, if you see that the patient is weak or has another illness besides hydropsy, such as diarrhoea and similar conditions, then do not use iron, for there is doubt in these cases. But if you see the patient is strong and has only hydropsy, and is neither too young nor too old, then you should proceed thus:
lieve le malaide droit sus tes mains, et li ministres presse le ventre em boutant l’aigue a la plus basse partie dou pis, puis pren le spatumile espinous selonc ceste forme: Et soit trenchans de .ij. pars. a pointe, et toutevoie ne soit mie si entrans qu’il puist venir jusc’a l’intestine quant on le fiche ens, et ne le puist blecier;	Take the patient by the right hand, and the assistant presses his belly by pushing water to the lowest part of the foot. Then take the spathula with spines according to this shape: it should be pointed at both ends, yet not so sharp that it can pierce all the way to the intestine when inserted, nor can it cause bleeding.
puis regarde se li ydropisie est enjanree devers les intestines: si covient que tu fendes ensus de la boude .iij. dois droit desoz sus lou poignil; et se li ydropisie est por la maladie dou foie, si soit ta fendure au senestre de la boude .iij. dois; et se c’est por la miuce, si soit a destre, et ne covient mie que li malaides gise sus la fendure que les superfluitez ne corrent a celui foible leu;	Then examine if the dropsy is in the intestines: you should split under the navel on the right side for three fingers; and if the dropsy is due to liver disease, then the split should be on the left side for three fingers; and if it's due to spleen disease, then it should be on the right, and the patient must not lie on the split so that the fluids do not flow to that weak spot.
puis perce tout le cuir a l’estrument, et le boute, et lieve ta main a tout le spatumile entre le cuir et le syfac ausi com en escorchant a la quantiteit d’une ungle ou enqui entor; puis perce lou syfac tant que li spatumile viegne au leu vuit, et c’est li leus de l’aigue, puis le trai fuer, et i boute cest estrument de coi ci est li forme: Et est semblans a une caine d’argent subtil, et est d’arain ou d’archaut legier, et a en la partie desoz .i. petit pertus; et ou costeit d’une part, .iij. pertus; et .ij. d’autre part, et .i. d’autre; et est li chiés tailliez si com une penne, et c’est li forme de l’incision dont li escrivains taille la penne:	Then pierce the skin with the instrument and draw it out, and lift your hand as you insert the entire spathula between the skin and the syphon, just like when skinning an animal to the thickness of a fingernail or more; then pierce the syphon until the spathula reaches the desired location, which is where the water is, then pull it out and insert this instrument, from which comes the shape: It resembles a silver needle, made of copper or lightweight brass, and has a small hole on the lower part; and on one side there are three holes, two on one side, and one on the other, and the head is shaped like a feather, and this is the shape of the incision that scribes make to shape a pen:
au chief desus est li alemele, si que quant li estrumens vient a l’aigue, si dessent maintenant sus l’estrument; vuide la donques la moitiet ou la tierce part, car se tu en vuides plus qu’il ne covient en celle houre, par aventure si muert li malaides por la resolution de son esperit de l’arme, ou il chiet paumez, ou il aproche a la mort;	the head of the penis is the foreskin, so that when the instrument comes to water, it goes up onto the instrument; therefore empty half or a third, because if you empty more than you should in that hour, by chance the patient dies from the shock to his spirit from the weapon, or he falls limp, or he approaches death;
mais en vuide selonc la quantiteit de sa vertut, et selonc ceu que les dispositions de la vertut dou malaide signifient, et ses poulz; puis trai l’estrument et retien l’aigue, et elle est retenue maintenant por le keur qui estoupe le pertus qui est sus le syfac, de coi j’ai parleit, que tu perces selonc ceste maniere; puis rencomence l’estrument l’autre jor, se tu vois le malaide soffrant ceu, et trai de l’aigue une petite quantiteit;	but empty according to the amount of its virtue and according to what the dispositions of the virtue of the patient indicate, and his pulse; then remove the instrument and retain the water, which is now held by the membrane that blocks the opening that I have described, that you pierce in this manner; then use the instrument again the next day if you see the patient suffering from it, and draw off a small quantity of water;
fai ce aucun jor, et te garde de foloier tant qu’il ni demore mais c’un poc d’aigue. Et se tu doutes sus le malaide, et tu i lais mout d’aigue, si le cure de la sepulture ou sablon chaut, et par mout sueir ou bain et au soleil, et se teigne de boivre; et le cure de medicines desiccatives tant qu’il soit sanez, et cauterize sus l’estomac et sus lou foie et sus l’esplen aprés l’estraction de l’aigue, si com j’ai dit devant.	Do this each day, and be careful not to leave any water in him but a little; and if you doubt about the patient, and you leave a lot of water in him, then use the treatment of burial or hot sand, and sweating or bathing, and drinking tea, and the treatment of medicines that dry up his body until he is healed, and cauterize the stomach and liver and spleen after drawing off the water, as I said before.
de l’estopement de la verge	of the foreskin of the penis:
Aucune fois naissent enfant qui n’ont point de pertus en la verge, ou li pertus est petis, ou il n’est mie en son leu. Si le covient tantost qu’il n’aist percier a tout .i. spatumile molt subtil selonc ceste forme: puis met ou pertus .i. clo subtil de plonc, et le lie et le tien ensi .iij. jors ou iiij. et quant il vuet faire urine, si soit ostez li clos, et faice urine, et puis li remet; et par aventure nen i couvient point, car li urine qui vient fuer ne lou laisse close.	Sometimes children are born without an opening in their penis, or the opening is small, or it is not in its proper place. They should immediately have a very fine spatule inserted according to this form: then put into the opening a very thin plug of lead, and tie and hold it there for three or four days, and when they want to urinate, remove the plug and let them urinate, and then replace it; and perhaps they do not need it at all, because the urine that comes out will not allow the plug to stay in.
Cil de cui li pertus est petis, si est medicinez dou clo de plonc, si com nos avons dit, si s’eslargera. Cil qui n’ont mie le pertus en lor leu sont bleciet, car aucun naissent qui ont le pertus au chief de la verge, por coi il ne puient pissier avant s’il ne lievent lor verge en haut; et ne pueent enjanrer por ceu que li matiere ne puet venir jusc’a la marris, et c’est une male maladie.	Those with a small opening will be helped by the lead plug, as we have said, and it will widen. Those who do not have the opening in its proper place are afflicted, for some are born with the opening at the tip of the penis, so they cannot urinate until they lift their penis upwards; and they cannot copulate because the matter cannot reach the testicles, and this is a serious illness.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, puies estent le chief de la verge et le cope ausi com la taille d’une penne, si ke li pertus chiece em mileu, si com il covient; et te garde de decorrement de sanc qui i vient maintes fois, et s’il avient, si l’estainche de ceu qui estainche sanc, et cure la plaie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the way to treat it is for the patient to lie on his back, then the tip and shaft of the penis are made as hard as a feather, with the opening in the middle, as it should be; and beware of bleeding that often occurs, and if it does, stanch it with what stanches blood, and cure the wound until it is healed.
des pustules de la verge	of pimples on the penis
Maintes fois vienent cist albathe en la verge, et est une apparance de char laide; et en i a malignes et non malignes; si covient que tu les preignes a .i. oncine subtil, et les cope et munde toutes, puis met sus coton moilliet en oignement egiptien; puis le cure d’oignement diafinicon tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many times this albata occurs in the penis, and it is an ugly-looking swelling; there are both malignant and non-malignant ones; you should grab them with a pair of tweezers, pull them out carefully, then clean and dry them thoroughly, apply moistened cotton wool in Egyptian ointment, then treat the area with diaphenicon ointment until it heals.
Et se li albathe est maligne, de pute color et depuant, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere. Quant tu l’as copeit, et se li albathe est en som la verge, et en ait partie dedens la peil et partie defuer, si covient que tu oste l’albathe qui est dedens premier; et quant il est soudez, si le cure defuer. Car quant tu le cures ensamble, si n’est mie asseurez li chiez de la verge qu’il ne soit perciez, et vient noiror et corruption en son la verge et ou coion; si covient chever tout ceu qui est noir et corrumput, puis lie sus l’emplaustre de miel et de farine qui soit fait d’escorce de poumes grenates et de veces, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the albata is malignant, putrid-looking and foul-smelling, you should apply cautery to it. When you have pulled it out, and if the albata is on the surface of the penis, with part of it inside the skin and part outside, you should first remove the albata that is inside; and when it is healed, treat the external portion. For if you treat them both together, you cannot be sure that the glans of the penis will not be pierced, and blackness and corruption will come upon the penis and testicles; so you must cut away all that is black and rotten, then apply a poultice of honey and flour made from pomegranate rinds and rose petals, then treat it with further treatments until it heals.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si amenistre le cautere lunaire selonc ceste forme: Li cauteres si aide as .ij. dispositions ensamble: c’est asavoir, au decorrement de sanc, et a la corruption; et se li chiés de la verge est corrumpus et retrais, si covient que tu boutes ou conduit de la verge une cainne de plonc, et pisse li malaides parmi; et quant li pelz iert aerse au chief de la verge qui avient a ces qui n’ont mie esteit circoncis, ou il avient por plaie ou por aposteme, si covient donques que tu l’escorches a .i. estrument cheveit, tant que li liiens soit desliiez, et soit delivrez li chiez de la verge de toutes pars;	And if there is bleeding, you should apply the lunar cautery in the following way: Cauteries have two purposes: for bleeding and for corruption; and when the glans of the penis are withered and shrivelled, you should insert a tube into the penis and let the patient urinate through it. And when the skin at the tip of the penis becomes raw, either due to a wound or an abscess, you must circumcise it with a sharp instrument so that the foreskin is completely removed and the glans of the penis is freed from all sides.
et se c’est grief chose de deviser ceu, si covient que tu l’escorches a .i. spatumile aucun poc dou chief de la verge et de la peil; puis dessevre belement entre .ij., et i met .i. subtil drapeil de lin moilliet an aigue froide, qu’il n’aerse derechief.	and if it is painful to urinate, you must incision with a spatulum at the tip of the penis and scrotum; then withdraw quickly between two incisions, and place a thin piece of wet linen in cold water so that it does not dry out again.
de la circoncision	of circumcision
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies; toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	Circumcision is not like other wounds in terms of healing; however, when we perform this procedure intentionally, especially on infants, it is necessary to do it properly and gently for their well-being.
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il n’en usent mie en lor loi, et n’en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	I say that the ancient authors did not describe the circumcision of their children because they did not practice it in their law, and we only have what we have acquired through experimentation.
Car j’ai veut la plus grant partie des maistres et des sainors qui faisoient circumcision entor .i. dal, et as forces, et a tout une novacule; si fuioit li keurs car il i a .ij. toiles, et par aventure si cope on celi desus et demore celle desoz.	Because I have seen most of the masters and surgeons who performed circumcision all around the glans, and in some cases even cut off the foreskin entirely; this caused the skin to dry out and form a scar, as there were two membranes, and sometimes the upper one was removed while the lower one remained.
Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal n’est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre; et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut.	Then they cover it again, and the pain is doubled, and with the washing of the glans, which is not healed at the tip of the member; and in washing the nail, sometimes the instrument slips, and they injure the work, and many times they grow back so that they don't need to be washed, and I have seen this.
De la mondification qui est faite as forces a tout le liien de fil ai je troveit la bonteit de l’experiment, car les forces taillent justement ausi bien desus com desoz.	Of the washing that is done around the glans, I have found the goodness of the experiment, for the forces cut accurately both above and below.
Car quant tu presses ta main, si tailles igalment en .i. tout soul tens; mais que li filz soit bien estrois entor lou cuir; et soit li maniere dou premier ovraige si est que tu faices penser l’enfant, s’il entent, que tu ne li fais fuer que liier le fil entor la verge tant soulement, et pues le fai esjoir en toutes les manieres que tu pues;	Because when you press your hand, it cuts evenly all around; but the thread must be well stretched against the skin; and the method of the first operation is that you should make the child think, if he is conscious, that you are only tying the thread around his penis, and then you should make him urinate in all the ways you can.
puis le fai ester entre tes mains tout droit, et repont les forces entre tes mains ou desoz tes piez que li enfes ne les voie, ne aucun des estrumens; puis boute ta main a la verge et souffle ou keur, et la trai en haut tant que li chiés de la verge soit ens; puis la mundifie bien de l’ordure qui i est assemblee, puis lie le leu signiet d’un fil double, puis la lie desoz .i. poc a .i. autre liien; et la tien as .ij. dois par la seconde lieeure au pouchet et au doit indice, et cope entre les .ij. liiens, puis lieve le keur desus hastanment et trai le chief de la verge;	then let him hold it upright between his hands, and press the forces between his hands or under his feet so that the child does not see them, nor any of the instruments; then put your hand to the penis and breathe or sniff, and pull it upwards until the head of the penis is inside; then cleanse it well from the dirt that has gathered there, then tie the place with a double thread, then tie it under with another ligature; and hold it with two fingers by the second ligature at the foreskin and index finger, and press between the two ligatures, then lift the glans quickly and pull the head of the penis;
puis laisse corre le sanc poc et poc, car c’est li muedres; et met poudre sus et sus la poudre .i. drapeil glueit d’un moieuf d’uef cuit destempreit d’aigue rose, confit avec oile roset boin et fres, et lou laisse sus jusc’a l’autre jor, et le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	then let the blood flow little by little, for that is the wound; and put powder on top, and on top of the powder a glue-soaked cloth made from a cooked egg yolk tempered with rose water, cooked with good and fresh rosemary oil, and leave it until the next day, and treat it again until it is healed.
Li forme des forces a la mundification si est ceste: li dui chiés soient tenves et soient trenchans, et soient li chiés ausi grant com li mainche igalment:	The shape of the forceps for cleansing should be as follows: the two heads should be thin and sharp, and the handles should be as wide as the palm of the hand equally.
li error de la mundification si est quant li keurs dedens fuit a l’incision; donques il covient que tu l’estendes a ton ungle, ainsois que li leus faice aposteme; et le cope igalment, et se tu ne lou pues tenir a ton ungle, si le tien as tenailles, et puis le cope.	The mistake in cleansing is when the glans slips inside during incising; therefore, you must stretch it with your nail so that the glans makes an abscess; then, press equally and if you cannot hold it with your nail, hold it with tweezers, then press.
Et s’il trespassent .iij. jors, et ceu qui est desoz la verge est enflez, si le laisse tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et l’escorche legierement; si le cope si com tu pues mues, et te garde de la partie de la verge, ce ne li nuira niant.	And if it persists for 3 days, and that which is under the foreskin is swollen, let it be until the hot abscess is soothed and the skin is lightly scratched; then copulate as much as you can, being careful not to touch the foreskin, this will do him no harm.
Cure donques le leu de choses soudans plaie de poudre, que nos avons dit ou traitier des poudres, et s’on cope dou keur outre mesure, et il va au desus, si ne nuira point; cure le donques, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Treat therefore the area of sudden wounds with powder, as we have said in the treatise on powders, and if he copulates beyond measure, and it goes above, it will do no harm; treat it therefore, as we have said, until it is healed.
dou retenement de l’urine	from the retention of urine
Li retenue de l’urine si est d’opilation de piere, ou de sanc congeleit, ou de bowe, ou de char nee, ou de semblans choses, que nos avons dit en la division;	The retention of urine is from the stone, or frozen blood, or bowel, or birth defect, or similar things, which we have discussed in the division;
et se li urine n’est desliie, et tu vois estre la retenue por la piere qui est jai ou col de la vessie, si covient que li malaides soit corbés sus ses genoulz; et li soient mis li piez sor le dos, et estende son ventre de la partie desus lou dos, et restraigne li malaides s’alainne tant com il puet; et adonques est constrains li colz de la vessie a l’expression de la piere au desus, por coi li urine est desliie e;	and if the urine is not released, and you see it being held back by the stone which is lodged in the neck of the bladder, then the patient should bend forward over his knees; and his feet should be placed on his back, and he should expand his belly from above his back, and restrain himself as much as he can; and then the neck of the bladder is forced to expel the stone upwards, causing the urine to flow.
