et s’elle ne vient, si com nos avons dit, et li malaides sent grant dolor, si covient que tu i aministres extraction a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «siringue», de coi ci est li forme: et soit d’argent subtilz legiere chevee, si com li penne d’un oiseil; et soit li caine d’une palme de lonc et demie, et soit subtilz au chief.	and if it does not come out as we have said, and the patient feels great pain, then you must administer extraction using an instrument called a 'syringe'. This is its form: it should be made of thin silver, like the shaft of an arrow; the tube should be about a palm and a half long, and thin at the tip.
Et li maniere de l’issue de l’urine si est que tu pren .i. fil double, et lie au chief .i. poc de laine ou de couton, et boute le chief dou fil dedens la siringue; et cope la superfluiteit de la lainne et le boute jusc’au chief de la siringue, puis oint la siringue d’oile ou de burre et d’aubin d’uef, et fai seoir le malaide sus .i. siege, et li arose la vessie et la verge d’oile moiste et d’oile d’olive et d’aigue tede;	And the method of removing the urine is as follows: take a double thread and tie a small ball of wool or cotton at the tip; then push the tip of the thread into the syringe, and twist the excess wool so that it fits snugly against the tip of the syringe. Next, grease the syringe with oil or butter and egg yolk, and have the patient sit on a chair, and lubricate the bladder and penis with warm oil or olive oil and egg yolk;
puis met legierement la siringue en la verge, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la verge, puis double la verge desus devers la boude; puis boute la siringue avant jusc’a la vessie, et la sente li malaides venir jusc’a la chose vuide, et ceu n’est mie fait selonc cest ordre fuer que por ceu que li conduis ou elle vait est tors; puis estent le fil a tout la laine poc et poc, et li urine en suit la laine, puis l’estrai fuer, et fai corre l’urine;	then gently insert the syringe into the penis, until it reaches the root of the penis, and then bend the penis upwards towards the belly; then push the syringe forward into the bladder, and the patient will feel it enter the bladder, and this is not done correctly if it hurts; then pull the thread and the wool ball out, and the urine will follow the wool, then remove the syringe, and have the patient urinate;
et rencomence la siringue tant que li vessie soit vuidie, et soit aligiez li malaides.	and restart the syringe until the bladder is emptied and the patient is relieved.
des maladies de la vessie	of diseases of the bladder
Quant escorcheures ou sanc vient en la vessie, ou porriture i est assemblee, et tu i vues distiller aigues et medicines, si fai a tout l’estrument qui est apellé «clepsedre», et c’est li forme:	When scabs or blood come in the bladder, or pus is accumulated there, and you see water and medicine dripping from it, then do this with all the apparatus that is called a "clepsydra", and this is how:
Elle est close, et si a .iij. pertus: .ij. d’une part, et .i. d’autre, si com tu vois; et li leus chevez par coi li medicine cort soit telz qu’il estoupe bien la verge sens adition, si c’on em puisse traire la moistor, et bouter quant mestier est;	It is closed and has three openings: two on one side and one on the other, as you see; and the leather tube through which the medicine flows should be such that it blocks the shaft without addition, so that one can draw out moisture and push when needed;
et quant tu vues giter tes medicines en la vessie, met le chief dou keusteur en la moistor, et trai au traiant qui est ens; si trairas la moistor au kesteur, et puis reboute fort le traiant ens; si entrera li moistors ens, et venra a la vessie maintenant, si que li malaides la sentira;	and when you see your medicine flowing into the bladder, put the tip of the syringe into the moisture, and suck in the liquid that is there; then release it strongly into the syringe, and the moisture will enter the syringe, and go to the bladder immediately, so that the patient feels it;
et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil dont on clisterize la vessie: si est ci:	and this is the form of the subtle enema with which one enemas the bladder: here it is:
Et est d’argent ou d’archaut, et est li chiés plus haut; et desoz a .i. sein ou li liiens chiet; puis pren une vessie de mouton et i met la moistor dont tu vues clisterizer la vessie, puis la lie entre les .ij. seins forment d’un boin fil double, et chaufe .i. poc celle moistor sus le feu; puis boute le chief dou clistere en la verge, puis estrain ta main sus la vessie a tout la moistor avenanment, tant que li malaides sente que celle moistor est jai venue a la vessie;	And it is made of silver or brass, and the head is higher up; and below are .i. string or the strings hang; then take a sheep's bladder and put in it the moisture with which you want to enema the bladder; then tie the moisture between the .ij. strings formed by a thin double thread, and heat .i. pocket that moisture over the fire; then insert the head of the enema into the penis, then pull your hand on the bladder so that all the moisture comes gently in, until the patient feels that the moisture has reached the bladder.
et se tu n’as la vessie, si pren une piece de parchemin, et en fai .i. cercle, et le perce rondement entor; puis boute .i. fil fort en ces pertus, puis assemble le cercle si com on assemble .i. dal, et met dedens ceu que tu vues d’oile et de moistor et d’aigue, et le lie en l’estrument; et fai si com tu as fait de la vessie, de presser a ta main tant que li moistor veigne a la vessie.	and if you don't have a bladder, take a piece of parchment and make  .i a round circle, and pierce it all around; then insert a strong thread through these holes, then assemble the circle like you would assemble a dal, and put inside what you want to oil and moisture and water, and attach it to the instrument; and do as you did with the bladder, by pressing your hand until the moisture reaches the bladder.
de la piere	of stone
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines; et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille; et en la vessie, et en la verge; et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	We have already discussed in the division the ways of stone, and its extraction along with medicines; and I have described the difference between a stone lodged in the bladder, and all the signs, and in which type of stone one should operate: in the bladder, and in the penis; and I will tell you plainly and briefly.
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit; et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist; et a mout de ces saut li fondemens; et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont .iiij. ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece; et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	I say that the stone which is lodged in the bladder occurs most often in children, and it is a sign that the water flows from the bladder, resembling water in its subtlety; and it causes pain to the patient, and he grasps his penis, and can urinate many times, and then it blocks; and many of these cause the foundation [of the body]; and healing is easier for children until they are 4 years old, and it is much more serious in the elderly, and it is midway between youth and old age; and the cure is generally easier for those who have larger stones than for those with smaller ones.
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines. Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	And when we come to the treatment, it is first necessary to cleanse the patient with an enema to draw out any feces that may be blocking the intestines. For sometimes this can obstruct the extraction of the stone.
Puis prenez le malaide par les piez, et lou deboutez et movez au desoz, si que li piere dessende au parfont de la vessie, et saille aucune fois dou leu haut; puis le fai seoir entre tes mains appareilliet, et ses mains soient desoz ses cuisses, si que li vessie soit toute declinans aval; puis la quier et la touche ded ens;	Take the patient by the feet, and raise him up and move him about so that the stone descends to the bottom of the bladder, and sometimes it rises from its place higher up; then make him sit between your hands, and have his hands under his thighs so that the bladder is completely tilted downward; then examine and touch it inside.
se tu sens la piere en l’espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere. Et s’elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice d’oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis; et le boute en son fondement, et quier la piere, et quant tu la sens a ton doi, si l’amoine au col de la vessie; puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier.	If you feel the stone in its place, then you should cut into the stone right away. And if it does not slip out with the touch all at once, then wet your index finger of your left hand with oil, if the patient is a young man, or your middle finger if the patient is older; and insert it into its opening, and examine the stone, and when you feel it with your finger, pull it toward the neck of the bladder; then press on it with your finger, and push it out to where you want to cut.
Et comande au ministre qu’il presse la vessie a sa main, et li comande qu’il estende a sa main destre les coions en haut, et a sa main senestre oste le cuir qui est desoz les coions en la partie ou on fait la taille; puis i boute le spatumile copant, de coi ce est li forme:	And instruct the minister to press on the bladder with his hand, and tell him to lift up the testicles with his right hand, and with his left hand pull back the skin underneath the testicles in the area where the incision is made; then insert the spatulum firmly, following its natural curve.Et s’il sent la piere a son doi indice ou moien, si quier la piere avec li spatumile et li boutons dedens, et quant il la sens, si l’amoine vers le col de la vessie;
Et fent entre ceu qui est entre les coions et le fondement, ne mie em mileu mais au costeit de la naige senestre; et soit drois sus la piere, et tes dois soit adés ou fondement, et soit li taille dou traver si qu’ele soit large par defuer, et dedens estroite, selonc la quantiteit de la piere, ne mie trop grans;	And they cut between what is between the testicles and the anus, not in the middle but on the left side of the navel; and it should be straight on the stone, and both fingers should be on the anus, and the incision should be diagonal so that it is wide at the top and narrow inside, according to the size of the stone, not too large.
par aventure la presse si li dois qui est ou fondement, qu’elle saut fuer sens travail; et saiches qu’il i a teil piere ou il a angles, et marges: si est griés a issir; et si a teil qui est souez, semblans a une glant, et reonde, dont li issue est legiere.	By chance, the pressure from the fingers on the anus will cause it to slip out without effort; and you should know that there is such a stone in which there are angles and edges: it is easy to extract; and there is another type that is underneath, similar to a grape, and round, from which extraction is difficult.
A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant; et s’elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si qu’elle n’eschaipe; ou tu boute desoz li .i. estrument subtil corbé au chief; et se tu ne la pues engignier ensi, si eslarge .i. poc lou pertus, et se li sans decort, si l’estrainche de vitriole;	For one with angles and edges, make the incision larger; and if it does not slip out, you should use tweezers that are like a file at the end to extract the stone so that it does not escape; or you put under it a very thin instrument curved at the end; and if you cannot grab it in this way, then widen the opening a little and pour vinegar underneath;
et s’il i a plus d’une piere, si boute premier la plus grant au col de la vessie, puis cope sus, puis le trai fuer, et les petites aprés s’il en i a plusors. Et s’elle est mout grans, si la covient soier, et faire plus grant plaie. Car .ij. choses avienent au malaide: ou il muert, ou li urine vient adés par lai que li leus ne puet souder; mais toutevoie t’efforce dou traire, ou dou debrisier as tenailles, tant que tu la traies par pieces;	and if there is more than one stone, then first remove the largest one at the neck of the bladder, then cut it off, then pull it out, and the smaller ones afterwards. And if it is very large, then it must be broken up, and a larger incision made. For two things can happen to the patient: they may die, or the urine will come out through the gap where the foreskin cannot heal; but nevertheless, try to pull it, or break it up with tweezers, until you extract it in pieces;
et quant tu as acomplit ton oevre, si emple la plaie d’encens et d’aloe et de sanc de dragon, et l’estraint, et met par sus .i. drapeil moilliet en oile et en vin, ou en oile et en aigue rose et aigue froide, por apaisier l’aposteme chaut; puis resovine le malaide sus son col, et ne desliier lou lien jusc’au tier jor.	and when you have finished your work, then dress the wound with incense and aloe and dragon's blood, and bind it up, and place over it a damp cloth anointed with oil and wine, or with oil and rosewater and cold water, to soothe the hot abscess; then reapply the bandage around his neck, and do not loosen the ligature until the third day.
Et quant tu le desliies, si arose mout bien lou leu d’oile et d’aigue, puis le cure d’oignement dyafinicon et d’oignement basilicon, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you loosen it, then wash the site well with oil and water, then treat the wound with thin ointment and thick ointment until it is healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient en la plaie et corrosions, et congelemens de sanc en la vessie, et soit par ceu retenue li urine, qui est conue en teil maniere que sans saut avec l’urine: boutes donques ton doi en la plaie, et estrai celui sanc, car s’il i remaint, si corront la vessie, et la porrit;	And if hot abscesses and scorchings and blood congealings come in the wound and the bladder is blocked by this, which is known in such a way that it passes without urine: therefore insert your finger into the wound and extract that blood, for if it remains, it will corrupt the bladder and burst;
puis leve la plaie d’aigue et d’aisil et de seil, et li aide en toutes les manieres que tu seis, tant qu’il soit sanez; et covient que toutes les oures que tu le cures, que tu li lie les .ij. cuisses, et assemble les medicines sus le leu.	then lift the wound with water and vinegar and salt, and assist him in every way you know how, until it is healed; and it is necessary that every hour when you treat him, to tie his two thighs together and bring the remedies over the site.
Et se li piere est petite, et ele est ou conduit de la verge, et fichie ens, et li urine ne puet issir; si le cure de ceu que je dis ainsois, que tu lou tailles maintes fois, est on escusez de la taille per ceste cure. Je ai ja ce proveit ensi.	And if the stone is small and lodged in the passage of the penis, and fixed there, and the urine cannot pass; then the treatment of what I have said should be done repeatedly, that you should cut it many times, this is an excuse for cutting according to this treatment. I have already proven this.
Pren .i. foret de fer selonc ceste forme et soit a .iij. angles fichiees en .i. tison:	Take an iron rod according to this form and let it be filed into three angles:
puis pren .i. fil et lou lie entor la verge desoz la piere, si qu’ele ne puist venir arrier en la vessie; puis boute le foret en la verge legierement, tant qu’il viegne a la piere; et torne le foret a ta main en la piere poc et poc, tant que tu puisses percier la piere d’autre part; si venra tantost li urine, puis presse ta main sus ceu qui est demorez de la piere qui est dedens la verge. Si est tantost brisie, et saut fuer avec l’urine, et est garis li malaides;	Then take a wire and tie it around the penis below the stone so that it cannot go back into the bladder; then insert the rod gently into the penis until it reaches the stone; and turn the rod in your hand within the stone little by little, until you can pierce the stone from another side; then the urine will come out at once, then press your hand on what is left of the stone which is inside the penis. Then it is immediately broken, and comes out with the urine, and the patient is healed;
et se tu ne pues ce faire por aucune chose qui le deffent, si lie .i. fil desoz la piere et .i. autre desus, puis fent la verge endroit la piere entre les .ij. liiens, puis l’estrai fuer, et deslie lou liien, et mundifie lou sanc congeleit qui est en la plaie; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if you cannot do this because of any obstruction, then tie a wire underneath the stone and another one above it, then make an incision in the penis at the site of the stone between the two wires, then pull it out, and untie the wires, and cleanse the congealed blood that is in the wound; and treat it until it heals.
de la piere des femmes	of the stones of women
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por .iij. choses: l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge; et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	Sometimes stones form in women, and if they do, the cure is difficult, and it is prohibited for three reasons: one is that perhaps the woman is a virgin; and the second is that one cannot find a skilled woman who reveals herself to midwives, especially when she is chaste.
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains; et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a.	And the third reason is that one cannot find a skilled woman in this art of medicine; and the fourth reason is that the stone in a woman is often deeper than in a man, so a deeper incision is required, and there is great fear involved.
Et se necessitez semont a ceu, si covient que tu preignes une mieresse bien sachant, et a poines la trueve on, et se tu n’en trueves, point si quier .i. caste mire subtil; et li presente une baile bien saige en la vie des femmes, ou une femme qui saiche une partie de l’art, et li comande qu’ele faice ceu que tu li comandes de l’inquisicion de la piere;	And if you see this is necessary, then you should press a midwife who is well-skilled, and with great difficulty she may find it, and if she doesn't, then you must not hesitate to call upon a cunning woman who is wise in the ways of women, or a woman who knows a part of the art, and command her to do what you command regarding the inquiry into the stone.
et regarde mout bien se li femme est vierge: adonques li covient bouter son doit ou fondement et querir la piere; et s’ele la trueve, si la constraigne desoz son doit, et li recomande qu’elle boute son doit ou con la malaide, et quiere et presse sa main senestre sus la vessie forment.	and look very carefully to see if the woman is a virgin: then she should press her thumb into her vagina and search for the stone; and if she finds it, she should hold it under her thumb and recommend that she presses her thumb into her vagina with the pain, and press her left hand firmly over her bladder.
S’elle la trueve, si covient qu’elle la mueve de greit en greit des l’entree de la vessie jusque desoz, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la cuisse; puis cope sus la piere en la racine de la cuisse encontre le mileu dou con, lai ou il est mues apparilliet, et sent la piere en celle partie; et ne mueve son doi desus la piere ou desoz, et soit li taille au premier petite;	If she finds it, then she should move the stone gradually from the entrance of the bladder until it reaches the root of the thigh; then press on the stone at the root of the thigh against the middle of the urethra, where it is most sensitive, and feel for the stone in that area; and do not move her thumb over or under the stone, and let the incision be small at first;
puis boute lou rait en la taille, se tu sens la piere si acroi la plaie tant que li piere puisse issir fuer, et saiches que maintes manieres de pieres sont: c’est a savoir, petites et grans et aspres et souez, longes et reondes, et qui ont rains. si saiches les semblances por savoir l’issue.	then insert the probe into the incision, if you feel the stone is sharp enough to cut through the tissue so that the stone can come out, and know that there are many types of stones: some are small and smooth, others are large and rough, long, and rounded, and have various shapes. Know their likenesses in order to identify them.
Et se li sans te vaint, si met au leu vitriole broiet, et li tien une houre tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer, et aies des estrumens que je t’ai dit en l’estraction de la piere as homes por toi aidier en ton oevre;	And if the blood is slow to come out, put in a little powdered vitriol and hold it there for an hour until the bleeding stops; then return to your task and remove the stone, and have the instruments that I told you about before to help you with the extraction of the stone from men.
et se li sans te vaint, et c’est de l’artere qui est copee, si met la poudre sus le leu et l’estrain de tentes et de bendelz, et ne rencomencier plus ceu, et laisse la piere et ne la traire mie, que par aventure morroit li malaide; puis cure la plaie.	And if the blood flows and it is from an artery that has been cut, then apply powder to the site, and constrict with bandages and a tourniquet, and no more compression, and leave the stone alone and do not try to remove it, for fear the patient might die; then treat the wound.
Et quant li chalor dou sanc est apaisie, et li leus porrist, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer.	And when the heat of the blood has subsided and the site has healed, return to your work until the stone is removed.
de hernie carnouse	of fleshy hernia
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef; et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit .i. autre oef; et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit; et ceu n’avient se poc non.	Aquous fluid is nothing else but an assembly of moisture or white pus, which is beneath the heart of the testicles, containing the egg; and is called "pus", and sometimes it is properly in the membrane of the egg, if one thinks that it is another egg; and that is the skin of the testicle between the white pus that we have mentioned. And this does not happen rarely.
Et li generation de cest ramice si est de foibleteit que vient as coions, et est espandue celle matiere.	And the generation of this disease is due to weakness that comes to the testicles, and that matter is spread out.
Et aucune fois si vient de percussion sus les coions, et ceste moistor si a maintes colors: ou c’est color declinans a jaunice, ou c’est sans rouge, ou noir, ou aquous blans, et ce avient plus;	And sometimes it comes from a blow to the testicles, and this moisture has many colors; sometimes it is a yellowish hue, sometimes red, sometimes black, sometimes watery white, and it happens in other ways as well.
et ce sont li signe de conoistre ceste assemblee, car s’elle est ou blanc syfac que nos avons dit, si est li apostemes reons, .i. poc lonc si com li figure d’un oef, et n’apert mie li coions, car il a moistor tout entor.	and these are the signs to recognize this condition, for if it is in the white scrotum that we have described, then there are red spots, like a rose, and it does not open the testicles, for there is moisture all around it.
Et s’il a moistor en la propre toile, si est li apostemes reons avec une partie de l’uef, et por ceu pense on que c’est uns autres oef;	And if there is moisture in the scrotum itself, then there are red spots with part of an egg, and because of this, one thinks it is another kind of egg;
et se li moistor est entre le cuir des coions et le blanc syfac, si le sent om bien; donques quant tu vues savoir la color de la moistor, si esprueve a tout l’intromissoire quarreit, de coi li forme est ci devant.	and if the moisture is between the skin of the scrotum and the white testicle, he feels it well; therefore when you want to know the color of the moisture, test all over the entrance, from which the shape is as mentioned before.
Selonc ceu donques qui vient aprés l’intromissoire, juge de ceu qui est dedens.	According to this then, what comes after the entrance, judge what is inside.
Et quant nos la curons par fer, si covient que li malaides soit sainiez selonc som pooir et la repletion de son cors; puis le sovine sus son dos, sus une chose un poc haute, et met desoz lui mout de drapelz;	And when we treat it with iron, the patient should be healed according to his strength and the fullness of his body; then he should lie on his back, on something slightly raised, and have a lot of coverings under him;
puis sié sus sa senestre, et comande au ministre qu’il sié a destre, et estende la verge a l’un des .ij. costelz dou keur des coions;	then sit on his left side, and instruct the assistant to sit on his right, and extend the rod to one of the two sides of the heart of the scrotum;
puis pren le spatumile leit, et cope le cuir des coions parmi leu dou lonc jusque delez lou poignil, et soit ta fendure toute droite en devisant le cuir des coions jusc’a syfac blanc, et l’escorche subtilment selonc tom pooir;	Take the spatulum of lead, and cut the skin of the scrotum from its tip to the base, making an incision straight down to the white membrane, and then carefully scrape off the skin according to your ability.
puis perce lou syfac plain d’aigue a .i. large pertus, et estrai toute l’aigue, et puis met tes oncines, et estent lou syfac amont; et ne touchier le keur des coions, mais que le syfac soulement; cope tout ou par pieces meismement le costeit de lui subtil, que se tu ne le copes bien saigement, si revenra li aigue;	Then pierce the testicle with a large needle and draw out all the water, then insert your fingers and bring up the testicle; do not touch the skin of the scrotum but only the testicle itself. Carefully cut around its edge in sections, being careful to avoid bleeding too much, otherwise the water will return.
et se l’uef saut fuer a ton oevre, si le ramoinne en son leu quant tu avras acomplit l’uevre dou syfac; puis assemble les .ij. leivres dou keur des coions a une costure, puis le cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the testicle slips out during your work, return it to its place when you have finished working on the testicle; then sew together the two lips of the skin of the scrotum with a single stitch and treat it as you would any other wound until it is healed.
Et se tu trueves l’uef corromput d’autre maladie, si covient que tu lies les vasselz que sont suspensoire, en doutant le decorrement de sanc; puis cope le coion a tout le suspensoire, et estrai l’uef, et le cure si com nos avons dit.	And if you find that the testicle is corrupted by another disease, then you must ligate the vessels which are suspended, fearing a rupture of blood; then cut the scrotum all around the suspension, extract the testicle and treat it as we have said.
Et se aigue est assemblee en .ij. parties ensamble, saiches que ce sont .ij. ramices; si cope l’autre partie si com tu as fait la premiere igalment, puis essue lou sanc, et met en la plaie lainne moillie en oile roset;	And if water is collected in two parts together, know that they are two branches; then cup the other part just as you did the first, likewise, wipe away the blood and put soft linen moistened with rose oil into the wound.
et met defuer autre laine moillie en vin et en oile, et met sus les .ij. coions, et met desus drapelz doublés, et le lie sus a tout le liien qui est selonc ceste forme:	And put another piece of soft linen moistened with wine and oil on top, and place the two branches on it, and put doubled sheets on top, and tie it all along according to this form:
Puis pren .ij. drapelz, et les emple de laine charpie selonc ceste semblance et soient assemblez par cousture en la gorle des braies, et li uns des chiés preigne sus le fondement jusc’au dos, et li autres a la partie dou poignil; et li autre dui chief sus les .ij. angres, et soit toute assemblee li restreinture en la boucle dou braier;	Then take two sheets and fill them with wadded linen according to this shape and sew them together at the crotch of the breeches, and one end press against the buttock up to the back, and the other to the groins, and the other two ends on the two armpits, and tie all the fastening in the loop of the breeches.
et aucune fois est medicinee ceste ramice de cautere en leu de taille de fer, et est que tu preignes .i. cautere cultellaire subtil, et cope le cuir des coions, et soit eschaufez si com nos avons dit, si que li syfac blanc que contient l’aigue est descovers;	And sometimes this branch of cautery is used instead of an iron knife, and it is that you press a thin cautery knife against the skin of the branches, and it is heated as we have said, so that the white puss containing the water is uncovered;
si pren lou cautere selonc ceste forme, et perce celui syfac as oncines, et l’escorche a cest subtil cautere chaut:	take the cautery according to this form, and pierce the ulcer at the base of the fingernail, and scorch it with this delicate hot cautery.
Et lou cope en toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que tu esraiches tout; et garde que li feus ne touche l’uef; et saiches que ceste oevre est plus salve; et mues gardans de decorrement de sanc, et muedres que li ovraiges de taille;	And the scrotum in every way you can, until you pull it all out; and be careful that the fire does not touch the nail; and know that this operation is safer; and watch for blood loss, and damage from cutting operations.
et se nulle chose te fait contraire, ou aposteme chaus ou decorremens de sanc ou autre chose, si cure ce qui te fait contraire, selonc ceu qui est devant dit.	And if nothing makes you contrary, or hot abscesses or blood loss or anything else, then cure what makes you contrary, according to what is said before.
Et se li malaides est paourous, et ne vuet atendre cest ovraige por son horribleteit, si amenistre perforation, si com je te di, et est que quant tu es bien certains par les significations que nos avons dit que ramice aquouse est lai,	And if the patient is fearful and does not want to undergo this operation due to its horror, then administer a perforation, as I have told you, and when you are certain through the signs we have discussed that the pus is laid out,
si fai seoir le malaide sus .i. siege leveit; puis perce l’aposteme an la partie desoz a tout le spatumile large, et met la perforation dou lonc dou cors; et soit larges li pertus, si que toute li aigue corre fuer;	let the patient sit on a high seat; then pierce the abscess at its base to the full depth of the spathum, and make an opening in the long bone; and let the holes be large so that all the pus may flow out;
puis met coton sus le leu, et le lie, et laisse por corre le remenant de l’aigue, puis le cure tant que li plaie soit sanee;	then put cotton on the spot and bandage it, and let it be so that the remaining pus may flow out, then treat the wound until it is healed;
et se li blainche toile ne laisse issir l’aigue en la bouche de la plaie, si covient que tu i boutes une penne ou l’estrument dont on trait l’aigue des ydropiques, de coi li forme est ci devant; et eslarge .i. poc la plaie, et saiches que li aigue revient, et est assemblee aprés .vj. mois ou enqui entor, et quant elle est assemblee si com devant, et ensi passera li malaides ses jors.	and if the white thread does not let the pus flow out through the mouth of the wound, then you must put in it a feather or instrument used to treat the sick, as described earlier; and enlarge the wound a little, and know that the pus will return and be accumulated after six months or so, and when it is accumulated as before, and thus the patient will pass their days.
de l’aposteme des coions	of the testicle abscess
Saiches que en la section de ceste ramice a paor em plusors dispositions, por coi il me semble que mues vaut c’on la laisse;	Know that in the dissection of this nerve there are many places where fear occurs, for which reason I think it best to leave it.
et je vos dirai l’ovraige et les semblances de l’aposteme.	And I will tell you about the treatment and appearance of the abscess.
Je dis donques que maint aposteme vienent ou cors, et meismement as coions; et c’est par mout de cas.	I therefore say that many abscesses come in the body, especially in the testicles; and this happens in many cases.
C’est a savoir par superfluiteit aigre et ague, qui est espandue as coions, ou de percussion;	This is to know about excess bitterness and agility, which is spread in the testicles, or from impact;
et est li color de l’aposteme selonc la color dou cors; et ne trueve point de dolor, et est aposteme grief;	and the color of the abscess is according to the color of the body; it does not hurt, and the abscess is serious.
et par aventure est uns apostemes griés paourous et pierous, et de fuxe color, et aucune fois vient de nout d’artere, ou d’enfleure de voine.	and by chance there are some grayish, hairy abscesses with pus-like color, and sometimes they come from a burst artery or vein inflammation.
Quant c’est par nout d’artere, si est conus par la disposition d’aposteme chaut, quant tu la presses a tes dois;	When it is from a burst artery, it is recognized by the hot disposition of the abscess, when you press it with your fingers;
et ne covient mie que tu i touches.	and you must not touch it.
Cil qui est fais d’enfleure de voine est conus par sa disposition a l’expression dou touchement des dois,	Those who are affected by swelling of the vein are known by their appearance and the touch of the fingers.
et puet om bien faire la taille sus ceste semblance, et sus les autres chars;	and one can well make the incision on this appearance, and on the other marks;
et est que tu cope lou keur des coions, puis estent l’uef en haut, et le trai fuer dou blanc syfac, et delivre lou suspensoire de toutes pars de l’uef.	and you should cut the skin of the testicles, then the eggs will be on top, and the thread will be removed from all parts of the egg.
Se li uef est ja sodez avec ces chars nees, si covient donques que tu traies l’uef, et lou cope;	If the eggs are already cooked with these new marks, then you should cut the egg and the thread;
et s’il est aers au syfac, ou en ceu qui est dedens les vasselz, si covient que tu delivre toute celle tenve, et la cope reondement.	and if it is in the skin, or in that which is within the vessels, then you must free all that membrane, and smooth out the lump.
Et se li naissance de la char est ou leu derrier, si covient que tu la copes toute, et estrai l’uef, si com nous avons dit.	And if the growth is in the back, then you must cut it all out and extract the egg, as we have said.
Et quant tes ovraiges est acomplis, si emple la plaie de laine moillie en oile roset et en vin, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when your work is finished, then dress the wound with wool moistened in rose oil and wine, then treat it with other remedies until it is healed.
de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscess of the testicles:
Cis est uns apostemes envoloupez d’un envoloupement semblant a .i. borjon, avec le mollifiement des coions,	Here is an abscess wrapped in a covering resembling a cherry, with the softening of the testicles,
et se muet li malaides griement quant il vait;	and the patient groans painfully when he urinates;
et li cure de ceste maladie si est bien pres ausi paourouse com ceste ci devant,	and the treatment of this disease is also as dangerous as the one mentioned earlier,
et toutevoie nos vos dirons l’ovraige de li, selonc ceu que li ancien firent.	and nonetheless, we will tell you about it according to what the ancients did.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus .i. siege aleveit, puis li boute le suspensoire des coions aval a tes dois,	The patient should sit on an elevated chair, then you tie the suspenders of the scrotum tightly with your hands.
a tout le vasseil qui sont prochien a la verge, et les teigne li maistres, et les estende forment;	You should also tie all the vessels that are close to the penis, and tie them tightly, and extend them firmly.
puis cope au spatumile trenchant large dou traver endroit les vasselz, tant qu’il soient descovert,	Then, with a sharp knife, cut through the vessels, as far as they are exposed,
et puis escorche de chescune part, si com nos avons dit en l’estraction des arteres qui sont en temples;	and then skin from each side, as we have said in the extraction of the arteries that are in the temples;
puis i fiche une aguille ou il ait .i. fil double, et le lie au premier leu ou li vis est venue, et le lie derechief a l’autre chief;	then I insert a needle where it is, with a double thread, and tie it at the first place where the thread came out, and tie it again at the other end.
puis les cope em mileu droitement, selonc la longesce dou cors, et en trai les moistors corrumpues;	then cut them in the middle correctly, according to the length of the body, and draw out the corrupted moisture;
puis cure la plaie si com les autres ou on enjanre bowe, si que aucun vassel chiecent que norrissent l’un des coions;	then treat the wound as in the others, so that no blood vessels burst that might cause bleeding in one of the eyes;
car par ceu n’i vient point de mal, et se a toz les vasselz vient vis, si covient traire les coions a tout les vasselz;	for this does not cause harm, and if all the vessels are bleeding, then one must draw out the eyes at every vessel;
si que li oes ne perde son norrissement por l’incision des vasselz, et sechent et ne se puient aidier.	so that the blood does not lose its heat through the incision of the vessels, drying up and unable to help themselves.
de la routure dou syfac	of the rot of the eye socket
Li avenemens de ceste ramice si est par la section que vient ou syfac, ou l’estension sus le ventre en la partie des angres, por coi li intestine dessendent de celle routure a l’un des coions;	The cause of this disease is from the incision that comes to the eye socket, or the extension above the abdomen in the part of the intestines, causing the intestines to descend from that rot to one of the testicles;
et ceste routure est ou dou syfac, ou de l’estension de li, et vienent ces .ij. manieres de mout de causes: ou de percussion, ou de saut, ou de braire, ou de levement de grief faix, et par semblans choses;	and this rot is in the eye socket or from its extension, and these two ways come from causes: from concussion, or jumping, or crying, or lifting heavy objects, and similar things;
et li signes quant c’est de l’estension dou syfac, si est qu’il avient poc et poc, en lonc tens, et ne vient mie soudainnement;	and the signs of dysentery are that it happens a little bit at a time over a long period and does not come on suddenly.
et est li apostemes igalz jusque vers le parfont, por ceu que li syfac apresse l’intestine.	and the abscesses are even throughout to the depth, because dysentery presses on the intestines.
Et li signes est quant c’est de la section dou syfac, qu’elle fait venir a l’encomencement dolor soudaine, et est li apostemes divers apparans, desoz le cuir pres, et c’est por l’issue de l’intestine et le cors au defuer dou syfac.	And the sign is when it is from dysentery, that it causes sudden pain at the beginning, and the abscesses are various appearances below the skin, and it is due to the exit of the intestine and the body's defense against dysentery.
Et aucune fois dessent li cirbes avec l’intestine, et est retenus enqui, et fait grant dolor soffrir au malaide, meismement quant il est pressez.	And sometimes the peritonitis is retained inside, and it causes great suffering to the patient, especially when it is pressed.
Et en ces cures de fer a paor, por coi il s’en covient eschuir.	And in these cures of iron there is fear, which is why one should avoid it.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que tu comande ou malaide qu’il ramoine l’intestine a sa main au dedens en la plaie, s’il i puet rentreir;	And the manner of the operation is that you command the patient to draw in his intestines with his hand into the wound, if he can reach it.
puis soit sovinez sus son col. entre tes mains, et lieve les cuixes;	Then lean over his shoulder between your hands and lift his hips.
puis estent le keur au desus, et cope tout le cuir des coions dou lonc;	Then press the chest upwards, and cut all the skin of the scrotum from the top;
puis boute dedens les leivres de la taille uncines selonc ceu que tu en as mestier por ovrir la plaie, et soit telz que li oes em puist issir;	then push inside the lips of the wound hooks according to what you need to open the wound, and let it be such that the pus can come out;
puis escorche lou syfac que est desoz lou cuir des coions, tant que li blans syfac dur soit descovers de toutes pars;	then scrape off the scurf which is under the skin of the testicles, as far as the white, hard scurf is exposed all around;

et comande au ministre qu’il estende l’uef en haut, et deslie ceu qui est aers derrier le liement;	and instruct the minister to extend the arm upward, and loosen what is constricted behind the elbow;
et quier a tes dois s’il a point de l’intestine envoloupeit ou blanc syfac dur, et se tu en trueves aucune chose, si le boute au ventre desoz;	and feel with your fingers if there is any hardened intestinal swelling or white phlegm, and if you find anything, push it back into the abdomen below;
puis pren une aguille ou il ait .i. gros fil fait de .x. filz, et la boute en la derriere partie dou syfac, qui est aprés lou cuir des coions; aprés la taille, puis cope les chiés qui apperent des filz, tant qu’il i ait .iiij. filz;	Then take a needle with .1. large thread made of .10. threads, and insert it into the rear part of the syphacus, which is beneath the scrotum skin; below the testicles, then pull on the head, which will appear through the threads, until there are .4. threads;

puis envoloupe les chiés des filz, et les lie forment de .ij. pars, si que nuls des vasselz que les norrissent ne puissent entrer en ous, que aposteme chaus n’i viegne;	then wrap the head with threads, and tie it tightly in two parts, so that no vessels which nourish it can enter, lest an abscess form there;
et met derechief le liien selonc le premier liien lonc .ij. dois de celui, et aprés ces .ij. liiens laisse dou syfac qui est desoz lou keur des coions le grant d’un doi;	and place the ligature according to the first long ligature in two turns of that, and after these two ligatures leave the syrup which is under the core of the testicles the size of a bean;
et aprés tout l’autre selonc la rondesce que li euf porte; puis cope en la partie qui est desoz le cuir des coions, tant qui li sans corre, et li bowe, si com nos avons dit ci devant;	and then cut in the part which is under the skin of the testicles, as far as the blood flows, and the scrotum, as we have said before;et quere que le sang corre tant qu’il soit arresté, et la piere ne vienne en la fente; et s’ele est venue, que l’on li traie adés par la fente, si com nos avons dit ci devant.
puis amenistre laine moillie en oile, et met em plaies, et i amenistre le liien que nos avons dit.	Then bring moist wool in oil and place it on the wounds, and then bring the ligature which we have said.
Et aucune fois est cauterizez li blans syfac que nos avons dit, aprés l’incision, par doutance de decorrement de sanc.	And sometimes the white syphilitic sore which we have described is cauterized after an incision out of fear of bleeding.
Car ce avient maintes fois, et laisse le liien tant qu’il chiece per lui; et s’il tarde au cheoir, si soit arosez d’aigue chaude, et met sus ceu que nos avons dit, tant qu’il chiece;	For this happens many times, and it leaves the wound open until it drains through it; and if it is slow to drain, then it should be opened with hot water and the application of what we have described should be repeated until it drains.
puis cure la plaie d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	Then treat the wound with another treatment until it is completely healed.Quant li membres sont disloquez ou esloigez de lor leu, covient il que tu les remettes a lor leu; et s’il ne demourent, qu’il soit desaloiez par cause de moistor, et covient il que tu le remettes aler, si com il est dit au chapistre de l’ajutoire.
de hernie carnouse	of carnous hernia
En ceste ramice ne vis je onques nul qui osast faire la cure par fer.	In this remedy I have never seen anyone dare to perform the cure with iron.
Et li ancien dirent qu’ele est faite si com li ramice qui est ensamble la vis, en teil maniere que tu lie les vasselz, aprés la taille sus ous legierement au desoz;	And the ancients said that it is done like the remedy which is together with the vein, in such a way that you tie the vessels, after the cut above, lightly from below;
puis cope em mi, et cure l’aposteme de ceu qui oevre, tant que li vasselz chient; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	then press gently on it, and cure the abscess of that which opens, until the vessels shrink; and cure it as we have said, until it is healed.
Aucune fois vient routure ens angres, si com nos avons dit, et apert li leus; et ne dessent nulz des intestines as coions, et s’il en i dessent, c’est poc, et repaire toutes houres;	Sometimes there is a rupture in the veins, as we have said, and it opens; and none of the intestines come out into the rectum, and if any do come out, it is a little, and they heal every hour;
et toutevoie s’il demoure trop en cest point, si croit li plaie ou syphac, tant que li intestine dessent;	and yet if he remains too long in this state, the wound or fistula believes that the intestines are descending;
et ceu avient par l’estension dou syfac qui est as angres, si com nos avons dit, car il est estendus, puis est mollifiez et enflez li leus et apert;	and this happens through the extension of the fistula which is in the intestines, as we have said, for it is extended, then softened and swollen open;
et li cure si est par cautere, si com nos avons devant dit; et aucune fois est curee par fer en ceste maniere:	and the cure is through cauterization, as we have previously said; and sometimes it is cured by iron in this way:
et est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos entre tes mains, puis cope le leu de la routure enfleit dou large selonc la quantiteit de .iij. dois;	and the patient lies down on his back between your hands, then press the area of the rupture, swollen with pus, according to its size, about the amount of 3 ounces;
et puis estrai le syfac qui est desoz le cuir que l’ensuet, puis pren lou rait et lou met sor le leu apparant dou syfac;	and then extract the boil which is under the skin, then take the thread and place it over the visible part of the boil;
et lou presse au parfont dou ventre, puis cout les .ij. leus apparans dou syfac sus lou chief dou rait, et cout l’un et l’autre;	and press it to the bottom of the abdomen, then tie the two ends of the thread visible over the boil on the head of the thread, and tie one and the other;
puis estrai le chief dou rait, et ne coper point dou syfac ne n’estendre l’uef n’autre chose, si com je t’ai fait savoir en la cure de la ramice des intestines;	then extract the head of the thread, and do not cover the boil or stretch the vejiga or anything else, as I have told you in the treatment of the rupture of the intestines;
puis le cure par la cure des plaies. Et quant tu copes les filz, si le mundefie et cure la plaie, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	then treat it with wound treatment. And when you tie the threads, if the patient is clean and the wound is healed, as much as it needs to be.
Li syfac est constrains, et n’a point d’apparance en la routure, et li cauteres est muedres en cest leu, et plus prochiens a salut.	The ulcer is constrained, and has no appearance in the wound, and cautery is effective in this case, and closer to safety.
de l’amollissement dou cuir des coions	of the softening of the skin of the scrotum
Maintes fois est amollis li cuirs des coions en aucuns homes, por ceu que les chars que sont dedens sont mollifiees, et est lait a veoir; et est mestier, quant on le vuet curer, c’on faice gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li cope le cuir qui est mollifiez sus le cuir natureil; puis assemble les .ij. levres a une costure, et se tu vues, cout premier la superfluiteit dou cuir mollifiiez a .iij. costures ou .iiij. fermement; puis cope entre les costures, et lou cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez, et chient li fil.	Many times the skin of the scrotum softens in some men due to the testicles within becoming softened, and it is milky in appearance; and when one wishes to treat it, they should make the patient lie on his back, and cut the softened skin on the skin of the scrotum; then bring together the two edges with a single stitch, or at most two or three stitches, firmly; then cut between the stitches, and treat it as you would other wounds, until it is healed, and remove the sutures.
dou chastrement	of chastisement
Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi, et por ceu il me plairoit que je n’en parlasse mie en cest livre; et n’est necessaires fuer que por .ij. manieres: dont l’une est que li mires en saiche respondre quant on li demandera, et en saiche la cure; et li autre, por ceu que nos avons sovent mestier de chastrement d’aucunes bestes por nos aidier, si com de bouc et de mouton et de chait et d’autres bestes. Je dis donques que chastremens est fais selonc .ij. manieres: ou par atraction, ou par fendure.  En celle que nos faisons par attraction, faisons nos seoir la beste en aigue chaude, tant que li coion soient mollifiez et pendant; puis les preing a ta main, tant qu’il soient remis et que tu ne les sentes plus.  Du chastrement de taille: covient que tu teignes la beste, et li presse le cuir des coions a ta main senestre, puis lie le suspensoire, et cope sus chescun oef a .i. cop, quant tu les avras bien escorchiez; et i laisse aucun poc dou syfac et lou subtil syfac qui est sor les vasselz; et ceste maniere de chastrement est muedre que cele qui est faite par attraction, por ceu que a l’atraction demoure par aventure aucune chose des coions, par coi li beste desire luxure; puis cure la plaie tant qu’ele soit sanee.	You know that castration is despised in our law, and because of this, I would rather not discuss it in this book; and it is only necessary for two reasons: the first is so that the person who cares for the animal knows how to respond when asked, and knows how to care for it; and the other reason is because we often need to castrate certain animals to help us, such as bulls, rams, goats, and other beasts. I say then that castration is done in two ways: by attraction or by cutting. In the method we do by attraction, we make the animal sit in hot water until its testicles are softened and hanging; then squeeze them in your hand until they are relaxed and you can no longer feel them. As for castration by cutting: you must hold the animal down, and press the skin of the testicles against your left hand, then tie off the scrotum, and cup your hands over each testicle ten times when you have scrotched them well; and I leave some pus and the fine pus that is on the vessels; and this method of castration is better than the one done by attraction, because in attraction, something from the testicles may remain, causing the animal to desire lust; then cure the wound until it heals.
des hermofrodites	of hermaphrodites
Hermofrodie est selonc .ij. manieres as homes: l’une si est que entre les .ij. coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine.  Et li autre maniere si est en femmes, et ait sus lou poignil ausi com une verge et .ij. coions.  Et li cure de l’ome et de la fame si est que tu copes les chars ajostees toutes, et les cure si com autres plaies; en la seconde maniere, des homes dont li urine saut par lou cuir des coions, si n’a point de cure.	Hermaphrodites are of two types in men: the first is where between the two testicles appears also as the figure of a woman's nature, having hair, and sometimes urinating from it. And the other type is in women who have on the scrotum a penis and testicles. The treatment for both men and women is to cup the swollen areas, and treat them like any other wound; but in the second type of man, where urine escapes through the skin of the testicles, there is no cure.
de la tentigene	of the tentigenes
Tentigene est une chars ajostee sus la partie natureil, tant qu’elle est trop laide a veoir; et aucunes femmes l’ont ausi grant com une main, et c’est li cure. Il covient que tu teignes la superfluiteit de la tentigene a ta main ou as oncines, et la cope legierement; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et a une autre char que naist a la bouche de la marris, et l’emple, et par aventure saut fuer, et est selonc la semblance d’une kowe, et por ceu l’apelerent li ancien «maladie kowee». Si covient que tu la copes, si com nos avons dit la tentigene, et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	of the tentigenes Tentigene is a growth attached to the natural part, so large that it is ugly to behold; some women have them as big as a hand, and this is called the "cure". You should cut away the excess of the tentigene on your hand or fingers, and scrape it gently; do not go too deep, lest bleeding occur, then cure the cure until it is healed. There is also another growth that arises at the mouth of the wound, which you should use, for it may heal, and it resembles a cyst, hence the ancient name "maladie kowee". You should scrape it as we have said for the tentigene, and cure it until it is healed.
de erratique	of erratics
Erratique si est quant li nature de la femme n’est mie percie, ou li pertus est petis; et est naturez par naissance, ou accidens par maladie que venue i est; ou c’est par char ajostee, ou dou syfac subtil ou espés, et est fais em parfont en la marris, ou en costez, ou desoz, ou que soit; et deffent le concevoir, et l’enfantement, et par aventure les flors a avoir; et li connoissance de ceu si est par le regart de la baile. Se li estoupemens est prochiens apparans, si quier a tes dois ou au rait. S’il est dou syfac subtil, et il est prochiens as .ij. leivres, si te haste, et la ront ensi: met tes .ij. dois indices ensamble, et li femme soit sus son dos, espandues ses jambes; puis estent les .ij. leivres forment, tant que li subtilz syfac soit rons, et soit overs li estoupemens; puis pren laine, et la moille en oile, et la met sus le leu, et gise li femme a home chescun jor, si qu’il ne puist souder. Et se li syfac est dur et espés, si covient que tu lou copes au spatumile semblant a foille de mirte. Se li estoupemens est de char nee, si la sospent a l’oncine et la cope; et aies les medicines estainchans sanc, si com acaice, sanc de dragon, encens, ensamble abun d’uef; puis amenistre une caine de plonc large, si que li plaie ne puisse souder; et ensi soit longement, et li amenistre une tente de lin sec; puis soit curez d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.  Et quant en la marris vient char nee, si la covient coper selonc ceste maniere, se ce n’est apostemes enchancrez. Car a l’aposteme enchancreit qui est en la marris, ne doit on touchier de feir.	of erratics Erratic is when the orifice of the woman's womb is not perceived, or it is very small; it can be by nature from birth, or as an accident due to illness that comes upon her; or it may be due to a growth, or a thin or thick membrane, and is located deep in the wound, or on the sides, or underneath, wherever it may be; it affects conception and childbirth, and can even cause flowers to wither; and knowledge of this is through observing the dance. If the opening is apparent, then use your fingers or a rod. If it's a thin membrane, form it into a tube, and hold it in place until the membrane is broken and the opening is covered; then take wool, moisten it in oil, and apply it to the area, and let the woman lie on her back every day so that it does not adhere. And if it is hard and thick, you should scrape it with a spatulum similar to myrtle leaves. If it's an abscess, treat it as follows: use medicines that stop bleeding, such as acacia, dragon's blood, incense, and egg white; then insert a broad piece of linen so the wound does not close; this should be maintained for a long time, and apply a tent made of dry linen; then cure it with other cures until it is healed. And when there is a growth in the wound, treat it as follows, if it's not an abscess with an incision. For you must not touch an abscess to incise it.
des emorroides	of hemorrhoids
Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul; et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation. Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer. Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer. Il covient donques que tu mettes la femme en une maison froide, puis estent l’altelul as tenailles, et le cope en ses racines, puis poudre sus medicines restraignans sanc, si com acaice et sanc de dragon et encens, et semblans choses; puis boute ses piez a la paroit une houre, puis la met en aigue froide; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, si la fai seoir en une decoction de sumac et d’escorce de pomes grenates et de gales et de semblans choses, et puis pren farine d’orge, et la confis avec miel et aisil, et en fai .i. emplaustre sus son dos. Et se il estainche, c’est boin. Se ceu non, se li fai aerdre ventouses au dos et as mameles sens ferir; puis pren lainne, et la moille en jus de plantain ou en jus d’aglentier avec vin viel, et fai aerdre au leu.  Et quant li aposteme repose, si cure lou leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et celle qui est apelee «albathir» est rouge, et est semblans a .i. chief aspre, si le covient coper si com j’ai dit le thelul; et puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Hemorrhoids are openings in the veins that cause pain, and when they are old, they become throbby. We have already discussed their similarities to ulcers, as well as the signs, and I will now mention those that can be cured. I state that hemorrhoids and throbby masses, when they are very painful in the anus, and there is no relief without using a sharp tool, can be treated with cauterization. If they are located near the mouth of the anus, then they can be felt and treated effectively. Therefore, it is important to place the patient in a cool room, cut off the hemorrhoids with tweezers at their roots, and apply a powder made from blood-restraining medicines like acacia, dragon's blood, and incense. Then, tie her feet to the wall for an hour, after which she should be placed in cold water. If there is bleeding, use a decoction of sumac, pomegranate bark, galls, and similar ingredients to soothe the area. Make a poultice with barley flour, honey, and garlic, and apply it to her back. If the pain subsides, that's a good sign. Otherwise, use leeches on her back and breasts without piercing them with a needle. Soak a cloth in plantain juice or dogwood juice mixed with old wine and place it over the affected area. Once the abscess has drained, treat the wound with ointment until it heals completely. The one called "albathir" is red and resembles a rough head; it should be cauterized as mentioned earlier and then treated until it heals.
des apostemes de la marris	of absesses in the anus:
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division. Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe; et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.  Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie; et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus .i. siege, et ait .ij. petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe; et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien; puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme; et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide; et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve; et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument. Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit; et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec; et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites; puis le cure aprés .ij. jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites; puis reveigne a l’oignement.  Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	There are many types of abscesses that can occur in the anus, such as sores, piercings, herpes, fistulas, hemorrhoids, and hot abscesses, as well as other conditions that have been mentioned earlier. Now, I will describe the treatment for a hot abscess in the anus, which is not the same as a bowel abscess. If you notice that the abscess is firm at the beginning of its appearance, and there is heat and fever, and it turns red, then do not rush to pierce it immediately; instead, let the pain subside first. Then, make the patient sit on a chair, with two small pillows to lean against, one on the back and one under the feet, with the legs apart and the arms bent at the knees. Tie the arms under the knees with a good linen cloth, then insert the tip of the instrument used to open the anus and check the depth of the abscess so that the instrument does not go too deep and harm the patient. If the instrument is larger, cover the entrance of the anus with cloth so that it does not cause discomfort to the patient. Then, apply the instrument while holding it upright, and let the patient defecate. After that, clean the area with a moistened sponge or a cloth soaked in rose oil or dry vert oil, and insert the tent into the wound, pushing it deep into the anus and against the wall of the rectum. Then, place a cloth soaked in warm water or a decoction of mallows over the wound, followed by a poultice of linseed and honey on top, covering the entire area. After two days, remove the poultice and treat it with ointment until it heals. Sometimes, raising the anus and cleaning the wound with a clistere made of water, honey, and a decoction of lilies and aristolochia helps. Then, return to treating it with ointment. If the wound has drained and healed, avoid using heat, but treat it as mentioned earlier in the division.
de l’enfantement	of childbirth
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar: adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir; adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui; et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost; car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification; et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment. Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises; si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	It is necessary for the midwife to know the natural shape of childbirth and its signs: when you see a woman straining downward and desiring to smell aromatics, then hasten the child's emergence; then you will know that this childbirth is according to nature, and the placenta comes out with the child; and when you see these signs, it is necessary to gently press her belly so that the child comes out quickly. For when the child comes down on its head, the placenta follows, and the mother is cleansed of her excesses by good cleansing. But those who come in other ways do not come naturally. For sometimes a child comes out on its feet, or outside the body from the chest, hands, abdomen, or back; sometimes it is turned upside down on the neck, or it may take on other bad shapes. It is necessary for the midwife to be wise and skilled in these matters, guarding against error and deception, and I will show you all the forms and how they should be helped.
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent; et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	If the child comes out head first in a natural way, and the woman gives birth painfully, and her strength is weak, then let her sit on a stool or be held by women; and let her drink the juice of roasted oil or fenugreek, and then let the midwife insert the little spatulum, of which I will now describe the form:
et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers; et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament; puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre: si istra maintenant l’enfes.Et se les .ij. mains issent fuer, si covient que tu les ramoinne legierement poc et poc; et s’elles n’i puent entrer, si met la femme sus .i. siege, et li lieve les piés en haut; puis deboute le siege sus terre, et teigne on la femme, qu’elle ne chiece au deboutement; et se li mains n’i puet entrer, et li enfes muert, si li cope les mains au couteil qui est ci devant mis, et estrai l’enfant, et ramoine igalment.	and split the placenta, and scrape away the mucous membrane with her fingernail until the moist fluid that is within flows out; and pinch the woman's belly so that the child comes down, and if it does not come down, then the woman must be enemaized with a fenugreek poultice mixed with oil of sweet alyssum; then let her drink and sneeze with condisi, and hold her mouth and nose for an hour: then the child will come out. And if both hands come out, then you must gently pull them in little by little; and if they cannot enter, then put the woman on a chair, and lift her feet up; then stand the chair on the ground, and let someone hold her so that she does not lean forward; and if the hands cannot enter, and the child is dead, then grasp the hands at the knuckles that are mentioned above, and pull out the child, and reset it in the same way.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses piez	of the baby's birth on its feet
Quant li enfes vient sus ses piez, si lou covient bouter en haut;	When a child is born standing, it should be turned upside down.
et puis le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit igalz;	And then turn it slowly and gently until it is straight;
puis preigne .i. des piez et l’estende poc et poc.	then grip one of its feet and extend it slowly.
Cant il saut jusc’as cuixes, si la comande a preindre, et la fai esternuer de condisi;	When it jumps up to the armpit, instruct him to catch it, and make him sneeze by sprinkling pepper.
si saut fuer, se Deus vuet.	If it jumps away, God willing.
Et s’il n’ist fuer si com nos avons dit, si le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit selonc la figure natureil.	And if it doesn't jump as we have said, then move it little by little until it returns to its natural position.
Car adonques ist il legierement.	For then it will be easy.
Et s’il ne vient fuer si com nos avons dit, si pren muscillaige de altee, et oile de sisament, et gomme fondue, et broie tout en .i. mortier;	And if it does not come out as we have said, then take a mixture of honey and lard, and oil of sweet almonds, and melted gum, and grind them all together in .i. mortar;
et met sus la nature de la femme dedens et defuer cest oignement,	and put this ointment on the woman's nature inside and out,
puis la fai seoir en aigue tede jusque desoz les costelz;	then have her sit in warm water up to her ribs;
et quant elle est moillifie desoz, se li fai .i. coliere de mirre, et li met desoz, et li laisse une houre;	and when she is moistened underneath, make a collar of myrrh for her and put it on her underneath, and leave it for an hour;
puis la fai seoir sus .i. siege, puis la fai esternuer et estraint sa bouche et son neis, et li preint le ventre legierement, car li enfes saut maintenant.	then have her sit on a chair, then have her sneeze and pinch her nose and mouth, and gently press her belly, for the child will come out at once.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses genous	of the child's delivery upon his knees
Quant li enfes vient en ceste forme, si i mette li baile ses mains poc et poc;	When the child comes in this way, he puts his hands on his feet little by little;
puis soit sovinee sus son col, et li pendent li piez aval, et soit gisans sor .i. lit;	then he is laid on his back, and his feet hang down, and he lies on a bed;
et plie ses mains poc et poc, et puis li preint les mains sus lou ventre, et li oste les cussins desoz, tant qu’elle soit appareillie aval;	and folds her hands a little, then presses her hands on his stomach, and lifts the cushions underneath, until she is satisfied with what she sees.
et se li enfes ne saut, si pren ses piez et li muef forment, puis li muef lou ventre amont, puis i boute tes mains;	and if the child does not cry, she takes her feet and moves them gently, then moves his stomach upwards, then she puts her hands in;
et ewe l’enfant poc et poc; et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse.	and rocks the child gently; and instructs the woman to hold on until the child passes.
de l’issue de l’enfant qui vient dou large une main pendant	of the baby's birth, which comes out wide enough for one hand to pass through
I covient engignier a ramener la main:	It is necessary to engineer how to bring back the hand:
s’on ne la puet ramener, si fai lever la femme, et aler;	if one cannot bring it back, then have the woman lift herself and walk;
s’elle ne puet aler, si la fai gesir sus .i. lit, et li deboute les jambes forment;	if she cannot walk, then have her lie on a bed and stretch out her legs;
puis amenistre lou muscillaige que j’ai conteit;	then bring the castor oil that I have mentioned;
et s’elle n’enfante, si la fai seoir sus .i. siege, puis estudie au rameneir la main;	and if she does not give birth, then make her sit on a chair, then study to bring the hand back;
et ewe l’enfant selonc la figure natureil, et la fai esternuer, et li comande qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse fuer.	and turn the child according to its natural position, and make her sneeze, and command that she hold on until the child comes out.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus son col, et ait espandues ses mains, et sa faice tornee devers lou dos sa mere	of the emergence of the child above his neck, and has his hands spread out, and his face turned towards his mother's back
I covient que li baile teigne sa main, puis le torne poc et poc, et l’ewe legierement;	I must have him grip her hand, then turn it slowly, little by little, and gently;
et quant il est igalz, si met sus la nature muscillaige de altee et oile, si com nos avons dit, puis li comande qu’elle se mueve poc et poc;	and when it is even, he puts on the mustard mixture with honey and oil, as we have said, then he instructs that it moves little by little;
et quant tu avras ce fait, si la fai seoir sus .i. siege, et li comande k’elle se preigne; et la fai esternuer.	and when you have done this, make her sit on a seat, and instruct her to sneeze; and make her yawn.
de ceste meisme maniere a tout la secondine	in the same way for all of the afterbirth
Quant il vient fuer en ceste maniere a tout la secondine, si cope la secondine a ton ungle, tant que li moistors soit vuidie;	When it comes out in this way to all of the afterbirth, catch the afterbirth with your fingers, as long as the fluids are drained;
et se li enfes pent sus sa faice et sus son col, si la cope des la boude, qu’elle ne soit retenue, et muere li enfes;	and if the child lies on its face and on its neck, if the mother ignores it, it will not be retained and the child will die.
puis boute l’enfant dedens, tant que tu l’aies mis si com il covient, et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne aucune fois:	then place the baby inside, as long as you have placed it as it should be, and instruct the woman to grip herself several times:
adonques si istra legierement.	then press gently.
de l’issue des gemelz	from the exit of the twins
Saiches que gemeil naissent maintes fois, et aucune fois en naissent .iij. ou .iiij.; et ceu n’est mie estrainge chose, et poc avient.	Know that twins are born many times, and sometimes three or four are born; and this is not a strange thing, and it happens rarely.
Dui sont estrainge chose, et ne vivent mie, se poc nom;	Twins are a strange thing, and they do not live long if it is rare.
je sai ceu, qu’il soient multipliiet, et sont desevrez par lou syfac qui les devise, qui est liiez a la boude;	I know that they are multiplied and separated by the placenta which divides them, which is attached to the womb;
et aucune fois issent ausi naturelment com uns tous sous, si com nos avons dit.	and sometimes they issue just as naturally as one alone, as we have said.
Et s’il issent griement, si la cure si com nos avons dit, et soit li baile subtilz, et faice tost et legierement ceu qu’elle fait;	And if they are bleeding profusely, then the treatment as we have said, and be subtle in giving it, and do quickly and lightly what she does.
et faice ensi com il vaut mues a salut.	and do thus as it is good for his health.
de plusors enfans	of many children
Aucune fois sont formez en la marris .i. ou .ij. ou .iij. ou .iiij. ou .v. ou .vj. ou .vij., ou plusors jusc’a .xv., et sont tout formeit en forme d’enfant par le mesurement dou saige glorious,	Sometimes they are formed in the womb: one or two or three or four or five or six or seven, or more up to fifteen, and they are all formed in the shape of a child according to the measurement of the glorious sage,
et couvient que li baile saiche tout ceu, car par aventure semblans chose li avient;	and it is necessary for the surgeon to know all of this, because a similar thing might happen to him;
si faice selonc ceu qu’il covient.	then act according to what is appropriate.
de l’enfant mort	of the dead child
Quant tu cures la femme de l’enfant mort ou ventre, si com j’ai dit en la division, et il ne vient fuers, et tu es constrains d’ovraige de mains;	When you are treating a woman of a dead child or in the womb, as I have said in the division, and there is no pulse, and you are forced to work with your hands;
si covient que tu saiches se li femme est de saine vertut, et n’ait accident ou elle ait paor de mort;	if you should know whether the woman is of sound health and has no accident or fear of death.
si covient que li femme soit sovinee sus son dos, et soit ses chiés enclins aval, et les jambes levees;	the woman should be laid on her back, with her hips tilted downward and her legs lifted up.
et li ministre la teigne de .ij. pars, ou elle soit liie au lit si qu’elle ne soit traite au dessendement de l’enfant;	and the midwife should apply the tea to her vagina, or if she is tied to the bed so that she does not move around too much and harm the baby.
puis frotez la bouche de la marris d’oiles moistes avec muscillaige de altee et de fenugrec et semence de lin, puis oigne li baile ses mains de ces oiles et de ces muscillaiges;	Then rub the mouth of the mother with moist oil mixed with almace and fenugreek and flaxseed, then anoint the midwife's hands with these oils and musks.
puis les boute en la marris legierement, puis quiere .i. leu ou elle boute les oncines que soient covenaubles a ceu,	then gently push them into the marrow, then heat .i. needle until it is red hot
et pren warde se li enfes est apparilliez qu’il dessende sus son chief;	and be careful that the needle does not enter the brain
si fiche les oncines en ses eulz ou en son col ou en sa bouche ou en som palais ou desoz la barbe ou en la forcele ou pres des costez,	if he pierces them in his eyes or nose or mouth or palate or under the beard or near the armpit,
et se li dessendemens est sus piez, se li fiche ou poignil et as costes moienes;	and if the swelling is on the feet, pierce or press it at the middle of the shins;
et covient qu’il teigne l’oncine a sa main destre, et mette la corbeure entre ses dois de la senestre main, et li boute a tout sa main legierement, et fiche l’oncine en aucun de ces leus que nos avons dit, tant qu’il viegne a la chose vuide;	and you should have him hold the needle in his right hand and place the thread between the fingers of his left hand and wind it around all his fingers lightly, and insert the needle into any of the places we mentioned so that he comes to the empty spot;
et c’est li forme de l’oncine:	and this is the shape of the needle:
