Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne;	Cauteries are a great help if the bone is healthy and the nail is healthy;
et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece,	and if the nail pushes against the flesh and starts to grow out, and the bleeding
si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char,	then you should put a thread under the nail so that it does not pierce the flesh,
et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement,	and pour it on top, and gently and lightly beat this thin flesh.
et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout;	and place upon the remaining flesh burning and corrosive medicines to remove everything;
puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	then heal it with ointments until it is healthy.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner;	And if the corrosion is in the bone, then cut it out and throw it away, because as long as the corrupted bone remains, it cannot heal.
et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en .i. des nous si com il est devant dit,	and if you see the tooth decay, then cut it in half as it is said before,
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	then clean it until it is healthy;
et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier;	and if it is rotten and hollow, and he feels great pain, then you must heal him first;
puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus,	then cut the nail of the little finger with a slanting cut from above,
et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor;	And make sure the cut does not reach the flesh underneath the nail, for the patient would feel too much pain.
et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	And if it happens [the cut reaches the flesh], then place something on top to soothe it.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	The pain should be dulled in the hand
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus,	The joints of some people's hands are naturally very fleshy,
et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle,	and sometimes there is tissue or bone, and occasionally there is a toenail,
et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	and some of them grow from the root of the joint, or the growth is in one of the fingers.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet,	That which grows in any finger of the hand does not move,
et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet;	and that which grows at the joint of the finger, sometimes moves;
la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere:	the cautery of fire is light, in such a way:
taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	cut it at its root with a broad spatulum.
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer: si te tien dou coper.	He who is born at the root of the joint is painful to cure; keep him covered.
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os,	In one who is born in the hip socket, you must first cut away the round flesh up to the bone,
puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	then cut the bone with a suitable thread, then treat it until it is healed.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The dislocation of two bones together occurs through birth, or the sudden impact of a wound, or the scalding of fire, or similar things.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz;	So you must cut that joint so that the bones can return to their natural alignment;
puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent;	then place between two tents or wet cloths in rose oil, so that they do not adhere;
ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	or you place it between two thin pieces of wood, so that they are glued together as they should be.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	If the glue comes to either of his hands with the palm, then cover the glue as it should be.
Des vils	Of the wicked
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors;	There are veins which are large and enveloped in excess of melancholy fluids, which come from various parts of the body;
et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	and more occurs in the legs of those who walk and work and carry things, than in others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	Therefore you should administer to him some purgative medicine sometimes, and then heal the wound with basil.
Li cure de fer si est selonc .ij. manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir;	The treatment with iron is done in two ways: one is by cupping, drawing out the black blood;
et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	and the other way is to open the vein and draw it all out.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez,	The incision is made thus: first, raise the leg with very hot water until the large veins become细 small.
puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil;	Then stretch the leg of the patient from above the thigh to the part below the knee;
puis cope la voinne en .i. leu, ou en .ij. ou en .iij., d’une taille large,	Then cut the vein in one, two or three places, with a wide incision;
puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir;	Then squeeze and draw out the black blood with your hand, from one end to the other, as much as the patient can endure;
et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire;	and then the scabs, and he is instructed to dye his skin with black gall;
et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	and begin the evacuation and bleeding again when the veins are full, and this is harmful to the patient.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil,	The treatment for him is as follows: raise the leg of the patient, if there is much hair,
puis le met ou bain, et li. arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes;	then put it in a bath, and raise the leg with hot water until it turns red, and open the veins;
et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville;	and if you have no bath, heat it over fire, and then apply it directly to the vein from the knee to the ankle, or in the part below the ankle.
puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent;	Then open the skin at the joint, and scorch the vein on both sides until it appears when you feel for it.
et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche;	And when it enters the skin, it looks like a white cord.
puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier,	Then push the thread beneath, until it is lifted from the skin, and then it can be pulled out easily at the joint.
puis le cope en .i. autre leu ensus iij. dois; puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere,	then cut in another place above it three times; then scorch the skin over the vein until it appears
puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers;	then ligature it at the base, as you did before, and bind it with another hook, as you did before;
puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet,	then cut another vein, or several if you need to, then ligature it, and cut the toe of the foot,
puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille; puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope;	then draw it and ligature from the second vein up; then draw it from vein to vein until it comes out completely, then cut it;
et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout .i. fil fort double,	and if you cannot pull it out and lift it, then insert a needle on a strong double thread.
et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz .i. rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse;	tie it and pull it out, and insert it under the nail, and move your hand from side to side until it comes out;
et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide;	and be careful that it does not tear, for if it tears, then it cannot be pulled or lifted, and the patient will be harmed;
et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and when you have pulled it out completely, put over the wound wool moistened with wine and rose oil; and treat it until it is healed.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit,	And if the eye is cramped and twisted and enveloped together, and it is not straight, as we have said,
si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie; et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	you should split it crookedly, but do not cover it; and treat it as we have previously stated.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne;	The shape of the iron used to cover the eye should be curved, and not cut so that it does not cover the vein;
et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	and is of a deep curve, for if it were subtle, it would cover the vein, but it should be thick as we have said, and here is its shape:
De la voinne civile	Of civil bleeding
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor;	This bleeding occurs in the legs, in warm regions where no herbs or trees grow, and in dry land where there is no moisture.
et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir,	It may also occur elsewhere on the body, and this happens due to a pustule that forms under the skin,
si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	such as serpents and worms that infect between the skin and flesh.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation,	And if the signs of the beginning of this wound are that a great inflammation comes in the leg,
puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	then change the place, and the wound will come out as if it were the root of a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a .ij. З., et la noe,	When the shoulder opens up, you must wrap around it a piece of linen three and a half to four inches wide, and tie it,
et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe;	and let the cloth hang down to the leg, and every time it is pushed out by the swelling, wrap around it with the cloth again, and tie it;
et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue;	and if it is too long, cut off a part of it, wrap up the rest, and do not cover the root at all until it comes out completely.
car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie;	because if you cover it, it will go back into the flesh, causing an abscess and pus in that spot, and a serious illness.
por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors;	Because of this, it must be treated little by little until the very end, so that nothing is left in the body.
et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de .v. paumes de lonc, ou de .x.,	And sometimes this vein, when treated from five to ten palm lengths,
et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de .x. paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute .i. rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons,	and a man came to me whose penis was ten palms long; and when you grab it, it goes into one hole or opening, and you pierce it all the way through
si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	so that all of its content is discharged; and after administering astringent remedies for several days, treat it like an abscess.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet,	And sometimes the vein will open in the joint of the foot or the leg,
et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	and it will spurt out a lot of blood; treat it therefore as we have said before.
Des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	Of worms that grow between skin and flesh
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués,	This disease is called "cattle disease" in our land because it often affects oxen:
et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant,	It is a small worm that grows between skin and flesh, moving throughout the body, going up and down:and li vers ont la figure de l’escarne.
et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer;	And the worm has the appearance of a scar. And one feels it well as it moves from member to member, until it breaks through the skin where it goes, and jumps out:et s’il adont le corps, il est mortel.
et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre;	and is filled with pus from some humors, like worms and snakes and roundworms in the belly;
et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil,	one fears its malice, for when it goes through the body, and it rises to the head, and comes to the eye,
par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	by chance it enters and destroys the eye; and this happens many times.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait:	When you see it being cured and bled, one cannot help but wonder when it will end:
si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement,	if therefore thou must tie the part above and below with a strong bandage well and tightly,
puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves,	then cut over it and pull it out, and if the blood flows profusely from the wound, and you do not stanch it,
si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire;	then cauterize it with fire until it stops bleeding;
et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit;	and the greatest harm it does is that it makes the eye water, as we have said;
et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer;	and if you see it coming near the eye, then squeeze under it the eyebrow firmly, then pull upwards and out.
et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries,	and one should use the patient's purification of the body with dissolving medications for putrid humours,
et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	and beware of meat that is decaying and putrefying.
De la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	Of the pain that comes from flatulence:
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres,	This disease is called "vakirir" in our land, and it is a pain that comes in some members,
et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	and then moves from one member to another; and I saw what I am telling you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais;	I was called to a sick woman, and she uncovered her arm, and I saw a small swelling on the vein of her arm;
et .i. poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule,	and soon after, I saw it rise up as a worm to her shoulder,
plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre;	as quickly as anything, like quicksilver when it moves from one place to another;
li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule,	the pain leaves that spot and goes into the shoulder,
et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais;	and then a little later it runs throughout the body until it reaches the other arm;
puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	then she started twisting around her body, just as I saw her.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I marveled much how she moved from limb to limb, for I had never before seen this illness in this way.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre,	Nevertheless, I had seen many who had pain moving from one place to another,
mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme;	but I had never seen it as I did in the woman;
et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes,	and I thought that it was because women had dry bodies and exposed their skin,
et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte;	and because of this the forced wind appears;
et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	and they do not appear according to this reason in those who are delicate, and who have moist bodies and relaxed veins.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit,	And when you see this disease being treated, and the patient feels the pain, if it appears to you as we have said,
si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer;	then press above and below until the forced wind emerges from its place;
et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz,	and cauterize the area; and if you do not see it with your own eyes,
si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	if the patient vomits up wind-eggs, as foul-smelling pills, and serapin pills, and similar things.
Des saiettes	Of arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	Arrows are diverse, according to their appearances and according to the places in the body where they land.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees;	The diversity of their (wounds) is such that some have great points, others small; some are sharp, and others blunt.
et de celles qui ont .ij. angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces;	some have two angles, others have a tongue-like shape, and others contain fragments;
et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc .ij. manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit,	and they can affect the body in two ways: they can affect a principal member,
si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	such as the brain, heart, liver, lungs, intestines, bladder and similar organs.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent:	When it occurs therefore in any of these limbs, and the signs of death that I will tell you about below become apparent to you:
si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions;	then you must be careful about extracting this arrow, for death comes after in many cases.
et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	And when these bad signs do not appear to you, and the arrow is not deeply embedded, then pull it out and treat the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil,	And the sign of the brain when the arrow hits and pierces the bone, and the blood vessels burst above the brain,
est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole;	is when there is scrofula and sores and ulcers and redness, and inflammation of the tongue, and spasms and confusion of the mind, and vomiting of bile;
et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix;	and perhaps there is a discharge from the nose or ears; and perhaps they lose their speech and voice; and
et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char;	and there is also white moist pus from the wound, and also blood-clots;
et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	And if these signs appear, then keep to the treatment, and pull out the arrow if it is stuck in.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide;	The signs of pleurisy when it occurs in the chest are that it is close to the left breast and feels as if it were pierced by a hard object, not hollow.
et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope:	And sometimes the chest mutes like the pulse, and short black blood comes out, and there is a coldness and cold sweat, and syncope.
saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	Then you know beyond doubt that death is imminent.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign of pleurisy that affects the lungs is that without pain foam comes out of the wound, and the throat swells, and the patient changes color, and breathes heavily and seeks the cold air.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	And if an arrow pierces the sole of the foot, it is near the small bones; and it causes great pain and great distress and sighing; and all the shoulder joints move.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if an arrow pierces the stomach, by chance some undigested food might escape from the wound.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if an arrow pierces the belly, and no feces escape through the bowel, then there is little hope of a cure, nor of extracting the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	And if an arrow pierces the bladder, and urine escapes and flows out, and the patient feels great pain: know that the wound is deadly.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other limbs, such as the face, neck, throat, shoulder, armpit, spine of the back, forearm, thigh, and leg, and similar limbs, are safe according to various dispositions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow is in a nerve or artery and is not venomous, as I will tell you so that you may do likewise.
Il avint a .i. home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis:	It happened to a certain man that an arrow hit him in the shoulder joint at the root of the arm:
je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	I probed it, and pulled it out from under the fat of the ear, and he was healed without pain.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz,	And put on one leg an arrow which fell into the fat of the eye below the membrane below.
et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust,	and the arrow was drawn back so that only the tip pointed towards the body,
et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout .i. fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	and was shot from a Turkish bow, at a distance of about 200 paces; the victim was unharmed and no bad accident happened.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles:	And they shot an arrow into the throat of a Christian, and it was shot from an Arabic bow at a distance of about 200 paces:
je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	I shaved the beards, and subtlely as I treated her, she was healed, and the Christians were saved.
Et traï une saiette a .i. home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit;	And I extracted an arrow from a man who had it lodged in his belly, and I thought he was going to die;
et puis qu’il ot passez .xxx. jors, si ne mua point sa disposition;	and after thirty days had passed, his condition did not improve;
je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	I cut into the arrow, and extracted it, and he had no bad reaction.
Et si vis .i. home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus;	And if you wish to treat a person who has an arrow lodged in his back, and the wound is sutured on top;
et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez,	and the arrow remains inside him, and his natural dispositions do not change,
ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	and he experiences no harm in any of his natural functions.
Et vis .i. autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie;	And if you see a man who has an arrow lodged in his face, and the wound is sutured;
et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	and remain thus without great pain; and many others similarly.
Et traï une saiette a .i. home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz,	And I treated an arrow that had pierced the neck of a royal prince,
et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue	and was slightly tilted to the right; and the arrow was fully embedded,
Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue .iij. jors. Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	I was called to treat it after it had been pierced for four days. I found the wound very narrow.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie;	I touched her all over with a subtle test, and felt nothing;
et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	and she felt prickling and pain beneath her right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette	I thought it was from the tip of the arrow
Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast;	I placed a cooling and digestive plaster on the site, so that the swelling would go down;
et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	and I saw the end of the arrow.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens,	I applied the ointment several times and healed the wound directly, and the patient remained in this state for a long time,
tant qu’il sentit la saiette .i. jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	until he felt the arrow inside his nose; and he told me so.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte,	I put corrosive medicine on the wound several times until it was open,
et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu;	and I touched it, and felt the head of the arrow which protruded from the wound;
puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement;	then I applied the ointment to the wound until the head of the arrow appeared visibly;
et trespassa bien li termines entor .iiij. mois,	and he recovered fully within four months,
et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir;	and then the wound festered where I had cut it with the forceps, and it could not heal;
adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris .i. jor as tenailles bien faites,	then I ceased not to devise and invent means of instruments until I took her .i. day with well-made tongs,
selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	according to what the form will be at the end of this chapter, as long as I treated her and restored the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer:	And I saw that the cartilage of the nose could not be restored:
je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	I restored it therefore, and the wound was sewn up, and the patient was completely healed.Et li mirent de sanz que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer:
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes,	Now I have told you about the extraction of certain arrows.
si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre;	so that you may apply my instructions to those things which I do not explain, for books cannot encompass everything.
mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant,	but wise teachers understand many things, and what is both present and lacking,
trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	they find new remedies, and nine instruments, for the treatment of foreign diseases that occur in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc .ij. manieres:	I say that arrows are drawn from the members where they are stuck according to two methods:
ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part;	either through the entrance wound or elsewhere;
et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	and that which jumped out through where it entered is an arrow that pierces through to the bone, and sometimes jumps out right away.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue;	And if it doesn't jump out immediately, leave it until the flesh around the wound is rotted away and the exit is relieved;
et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor;	and also if it is lodged in the bone, and cannot come out, then leave it there for a few days and move it every day;
et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout .i. foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	and then it will pop out, but if not, then pierce around the edge with a very fine awl until the opening is enlarged, and then pull it out.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil,	And if an arrow is lodged in the bone of the head, and goes just to one of the ventricles of the brain,
et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors,	and some of the accidents that I have described are harmful to the patient: then do not pull it out, but leave it for several days until it is even and smooth,
car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	for if the arrow comes to the throat, it is death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac,	And if the arrow is not stuck only in the bone, and does not come to the throat,
et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	and the patient remains for several days without any bad signs, then use the pulling engine.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it is stuck very tightly and cannot come out, then administer cuts around it, as I have told you; then cure the area until it is healed.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente;	And if the arrow is lodged inside the body where it cannot be seen, then she will feel it all over her body;
et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble;	and if you feel it, then pull it out with an appropriate instrument;
et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette,	and if you cannot due to the tightness of the wound and the depth of the arrow,
et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans;	and there is no bone or nerve or vein in the way, then cut through until the wound is large enough;
et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient,	and pull out the arrow if you can, and if there are ears on the arrow so it holds on,
si oste la char qui est ens fichie de .ij. pars au mues que tu pues,	then cut off the flesh that is stuck to it in two or three places that you can reach,
et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire;	and then break or bend the ears of the arrow, so that you may pull it out;
et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	and be careful not to break the arrow, for if you do, you will hurt them more when you pull it out.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you cannot at once, then let it lie until around the nail is soft, then pull it, for the extraction is eased.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre;	And if the flow of blood makes you feel contrary, then administer what we have said about the treatment in its chapter;
et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril,	and beware of cutting the nerve and of opening a vein, and use cauterization as you are able to draw out the arrow without danger,
ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens,	either quickly or slowly, or firmly or gently; and put the patient according to the way they were when the arrow hit them,
car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	for it is the greatest help he can get, and if you cannot do it, then follow what the signs show you.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment:	Arrows that come from elsewhere, where something is seen or felt through the skin or the skin is swollen in that spot:
taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	then cut into it with tweezers as deeply as they can grip, and then extract it; if it won't come out just yet, leave it for now.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	If it is stuck in the bone, then rotate your hand around, as deep as it can go into the bone, and widen the wound, then pull it out.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer;	And if it cannot come out, then leave it again, and then repeat the extraction until it comes out.
et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust;	and if it is of the arrow shaft, then fill it with all the stuff;
et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre .i. estrument cheveit,	and if the shaft is thin, and you want to administer a poultice, then administer a warm poultice,
si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer,	so that the tip of the arrow goes into the flesh of the wound; and then fill it up,
et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute .i. estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	and if the arrow is lodged, he pushes .i. instrument into it to ease its extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues,	And if the arrow is touching [the flesh], then you should cut around the whole wound where the poison is, if you can,
puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	then treat the wound as it should be.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope;	And if the arrow pierces the buttock, or the stomach, or the belly, or the bladder, or the ribs, and it is deep, and you can cut above it,
et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est;	and keep from covering the vein and the nerve, then pull it out, then cut the wound, if necessary.
et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	and treat it until it is healed.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shape of the tongs used to treat arrows is similar to the beak of a bird, and here is the shape:
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	And there are many types: large, medium, and small, depending on the size of the arrow.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel,	The shape of a bald person's head is like the feather of a bird,
por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	to push against the tip of an arrow, as is its shape.
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	the shape of tongs for pushing and gripping is thus:
des voinnes dou cors communes	of the common veins of the body
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont .xxxi., de coi il a ou chef xvi.,	Of the veins from which one heals there are 31, from which it has in the head 16,
c’est a savoir: .ij. batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»;	that is to say: 2 veins that are behind the ears, which are called the two "ear-veins";
et les .ij. arteres qui sont en .ij. temples apparans;	and the 2 arteries that are in the 2 temples, visible;
et .ij. voines que sont en .ij. larmiers des .ij. eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»;	and 2 veins that are in the 2 eyelids of the eyes, which are called  "eyelid-veins";
et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis;	and the vein that is within the forehead; and the vein that is at the top of the nose;
et les .ij. guindeges qui sont ou col;	and the two windpipes which are in the neck;
et les .ij. voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»;	and the two veins that are above the lips on the mouth, and those are the veins called 'augerich';
et .ij. voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	and the two veins that are under the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont .v. en chescun bras:	The veins which are commonly opened are five in each arm:
l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»;	one is the cephalic vein, which is on the left side of the neck, and common people call it 'the head vein';
et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique,	and the middle one is called the 'fast', and is composed of the cephalic and basilic veins;
et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit,	and common people call it the 'heart vein'; and the basilic vein is on the right side of the neck,
et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile,	and they call it the common people "wound of the belly", and it is on the scrotum,
et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	and it is the one that heals, which opens clearly above the testicle.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a .ij. rains;	And the salvadora is the vein that is between the little finger and the ring finger, and it has two branches:
et en la jambe et ou piet sont .iij. voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit,	and in the leg there are three veins: one is below the curve of the pouch of the left side,
et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei;	and the second sopmane which is at the ankle of the right foot; and the vein called "nesse", which is at the ankle of the other foot;
et en l’autre jambe sont .iij. voinnes desoz celles.	and in the other leg there are three veins below them.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine;	The bleeding of the veins that are behind the ears helps with old cataracts and with emigration [of the eye].
et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide,	and the quality of the bleeder is that as I told you, and it is that you raise the head of the patient,
et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis,	and rub the area where the veins are with a rough cloth; then squeeze the patient's neck with a twist of thread,
tant que les .ij. voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en .ij. leus dependens dou chief:	until the two veins appear behind the ears in two places extending from the head.
quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche;	Take it in your hand, and where you feel the pulse underneath your finger, grab it tightly;
puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont,	then take the lancelet, and stick it underneath the vein just to the bone, then lift your hand along the entire vein upstream,
et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien .ij. dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues;	and cut both the skin and the vein well. Make two incisions through the skin, and let blood flow until you see it;
puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee;	then stretch and tie it, until it is healed;
et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	and I have already described the incision and cautery in the first book.
Li sainie des .ij. arteres que sont en .ij. temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene,	The bleeding of the two arteries that are in the temples, it is worth to treat with old bloodletting,
et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz;	and blindness, and habitual dimness of sight, and in the body of the eyes, acute tears;
et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis:	and the qualities of the surgeon if he is as I say:
et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les .ij. voinnes aperent apertement;	and the patient stretches his neck so that the two veins are clearly visible;
et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche;	and feels pain in his chest, and then faints;
puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz,	then gently touch the vein above with your thumb, and push the lance underneath.
et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en .ij. autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit;	and gently open the vein above, and the vein, as you have done in the other veins, and let the blood flow according to your need;
puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton;	then loosen the bandage, and put your hand on the vein for an hour, then place cotton on top;
et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	and then tie it tightly, and leave it until it is healed; and we have spoken of their bandaging and their extraction, in the beginning of the book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor;	The bleeding from the vein on the forehead is just as effective as the bleeding of the cephalic vein for old diseases of the face, and for headache and redness.
et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere;	and the qualities are such that the patient twists his neck until the vein appears;
puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	then take the instrument called a "borer", of which this is the shape:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues;	and place the tip on the vein, and press with your hand or something else, and let the blood issue according to the amount you wish.
puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	then gently cauterize the neck, and ligate the vein until it is healthy, and sometimes the work is done with a broad flame.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	Nevertheless, the flames should not be too sharp; and it heals crookedly, because the bone is close by, and perhaps breaks the flame when it is delicate.
Li sainie des .ij. voines que sont en .ij. larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice;	The healing of the two veins that are in two layers, aids the eyes, and tigress, and redness, and oriel in the eye, and diseases of the face;
et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant;	and the qualities of their healing are such that the patient twists his neck by pulling with some thread, as before;
puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	then cleanse it, and let the cautery be of the size of a straw, a little longer than the flame, for there is no flesh there.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	And if the flames are subtle, perhaps it will break; then blood will flow, as much as you need, and then tie it with a thread, and tie it well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice,	The cautery of the vein of the nose is useful for nosebleeds, and for sudden madness, and for facial diseases,
si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene;	such as migraine and redness that comes to the face, and especially when it is persistent;
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre,	and the quality of the healing is such that the patient squeezes his neck, then squeeze his nose with your left hand,
et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les .ij. narines,	take a long, thin flame and insert it into the lip in the space between the two nostrils,
car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre;	because the vein will not open well otherwise, and the blood will begin to flow now;
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree;	and do not go too deep, and let the blood flow according to your need, then ligate it for a night, because it is very quickly restored;
et c’est li forme dou flaime:	and this is the form of the flame:
Li sainie des .ij. guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes;	The juice of two yarrow plants helps with inflammation of the liver, and at the onset of malaria, and many illnesses, and impetigo, and corrosion, and herpes, and ulcers;
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit;	and the quality of the juice is such that it pulls the illness out from under both sides, as we have said;
et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus .i. siege,	and let the master be standing above the head of the patient, and the patient sitting on a chair,
puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est;	then close the vein tightly, then open it a little widely, then draw blood moderately, as needed;
puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement,	then tie off the other vein, then untie it, and gently press both veins,
que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	and let the patient not be strangled; and leave it until the morning, so that the wound is healed.
De la sainie des leivres	Of the bleeding of the lips
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The healing of veins on the lips helps with sores in the mouth, and gum decay, and splitting of the lips, and toothache and gum pain.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit;	And the qualities of the healing are to have the patient sit before you, and stretch his neck as I have said;
puis torne la levre, et regarde as .ij. voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre,	then turn the lip, and look at two veins, one on the right lip and the other on the left;
et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires:	and recognize them by their being black, and by there being thin black veins around them:
cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance,	deal with them both; and if you do not know them, and you are in doubt,
si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des .ij. voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	then deal with the largest of each side, and do the same with the two veins that are above and below; for it is the same procedure.
De la sainie desoz la lengue	Bleeding under the tongue:
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche;	Bleeding from the veins under the tongue helps after bleeding from the head, and it is for the constriction of the throat, and for diseases of the eye, and for diseases of the mouth;
et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire:	and the qualities of the bleeding are such that the patient cuts between their fingers in front of the sun, and lifts up their tongue, and looks under each side for a black vein:
saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	Therefore bleed both sides, but do not go too deep, as there are arteries underneath.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc .ij. manieres:	The veins from which one bleeds commonly are bled in two ways:
ou em poignant a tout .i. flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»;	or with a sharp silver needle, or a fine olive-wood point, and is called «aniseed»;
et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	and are broad and narrow according to the breadth and狭nessof the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The form of the flame of myrrh is highly renowned, and it is broad as you can see:
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble;	And it is necessary to open the veins that are smooth and full of gross and troubled blood;
et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	and the form of the flame is like an olive:
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	is more pointed and is for bleeding the veins, where there is thin yellow blood.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre;	The basil vein, which is one of these veins, helps diseases that are below the throat, and in the neck, and in the chest, and in the belly;
et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	and the bleeder must bleed freely, and be wary of the artery below.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit;	And if he hits the artery, and there is a gushing of blood, then he must stanch it, as I have said;
et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	and the flame must not be gripping, but cutting like a scythe.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre;	And if the basil does not open clearly, then you must stretch it and change to another;
ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement;	or you can pierce a vein in his arm: it will open clearly;
et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	and apply the flame like a scythe, as we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz;	And if you wish to find the site of the bleeding, then you must stretch out the arm, feeling the area until you find the pulse;
puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil;	then sign the spot with a mark, and then tie off the vein above the flame, and stop the bleeding.
et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	And beware of cutting into an artery when you see the spot pulsing; that is an artery, so avoid it.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere:	And if you see it flowing upwards like a child's urine, and the blood is red and thin, know that this is blood from an artery;
haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient;	hurry therefore, and put your finger on it for a long time, then remove your finger if the bleeding stops, which often happens.
se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	bind the arm and leave it thus, and do not move it until the patient is healed, and let him be on guard and not move it until he is cured.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	And if the bleeding is not stopped and he faints, and medicine is not at hand, then press on the artery until it stops, for that is where the blood flows from; and stop the bleeding.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor;	And take a piece of fistice, split it in half, and bind the wound tightly with one half until the next day;
se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc;	if it stops the bleeding, that is good; if not, then treat it with the powders which stop bleeding, as we have said.
et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	and the bandages are not too tight in many positions due to the small size of the wound, and the strength of the arm.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz,	The vein's bleeding is helped if it draws blood from the head above and from the body below,
por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit;	because it is made up of basilic and cephalic veins, as we have said;
et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf,	and the surgeon must be careful not to cut too deeply into the nerve below, and if he cuts it,
et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner;	it will inflame and harm the patient, and perhaps they cannot heal.
et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	And this nerve opens in many people, and if it doesn't open in some due to its subtlety, then you must heal it with the instrument gently; and avoid harming the nerve as best you can.
Et se il a voinne entre les .ij. ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if there is a vein between the two nerves, they should cut it lengthwise.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz;	The bloodletting of the head helps if it draws blood from the head, and helps the eyes.
et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	and it is necessary to bleed with a flame of olive oil or a flame of myrtle, because it is the safest of all veins, because there are no nerves or arteries underneath it.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence;	Nevertheless, one should seek the lightest place, and not worry if one fails the first time, and one can try again.
et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	and perhaps it inflames the area in some men, when they fail the first time, but it does not worry them.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of healing depends on your thoughts.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit,	The first thing you need to know about healing is that it isn't just about curing disease but also about maintaining health.
et por eschuir les maladies a venir;	and preventing diseases from occurring;
et soit li sainie faite en l’une des .iij. voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique;	and it can be performed in one of three ways: through the head, stomach, or feet;
et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent;	and one must bleed in the beginning of spring, and in autumn and winter after eating, when the signs of fullness appear.
et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés .ij. houres ou .iij. dou jor.	and one must bleed the first or third day, after two hours or three days.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens;	The bleeding which is administered for diseases has no specific time, but when the need arises during the day or night, at any time and at all times.
et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a .xiiij. ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	and one must not bleed children until they are 14 years old, nor a woman carrying a child until the fourth month up to the seventh month.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez .lx. ans.	No one should bleed those who are older than sixty years.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier,	And when anyone wants to be bled, in any manner, it is necessary that he cleanse the intestines with a gentle enema,
s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz;	if he has accumulated feces, so that the veins do not draw harmful excesses from the intestines to the principal members;
ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques;	do not bleed those who are too full from eating meat, nor those who are drunk, until they have sobered up;
et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors;	and if anyone has a colic after pain, vomiting, diarrhea, and frequent intercourse with a woman, and from hard work, staying up all night, fasting, or injury to the body or soul;
puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir;	then subtly modify their humor if it is thick, through food and drink and medicine, if you have the ability;
puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc,	then take a bath if nothing else helps to thin out the blood;
et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit;	and treat the vein around the navel as we have said;
et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses;	and guard against that day of labour, pain, and lust, and similar things;
et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras .ij. fois ou .iij.,	and be bound and joyful, and let the surgeon be higher than those being treated, and rub the arm two or three times;
puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans;	then tighten the ligature above the vein, for if it is too loose or too tight, it cannot work;
et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on;	and then rub the area with the hands until the veins swell and can be felt;
puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier,	then moisten the bandage with the flame of a little old oil, then place your left-hand finger on that vein below the spot where you want to apply the cautery,
que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	so that the vein does not move and escape from the cauterisation.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit,	For there are veins which flow like cords when cauterised, and others which are full of wind,
si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus;	so that when one applies the flame, they withdraw from the heat and cannot open the vein, and thus it is with some people;
et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	and if he opens the vein, then the wound is too tight, so it is necessary that the surgeons be advised about these things.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	And if the vein opens the first time, it is good; but if not, open it again a little lower down or up above, depending on which way the vein is going, if the skin is not swollen.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse .i. jor ou .ij., et ne liier mie le bras:	And if the skin is swollen and the patient is frightened, let him go for a day or two without binding the arm:
par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait;	Perhaps hot abscesses will form; do not enter the bath, then restart the bleeding if she wishes;
et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement;	and if the holes are small, then cut the skin around it carefully and you doubt that not so much blood will come out as you see, then apply the flame directly to that hole;
et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	and work on it a little gently, so that the wound is not swollen; for this often happens when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile;	If you see the area swollen, do not restart the bleeding, and place a little lamb's wool soaked in oil on it, for oil lightens the body of blood, and is beneficial in this case where oil is concerned.
et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc;	And thus administer lamb's wool soaked in oil with every bleeding that you bleed the veins to stop the flow of blood;
et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	and it makes a triacle and bowels of them when one places it on the spot; so subtly does it draw out the poison when it is too large.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite,	And if there are large abscesses, which often happen, especially when there was no bleeding before the opening of the vein is small,
si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre;	if you are in a hurry, and place a moist sponge in warm water on the spot and hold it for an hour;
et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie;	and you should do this after the bleeding from the vein, and if it remains in place for several days with some blackness or greenness, it does not harm him;
et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	and if you see it, place on it something of aloe or myrrh mixed with medicine, ointment, or similar.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	And many times abscesses and appearances arise from the bleeding of the basilic vein; therefore place your hand upon it, and if you find the place soft to the touch, then that appearance is bad.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere; mais li fai .i. emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Avoid putting anything we have mentioned on it, however, for it might come from an artery; instead, make a dry poultice to harden the area, then treat the wound with another treatment until it heals.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And treat each wound according to its nature and the color of the blood.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	Because if the pus is black, let it flow out until it turns red; and if you see it is thick, let it flow until it becomes thin; and if it is too hot, let it cool down.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges;	And for those who are swollen and bloated, and need bloodletting, make the wound larger, and let the blisters be wide.
et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant;	And for those who are weak, do the opposite, and let them be bled less and often, and they should be bled by cutting across, not by pricking;
et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	and this method of bleeding is safe from bloodletting and cutting of nerves, and it is better than bleeding from the long or the wide vein.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates; s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc .iij. fois ou .iiij.	And to one whose body needs cleansing, give moist bread in pomegranate juice; if he is scorched, then draw out blood three or four times.
Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	And if he has a cold complexion, before the cleansing give moist bread in muscat-flavored syrup, or aromatic honey syrup with spices like pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and chicory, and pleasantly scented syrup.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil,	And if he faints during the cleansing, after losing a lot of blood, he should breathe in the fumes of warm meat broth and subtle aromatic syrup,
et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	and use the other things we have described in the section on syncope for opening veins.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if he wants to open his arm and bleed again, when it is weakened by heavy bleeding, he should bleed slowly according to the amount of his strength continuously.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine .vij. houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And whoever wants to open his arm after the first bleeding, and he has a strong pulse, let him bleed seven hours after the first bleeding or after the ninth hour.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And whoever wants to bleed elsewhere, let him bleed on the second or third day.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre; si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson;	Because there is a lot of blood in the body that has been heated and causes fever; so one must draw out a large quantity and enlarge the vein until it bleeds into the palm.
puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson,	then you must examine all signs of healing, and place your hand over the patient's pulse when it is healing, so that death does not come from a lack of blood flow.
et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens;	and this often happens when the healer is negligent;
et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus;	and you must not press firmly on a closed wound when you see the arm dislocating and blood emerging a second time;
ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz;	nor if it is crooked and the patient extends their arm suddenly, for that would be harmful;
mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois; ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer,	but let it grow back a second time; or poke the tip of the flame into the vein until the congelation at its opening melts away.
et met sus .i. poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	and place on it .a. little wool saturated in vinegar, and press gently.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the vein is swollen, leave it and do not bind it, until the abscess is relieved.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if it is necessary to draw blood a second time, then let him bleed in the same vein, or in another vein, or in the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	Veins in the arm are healthy at the site of the vein in the head because it is composed.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges;	And the manner of healing is for the patient to place his hand in hot water until the vein turns red:
puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc;	Then let him move it gently so that the vein appears well, then heal it from the top, not from the broad or long side;
et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez;	and the hole should be wide, and heal it well near the joint of the hand, and if it cannot issue, then put the hand back in hot water, and let the blood flow into the water until you have enough;
et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit;	and if it is winter, do not soak the hand in hot water, for we put it there more in winter than in summer.
et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	and the bleeding of this vein is safer than all other veins, as there are no arteries or nerves in it.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere:	The bleeding of the right hand's salvatele vein is good for all diseases of the liver, and this is how to do it:
estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie;	Apply pressure to the hand and soak it in hot water until the vein swells up, as one will see.
et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien;	and if it heals crookedly, and you cut it from all sides, then it will not hurt.
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char,	and do not go too deep, because the nerves are completely exposed underneath the skin,
et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	and then put the hand in hot water if the pain is frozen in the wound, and it cannot come out.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have bled as much as is necessary, then put oil and silk on the vein to close it up, and do the same for each vein.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The surgery of the left hand is similar to that of the right hand, and you should do everything as I told you about the right side.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors,	The surgery of the shoulder is used for all diseases under the chest,
si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	including diseases of the breast, and retention of fluids, and diseases of the kidneys, and of the hips and legs, and similar diseases.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere,	And the nature of its surgery is such that the patient puts his foot in warm water and rubs the wound until it breaks open,
et lie desus la jointure dou piet; et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains;	and lies above the joint of the foot; and if the vein is at the ankle, then it goes above the foot in many small veins;
saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	then heal it at the largest vein, or at the ankle, whichever is better.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant; et soit li flaimes anesil.	And if you heal it on the foot, then guard against the nerves that are underneath, and heal it across as well as up and down; and let the flames be anointed.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if the blood cannot come out, then put the foot in water, and let the vein drain well.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz;	And if the sutures come apart the first time, then sew them again the second time a little higher up, for the wounds are salty.
ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	Do not doubt about the nerve, as we have said, and likewise do to the other foot equally.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The location of the sciatic vein is at the ankle, and its treatment helps with hip pain when it is due to hot blood.
