Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville .iiij. dois en tordant,	And its quality of treatment is that the patient lies on their back, and stretches his leg straight upwards. Then he twists the leg two times in a winding motion.
car autrement n’apert li voinne; et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant;	for otherwise it does not open; and if it opens, then heal it in every way you can, and by crossing over;
et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	and it is better that you cover it, for the place is safe, and it is very vulnerable to many people.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners;	And if you do not treat it, then heal any vein that opens on the back of the foot, and towards the little toe, and be careful of the nerves;
et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint; ele est maintenant sanee.	and make the blood flow as much as you want, and then untie the ligature, and put on cotton and compress it; it is now healed.
Des sainies de ventouse	Of bleeding with leeches
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc .ij. manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	Leeches are made of horns, or brass, or glass; and bleeding is done in two ways: either by striking and drawing blood, or without striking.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc .ij. manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu;	And this bleeding without striking is in two ways: either it is all fire, or without fire;
et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en .xiiij. leus dou cors,	and bleeding that is done by striking and drawing blood is done in 14 parts of the body,
de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col;	from which one is all in the head; and the other is in the neck;
et .ij. autres en .ij. costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton;	and two others on both sides of the neck; and the cupping glasses under the chin;
et li ventouse des .ij. espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies;	and the cupping glasses on the shoulders; and the cupping glasses above the kidneys;
et les ventouses emmi les .ij. bras; et les ventouses des .ij. jambes;	and the cupping glasses in both arms; and the cupping glasses in both legs;
et les ventouses des .ij. chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char,	and the leeches from the two ankles; and the blood-letting does not treat blood, except for small veins that are scattered in the body,
et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne;	and therefore it weakens them no more, as they do through blood-letting from veins;
et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	and it should not be administered, neither on fire nor with fire, in any illness that comes from fullness, until the whole body is emptied.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens;	And if by necessity of illnesses we need to blood-let, or due to habits, then we administer it every hour in the beginning of the month, or at the end, and in between and in each time;
car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief;	for there are some who, when they need to belch, have a heavy head.
et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz;	and some who experience bloating and redness in their face, head, and neck, and darkness in their eyes;
et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc;	and some who have a drop of blood in their mouth, and have a swollen tongue, and bleed;
et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	and there are some who dream, and see by night bleeding wounds and pain and death and similar things.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés .iij. houres dou jor.	And when we see these signs, especially if it is in the middle of the month, we command him to be bled after three hours of day.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors;	Bleeding the nose helps with headaches ... that comes to the eyes, and it should not be after the evacuation of the whole body;
et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique,	and this bleeding is in the place of the headache,
et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement;	and it should not be used by those of a cold complexion, or who have catarrh, because it does them great harm;
et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	and for this reason, the elderly should not use it, nor those with cold diseases in their heads.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And those who often heal themselves become oblivous, and because of this, the leech must place the cupping jar a little lower down to avoid oblivousness.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis,	Cupping on the neck is in the place of healing from the head and basil, and for this reason, it is useful for constriction of the feet,
et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion;	and for splitting of the channel of the lung, and for coughing, and for retention;
et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	and it must be pushed gently, because if it is held too tightly, it injures the stomach or heart.
Li ventosations as .ij. costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens,	Ventilation from the two ribs on the neck is good for headaches, and for pain in the eyes and brain, and for strangulation, and for toothache.
et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	It is located in the basilic vein; and you must instruct the surgeon to express his hand when inserting it, so that he does not press on the artery and cause a bleeding of blood.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des .ij. levres.	Ventilation below the chin is good for mouth diseases, and for gum corruption, and similar diseases that are in the mouth; and it is located in the area of the veins of the two lips.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	The windings of the shoulders are effective for diseases that come from heat and fullness.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des .iij. voinnes dou bras,	The windings of the armpits are also as effective as three veins in the arm,
car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes;	because it draws blood from these large veins;
et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	and instruct the patient not to cut too deeply, for the area is naked of flesh and has nerves and arteries underneath.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	The cupping glass which is placed on the buttocks is good for hemorrhoids and diseases below, and it must be a large one made of copper, which needs to be carefully handled; otherwise, if it were thin, it would break and cause great wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des .ij. sophenes, et des .ij. chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	Cupping glasses on the legs heal quickly, as they attract blood from throughout the body and are beneficial for old pains in the joints, the hips, and the bladder, and bring relief to flowers; they are placed at the inside of the thighs and ankles, and even though they weaken the body after prolonged use, they bring relief in various conditions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	The method of placing the cupping glass is to first put it on empty, then suck gently, place it firmly, and move it evenly, and do not stop doing this until you see the area turn red and swollen, and the redness of the blood appears; then pause, remove the cupping glasses, and take care in the disposition of the body, for there are those with thin skin and large pores: therefore, one should suck only once, and make wide and somewhat deep wounds, and suck gently.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir .ij. fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	And if the blood is thick, it is necessary to suck twice: the first time to make the path for the thick blood.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	And if the vein is very thick, it must be pricked a third time; and when we want to draw a little blood, we only prick once.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement,	And if we want a lot of blood, we prick repeatedly; and if the vein is thick, we pierce it deeply, and the ends are such that the skin is suddenly pierced,
et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif:	and it is appropriate for those who have thick and tough skin, and who have small pores, that you grease the places of the leeches with an aperitif and dissolving oil:
se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite;	if it is in the state of violets, of sweet almond oil, or of pumpkin seed oil;
et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	and if it is on an artery, with oil of watercress, or of lily, or of chamomile, or similar.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the swelling is large and cold, take oil of marjoram, or of balsamite, or oil of aniseed, and similar oils.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile,	And if one is healing a wound in soft flesh with wide pores, no oil should be used,
mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	but if the swelling is hot and dry, then take oil of fenugreek, or linseed oil, or oil of Saint John's Wort, or oil of blackberry, or similar. But it should be washed after fomentation with rosewater, or cold water, or water of sorrel, or water of porcelain, or similar.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And those who have a lot of moisture, if they rise from bed, or water of myrrh, and of sumac, and similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans;	And those with large sores rise from old wine, or water of vinegar, or a decoction of fennel or chamomile, or other similar things;
et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou .ij.; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion,	and should not be bled with a cupping glass before the bath or em-bath, but after the bath an hour or two; and should not sleep after the bleeding,
et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	and it is necessary that he be careful when he is to be bled and when he has been bled.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez;	And guard against those who are choleric, and if their blood is too hot and inflamed;
si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses;	if they should eat cool things, like pomegranates and endives and lettuce with garlic, and similar things;
et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	and drink buttermilk, and meat juices, and moist meats.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons;	And those who have a cold complexion should drink honey syrup, and moderate aged wine, and meat juices, and buttermilk, and small birds and pigeons;
et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier;	and on the day he is bled, he must drink more than eat.
et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz;	and it is necessary to give certain people a small amount of triacle or musk before or after the bleeding to strengthen the main organs.
et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	Dilute the wine, but those who are hot-tempered should not drink it.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz,	The leeches that are used to cause bleeding are those that are placed on the liver, and the mouse, and podagra, and on the stomach and the gut, and the flanks, because these members cannot withstand bleeding on the eyes.
et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre,	and is done only to attract blood from one limb to another,
si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus lou ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre;	as we put leeches on the breasts when the nipples are sore; to reduce swelling in a limb, as we apply cupping to the abdomen and chest;
et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu;	and removes pain, when there is obstruction or stone, and by its attractive power perhaps dispels the obstruction or ejects the stone from its place;
et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue,	and it does the same when applied to the liver and spleen when there is retained wind,
et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede,	and these cupping glasses are administered empty to suck only; and sometimes they are administered with fire, and sometimes filled with tepid water,
si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	as in diseases of the lungs, and in such a way one fills the cupping glass with hot water, or with water in which suitable herbs have been boiled.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The shape of the cupping glass administered with fire is as follows:
Et ait .ij. dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu .i. petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille,	And it has 2 inches of width and half a palm of depth, and it has on the side all around in the middle a small hole, as well as for pushing through an awl,
et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre;	and is of iron, carefully heated so that it does not burn the patient when placed on the limb;
et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise,	and in its center has a bent rod of iron or steel, to hold a candle,
et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent;	and are both large and small according to the illnesses and ages of those who take them;
car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	because children's ventouses are different from adults', and thin people's from fat people's.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre:	And one must then place this cupping glass over the limb:
empren la chandoile de cire ou .i. linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse,	take the wax candle or a liniment, and place it inside the cupping glass through the tube which is inside the cupping glass,
si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide;	so that the flame is at the bottom of the cupping glass so that it does not burn the patient;
et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse;	and then place it over the limb, and your fingers should be over the hole that we have mentioned, so that when one wishes, the vapors will go in and out, and one removes the cupping glass;
et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	and apply the poultice as before, and reapply it frequently if necessary.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement;	In the cupping glass which is administered for pneumonia, for any acute disease, there is neither a tube nor an opening, and it is not removed until it is full of water, and is placed on the body only in this way:
et c’est li forme:	and its shape is:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus;	Leeches are not removed until they are placed in parts where cupping glasses cannot be used due to their small size, such as the lips and gums, and similar places;
et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans;	and in their naked flesh, as in the case of wounds or sores, and other similar afflictions;
et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren;	and the quality of the leeches is such that when you find those that are in clean, fresh water without mud, then take them;
et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres;	and put them in clean water for as long as they are hungry and have nothing in their bellies;
et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues;	and then cleanse the wound and use a cupping glass, then rub the member until it turns red, and put the leeches on it;
et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	and when they are flat and swollen, if it is in a place where one can put a cupping glass, one should do so, because it helps a lot afterwards.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint;	If not, then raise the area above, and then with water, very well, and then squeeze it out;
et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille .i. drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés;	and if the area around the bite is swelling too much after the body of the snake, then soak .i. linen cloth in cold water and place it over the bite until the swelling goes down;
et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez;	and if the bites are multiple, then apply ground vitriol, or gall, and similar substances, until the swelling goes down;
ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant;	or you put raw peas on the spot, leaving them until they adhere to the wound, which will now stop bleeding.
et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	and if you need more, take some leeches.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse,	And if the leeches won't attach, then rub the wound with fresh blood, or pierce it with a needle so that some blood comes out,
et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent;	and then place them on the wound, and as soon as they smell the blood, they will attach.
et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	and when you see them defecating, then powder on a little aloe and salt, or ashes, and they will stop now.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	Here begins the book of fractures
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is often necessary in the art of medicine, and is for the restoration of fractures and dislocations.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent;	Know, dear son, that the foolish people are talking about this chapter, which they have never seen in any ancient books or letters;
et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin;	and for this reason medicine is strangers to our land, for I have never found any good ones there;
et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie;	and I know nothing about it, except through the study of ancient books, in which I have studied so much that I have attained knowledge, and through experimentation, and through my own experiences in life;
et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces .ij. chapistres ci devant.	and I have described for you in this chapter what is contained in it, and have summarized it at the end, and have clearly shown the forms of the instruments that are used, just as I have done in these two previous chapters.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	Therefore, we should say in the prologue of this book the summaries of the matters and the chapters, so that those who are experienced may know and learn this noble art, and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars;	I say that when a fracture or dislocation or twisting or break occurs in anyone, you must hurry to heal the patient on both sides, if anything doesn't hold him back, such as weakness of the body, or old age;
ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	or if the weather is very hot or very cold; and eat cool foods, namely cold meats, and deer and rabbit meat, and do not drink any wine, nor consume any fatty foods, and do not fill yourself too much with foods that fill the veins with blood, until you have suspected a hot abscess, or the spreading of matter in the limb; then return to the patient's previous course of treatment.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken bones begin to heal, then one should nourish the patient with foods that promote swelling or粘稠度(viscosity), such as cooked wheat in water, rice, testes, feet, pig's stomach, ox's maw, fresh fish, and full-bodied wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For the body swells more quickly with moisture.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans;	And know that broken bones of the old and decrepit cannot be well set and joined according to their nature because of the dryness of the members, nor those which are also too tender, such as the bones of small children;
mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet .i. gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	but have no cure, reset the broken bone with a large tendon which stretches and joins the limb together, as much as it enforced before; and do not stop at all in his work, and for this he must nourish on coarse meats, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And you know that fractures are diverse in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the fracture of the head is different from that of the foot, or of the leg, and I will tell you in this chapter all types of fractures.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	Because there is a break that goes to the root, and another in sharpening, like the tip of a feather for writing.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And if there is a break with a wound, and a break throughout a small split.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu;	And each way has its own technique and proper instrument for restoration, according to what memory comes to mind in its place;
et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main;	and it is understood that the break of the bone is due to twisting, and it is evident by displacement, and sounds when pressed with the hand;
et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure;	and when there is no crookedness or swelling, and the patient does not feel great pain, then there is no fracture.
mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	but it can still have crookedness, or a split, or a small fracture.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	You should not move it with your hand, but put on the medicines that come below, and then hold it firmly and gently.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les .ij. parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne;	And you should know that the fracture that goes into the bone, and are the two disjoined parts, they must now be put back together evenly, just as with abscesses.
et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez;	and if cold abscesses come, let it remain for a day until the abscesses are relieved;
puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	then reset it gently and quickly, and know that the restoration of this one is easier than that of the one with parts; then hold it as it should be held afterwards.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de .ij. pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a .ij. cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main;	And if in the bone there are broken pieces, then stretch with two parts, if it is a hand or foot, or with one hand if it is a small member, or with two cords, or with one cord and the hand:
et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor;	and set the limb according to its natural shape, so that when the broken parts of the limb are separated, you must use all your skill to put the additions in their places as much as you can, and be careful that your work does not cause injury or pain to the patient.
et ajoste bien les .ij. chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	and align the two heads of the bone according to the best forms.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	And feel it with your hand whether it seems well or not; then adjust it nicely, and do not strain it too much or press it as those who cause hot abscesses and contractions in the limb through their work, as we have seen many times.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere;	And when the limb is set right, then instruct the patient carefully not to move it, not while waking or sleeping, not turning or in any other way;
et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	and make sure the limb is so secure that it feels no pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor;	For when he feels no pain at all, then he is not in any pain, and you should put him in such a position that he feels no pain;
et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez;	and be sure that he is placed straight, so that no crookedness comes when he is restored;
et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	and the quality of the broken member is according to what I tell you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	You know that broken bones are diverse in size, length, and shape.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz;	For there are small members like fingers, toes, and similar: it is necessary to wrap these with soft, thin linen.
et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche;	And for larger members like thighs and legs: it is necessary to wrap these with a wide, sturdy linen, as the wide linen wraps all around the large member and constricts it evenly all over, so that there is no swelling.
puis lie entor estoupes legieres, .iij. tours ou iiij. selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure;	Then tie around it light bandages, 3 or 4 times depending on the member, and tighten your hand a little at each of the bandages, then go above the break and loosen it less, so that the break is then moved away a little.
et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren .i. autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet;	and soften the ligament little by little, until you grasp a large part of the healthy joint, then take another ligament, and turn around directly on the broken joint;
puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus;	then go to the part below the break, and tighten it gently, not too hard or too gently, as we have said in the first hour above;
puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus .i. bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	then place between the ligaments, stuffed with flax or cloth, until it is all even, then tie it all up with a bandage above, and then put your splints on well, if there is no abscess or swelling.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors;	And if there is an abscess or swelling, then put something hot on the abscess that removes the swelling, and leave it for several days;
puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	then hold them over the fires, and let them be of half a cane’s length, wet with blood, or of wood used for making spades, or of palm fronds, and let them be in this shape:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres;	but it is necessary that the fire brand which one places over the break should be a little larger and wider than the others;
et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor;	and it should also be as long as it is appropriate for the limb in terms of its smallness or greatness;
puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure;	then hold them over the fires as you did at first, then tie a string on tightly, just as in the first instance on the dislocation;
plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol;	the tighter it is bound, the more it eases; and the thread should be medium-sized, not too thick or too thin, and it should be made of soft flax;
car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	because if the thread is thick, as I have often seen fools make their strings by twisting the flax, and this is a great error, for the string cannot be even if it is too thin, and there should not be less than two threads between each eye.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patient is sore under the eyes after the dislocation in their healthy state, then place beneath them linseed poultices or soft lambswool so that it does not break.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is with the fracture and the vein is broken, I will describe its treatment below.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And you shall know that it is not right to pull out all the broken members on the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés .v. jors ou .vij., ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant;	For when the member is large, it should not be put in splints until after five or seven days, or more depending on your assessment of the hot abscess;
et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	and here is the way of the ancient plaster for restoring broken bones, dislocation, and torsion: you should take flour that is held in the walls of the mill, and cook it with plenty of eggs, and apply this preparation, neither too thin nor too thick, and use it. This is the common way of the plaster that restores broken bones in various conditions, especially for women and small children, because it is not too hot or too cold.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana .x. З.; mirre et aloes, ana .v. З.; alechil .viiij. З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	Another way of plaster that restores broken bones and dislocation and torsion: take 3 grams of absinthe, and ladani, and enule, and asafoetida, and gum arabic, and mastic, each 10 grams; myrrh and aloes, each 5 grams; alechimic 8 grams. Make these into a powder and mix them with plenty of eggs; if the person's complexion is hot, use this plaster, because it is of good composition and restores broken bones quickly, and it is useful for many people.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana .x. З.; mirre et aloes, ana .viiij. З.; acaice vi. З.; bolic armenic .x. З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Another method of plaster that is useful for twisting: take mugwort and viscum, each .10; myrrh and aloes, each .8; acacia gum .6; Armenian bole .10, and grind well, and confit with water or egg white, and administer it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu. Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	Another method of plaster for joints and where the bones are dislocated from their sockets, and to soothe the resulting pain, and reduce swelling: take lamb's wool, soak it in oil and cook it, and apply it to the affected area. These plasters do not heal, but they are good for soothing hot abscesses and reducing pain.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Another method of plaster that heals broken bones: take dry fig leaves and earthworm leaves, grind them together, and make a plaster from them.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme. Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	Another method of plaster for healing broken bones and reducing swelling: take marsh mallow root, chamomile, violet flowers, and wheat flour, one part each; grind them together, and confit with wine. If the area is inflamed, confit with coriander water or water.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre. Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	Another method of plaster is stronger than the first, when a hard abscess comes to the restoration of the member. Take roots of viscumsalve, and seeds of flax, bastard-balm, melilot, and sanserica, and flowers of violets and camomile, of each one part; and bruise, and cook with water of salt, or sweet water, or with wine, according to the heat of the member, and its rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Hypocrites says in his book that one should not put anything on a broken member to restore it except for cerate made of wax and oil, and nothing else, and he says that it should be between two things, neither too soft nor too hard.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And it seems that Galen says that one should put on a broken member, to restore it, dry things slightly warm, such as myrrh and aloe and incense and similar things, as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Another method of plaster that is good for injury and pain: take mugwort and lamb's tail, or owl feathers, and viscumsalve, and salt equally, and bruise them, and make plaster and lie in it.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors	And then loosen it a little after, and be careful that the patient does not feel any pain, nor has the bone moved from its place; if so, loosen it by hand again.
Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor;	And if pain comes to the area, or itching, discomfort or swelling, then hurry and loosen it, and remove the plaster now; and take light cloth, and sponge of the sea moistened, and dip in water, and apply to the area until the itching ceases, and the pain is relieved;
puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut;	then let the limb rest for an hour, then apply a dry bandage, moistened in water or rose oil, and bind it up on a splint, until you are sure of hot abscesses;
et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	and reduce the inflammation of the limb, and let the pain subside, then restart the gentle stretching, and a little of the plaster, and do not stretch it as hard as before; and gently until it is healed.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that the abscess is hot and red and painful and swollen, take it all out, and you need to apply a poultice and a bandage, and do this again as you did before.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés .iij. jors ou .iiij. ou .v. ou .vij.; et aucune fois le laisse .xx. jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus;	And if nothing of what we have said happens to the limb, do not remove the bandage for 3 or 4 or 5 or 7 days, and sometimes leave it for 20 days, depending on how long it takes for the fracture to heal and the bone to come close to the skin;
adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir;	then tighten it more than before, and the meat will grow larger, as I said before. And if you see that the area is drying out more than it should, know that nourishment cannot reach it;
arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure;	then wash it with warm water every time you remove the bandage, and do this every third day, and loosen the bandage a little each time;
par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	through this work, therefore, shorten the growth in the limb, and gently mend what the foolish do, that they restore the limb crookedly: it is bad, and such work is cowardly, and I see no good in it except to tire oneself and do it properly.
des diverses manieres de brisure	of the various methods of fracture
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees;	Many types of fractures are there, with diverse shapes, and the causes are distinct.
car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	for there are fractures that are made by the impact of a sword, and the collarbone breaks right up to the syfac which is under the bone, as with an axe or staff; and this type of fracture is called a "haichure".
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces .ij. brisures grans ou petite.	Or the sword strikes the bone from above without piercing it, and this type of fracture is called "absolute"; and the wound of these two fractures can be large or small.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is a closed fracture, or a split, or from the impact of stone, or from falling on stone, or other similar injuries.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if there is a penetrating fracture, which approaches the membrane below the bone, or it is on top of the bone, and this wound can be large or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»;	And if there is a wound that is embedded in the bone as thin as a hair, and the fracture is small, then this type of fracture is called "capillary".
et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	and if the wound is made by a stone, or by falling, or by a similar object, and the bone enters below, and the place is shaved as the blacksmiths do when they work on kettles; then the stone enters inside.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant;	And this happens more to those who have soft bone at the top, such as children's heads;
et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	and it happens in all these ways of breaking that small pieces are dislodged, as in the case of splinters; and I will speak about this later.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And let us know all the ways of breaking by examination, and by corruption of the flesh that is above it.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The hair-like appearance is discovered when one uncovers the bone and rubs it, then the black crack becomes visible.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the treatment of fractures, be aware of accidental illnesses, and if you see any harmful events such as vomiting bile, loss of consciousness, extension, palpitations, fever, eyes popping out and turning red, and other similar symptoms in various conditions, then it cannot heal without a doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you do not see a surprising accident and you hope for healing, then begin the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the newborn comes to you first, and it is in winter, then it is necessary to remove the bone before the fourteenth day that you can.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it is in this state, then you must hasten to remove the bone before the seventh day, so that the membrane under the bone is not corrupted, and the accidents we have described do not occur.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues,	And if the fracture of the bone reaches the membrane that covers the brain, then you should split the fractured part thus: and you must press the head of the injured person, and expose above the bone in all ways that you can, and over the shape of the wound more gently than you can.
et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset;	and if bleeding occurs when exposing the bone, or pus forms, then treat it with what is appropriate, and you must fill the wound with moist bandages in rose oil;
et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc .ij. manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	and let the wound rest until the pus is relieved and bleeding stopped; then begin around the bone to remove, and it is done according to 2 methods of treatment: one method is that you cut with a narrow chisel in front, and that is the shape:
Et puis i boute .i. autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then he puts in another stitch larger than the first.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	And the second method is that you should have various different stitches, some narrow and some wide, and they should be pointed and made of iron; and work quickly so that you do not pierce the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou .i. cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des .iij. manieres de tareres:	And if the bone is thick and hard, then you should pierce it all around, so that you can use stitches with awls, not going deeper than the bone of the skull; and it must have a rim or circle on top so that the point does not go beyond the bone. You should have several of these so that each one goes into the thickness of the bone, and you will need awls for all parts of the skull. There are three types of awls:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes .i. tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	The quality for piercing around the broken bone is to place an awl on the bone and turn it with your fingers until you feel that the bone is pierced; then move the awl to another place a little later, and continue all around. Then use the chisels to chip away at the space between the fragments of bone, doing this as skillfully and gently as you can, as we have said, so that you draw out the bone with your hand or with one of the tools you are using, like tweezers or pincers; be careful not to touch the brain or the sinuses.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout .i. autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire;	And when you have pierced and treated the bone, it is fitting that you cut away the sharpness which remains on the bone with any other tool resembling an incisor, but it must be more blunt and thinner than the others.
et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a .i. des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	If anything remains of the small bones or any chips, remove them gently with one of the tools; then dress the wound as we have described.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And another way of doing it which is safer, according to Galen, who praised it highly, is as follows:
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	First, you must expose a part of the bone where the broken bone is visible, so that when you have exposed that part, you will place under the head of this incisor, a lenticular shape, which is its form:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en .ij. costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz;	And do not cut from one side, and the part is painful on both sides, so that the cutting is towards the bone; then strike with a small mallet upwards, so that you gently strike the bone all around, and take good care of the membrane that is underneath;
s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	if it is adhered to the bone, then loosen the bone slightly, for one can loosen the bone without harm, and without fear.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if the fracture of the bone does not penetrate to the membrane, and the bone is cut only slightly on top, and there are small pieces, then one must smooth that roughness, and remove the shards with a very thin rasp, of which you should have various sizes, in order to apply the most suitable one according to the work and the shape of the fracture.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	Take first a large rasp, and then a finer one, and do not cease doing this until it is well done.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	In each of the other haircuts and subtle breaks, you must minister according to its nature; and this is not answered by one who has devoted his study to this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes .i. drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie;	And if the wound is exposed, you should place a linen cloth over it, according to the size of the wound, and moisten it in rosemary oil, and apply it to the wound.
puis pren .i. autre drapeil doublé en .ij. ou en .iij., et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus .i. autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement;	Then take another folded cloth in two or three layers, moisten it in wine and rosemary oil, and place it over the first cloth; and do this as gently as you can so that you do not put too much pressure on the wound, then apply a bandage over it, and do not tighten it more than necessary so that it only holds the wound.
et le laisse ensi .i. jor ou .ij., tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication;	Let it remain like this for one or two days until the abscesses are relieved, then remove it and apply medicinal herbs such as lily roots, and wheat flour, and incense powder, and aristolochia, and similar things; make a powder from these things and apply it to the wound, and then apply other medicines without biting.
et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	And be sure that the wound is clean, so that you do not leave any ointment on it, or let anything stick to it, for when something sticks to the brain membrane, it rots and causes great harm to the patient; for when one applies something biting to the brain, it pierces through.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Therefore, take care that no evil accident happens to the patient as we have said, for it is certain without a doubt.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et .iij. parties d’oile roset et en glue .i. drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac;	And if blackness does not come from the medicine that is applied, but rather by some other cause, then you should take some honey and mix it with three parts of rose oil, and apply this mixture to the wound.
puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then treat the wound in the usual way until it is healed.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les .ij. parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont .ij. os; et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	Know that sometimes the two parts of the upper jaw are broken, one alone or both, for they are two bones; and the one underneath is cartilaginous, and does not break but only dislocates or twists, and then heals.
Et se l’une des .ij. parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil;	And if one of the two parts is broken, you should place your little finger or a tube in the nostril and press the break evenly with your index finger and thumb until the nose returns to its natural shape.
et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	And do this gently, and be careful that the patient does not feel pain from your action.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if the break is in the upper part of the nose, and you cannot reach it with your fingers, you should place it at the end of a thick piece of wood.
Et se li brisure est de .ij. pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues;	And if the fracture is of two parts, do likewise, and hasten to restore it on the first day, if you can;
se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	if not, after the seventh or tenth day, when the abscesses have healed, then tie to the head of the bone tent-like pieces of linen cloth, if the fracture is in one part.
Ou tu boutes .i. autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est; et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	Or you tie one to each side of the bone, if the fracture is there; and let the tents be so large that they fill the holes in the bone.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor. Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin; puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	And some restorers say that one should wet the tents in butter and change them every day. It seems to me that this is not good, but they should be wetted with egg white and flour; then leave the tent until the bone is healed and the cartilage hardened.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a .i. souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi; or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	And sometimes we put goose feathers in the wound instead of tenting, and then a thin cloth around it, and holds the fracture in place, and blows the patient's breath among them; now do as you see fit.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en .i. poc de dyaquilon.	And if warm abscesses arise in the nose while you are working on it, then put on cerate or cotton wetted in rose oil, or a little diaquillon.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis;	And if warm abscesses don't arise, then apply a hot plaster made of flour of linseed, and incense powder, cooked with egg white, then put on light tampons and don't bind the nose.
et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu;	and if the fracture of the nose is small, and it is broken into small pieces, then extract it with suitable instruments for this purpose, then cut the wound, and cure it with warm, healing ointments and poultices, as with plasters and ointments suitable for this purpose;
et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if there is no wound inside the nose, he should treat it with tenting and insert splinters of wood until it heals.
de la routure de la mandibule	of the dislocation of the jaw
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the jaw is dislocated below, and there is no external wound, and the joint is only slightly displaced without any fracture in the bone, it can be easily recognized.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide; et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	If the dislocation is on the right side, you should insert your right index finger into the mouth of the patient; and if the dislocation is on the left side of the jaw, then use the right index finger of the other hand, and gently push it into the dislocation and pull outward with the other hand, keeping the pressure equal on both sides.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en .ij., si covient que tu aministres extension de .ij. pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the break of the jaw is separated into two parts, then you must administer an extension of two parts until it is even.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus .i. drapel double; et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	And if there is movement of the teeth or dislocation, then bind them with a gold, silver, or silk thread, and then place ceratum on the broken jaw, and lay upon it a double cloth; and place upon the cloth a large well-made splint, or a piece of leather the same size, long and wide according to the jaw, and tie it onto the face as tightly as you can, and instruct the patient to rest, and to eat light foods.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet; et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote; et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez; maintes fois est sanez en .iij. semainnes.	And if you see that the jaw is changing shape, then loosen it after three days, and then reset it to its original position; and apply a poultice over it of powder from the mill with an egg or flour of chickpeas, after you have removed the ceratum; and place over the poultice a light layer of lamb's wool, and if the poultice becomes hot, and the condition of the patient does not change, leave it until it is healed; often it is healed within three weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if the jaw is dislocated due to moisture, then you must loosen and reset it, and instruct the patient not to move his jaw; and place over it light lamb's wool; and if you see that it is becoming dislocated, then place over it a piece of leather, or a small cloth, or lamb's wool, and the splint, and the ceratum, and the poultice, according to what is needed.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee; si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	And if there is a fracture and wound together, examine whether any piece of the bone has been removed; then remove it subtly with appropriate instruments for this purpose.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is narrow, widen it with flame according to your need.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus .i. des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have removed all these pieces and there remains none, then close the wound, if it is wide, and place upon it an appropriate poultice to encourage flesh growth, until it is healed.
de la forcele	of the scrotum
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc .iij. manieres: ou elle est brisie et desevree en .ij., et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer; ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	The collarbone breaks many times in front, towards the shoulder, and the break occurs in three ways: it can be broken and separated into two pieces, which is the easiest to heal; or there can be a break with a wound.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies .ij. ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie; et li autres estende lou col vers la partie; puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	And the treatment is, when there is no wound with the break, to have two assistants: one should hold the shoulder where the collarbone is broken; and the other should stretch the neck towards the affected side. Then, with your fingers, adjust the break so that it is aligned and there is no sign or evidence of the break.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit; et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And if you need to extend it further, place a round pillow made of cloth or wool under the shoulder of the patient; and they should relax the collarbone, and you should hold the pillow in your hand, adjusting the break so that it is aligned correctly.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule .i. oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you cannot pull the head of the collarbone out of its socket because it is too deep, then the patient should lie on their back, and place a small pillow under the shoulder, and the assistants should push the shoulder upwards, so that the collarbone bone is raised.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus; et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as; mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	And then address the fracture with your hands, and if you find it broken, you should split it open; gently pull out the pieces, and if the bone cannot be joined due to any protruding piece, cut it off with one of the knives you have; but place the tool under the forceps to direct the syrup.
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre; et ait .ij. chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os;	And it resembles a spoon, and is not hollow, and is as wide as necessary according to the size of the bone and the strength of the work; and has two heads, one wide and the other narrow, depending on the nature of the wound that you made when you treated the bones.
et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	And when you are sure of a warm abscess, cut the wound, and if the opening is small, or if you doubt a warm abscess, dress the wound with bandages and tenting, according to its size.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille .i. drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if hot absesses come, wet a bandage in rosemary oil and garlic and wine, and place it on top.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier;	The stretching of the bone, when there is no wound and no break, is to apply a plaster made from mill dust and egg white onto the bone, and then place light padding on top. If necessary, put a splint underneath the padding.
puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met .i. drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre; puis pren une estele subtil de .iij. dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant;	Then take a very wide strip of cloth about the width of a palm, place a double layer of padding on top of the plaster, and then wrap a thin staff around the bandage so that the end of the bandage hangs loose.
et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide; et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint;	and place the staff over the dislocation, and wrap the bandage around the neck, under the healthy shoulder blade, and then under the affected shoulder blade. Reset it from each side, and when you see that the dislocation is aligned correctly and that the staff does not move over the broken bone, then release the bandage and restrain it again the next day.
et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort .i. petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut; si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a .xx. jors;	and make the patient lie on his back and place a small pillow under the shoulder blade to raise the shoulder while he sleeps. This will ease the dislocation by aligning the shoulder joint, or you can bind the arm to the neck for up to 20 days if no complications arise.
puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez; et elle est restoree au plus en .xxviij. jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	then recommence the poultice, if you see that it is needed, and hold it and leave it thus, until it is restored; and it is restored in at most 28 days, and less for some men.
de la brisure de l’espaule	of the dislocation of the shoulder
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement; si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus .i. drapeil double; puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment; et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor; et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit; et li espaule est restouree en .xx. jors ou en xxv,  Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	It happens that the shoulder is dislocated or displaced in its socket, and it does not hurt unless touched; then adjust it according to the shape of the dislocation, and reset it according to its natural form, in every way you can; then put over the wound powdered flour with egg white, and light bandages, and place over it a double cloth; then place over it a large and thin board, slightly larger than the shoulder, and if under the board there is a swelling on the shoulder, then apply that swelling with linen bandages so that the board lies evenly; and then bind it tightly with a large bandage, so that the board does not move from its place, and check the binding every day; and each time it loosens, tighten it, and adjust the board if it has moved out of position, and let the patient lie on his side; and the shoulder is restored within 20 to 25 days. And when this period is complete, then loosen it, and be sure, for it is not a bone that sets quickly.
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	And if a piece of the bone sticks out above, and not under the heart, then split it open, and the bone, and do as we have said in the dislocation of the shoulder to soothe an abscess with heat.Et se li os est brise, et point tent avant, si met sor le leu de la brisure, un poultice d’uef et de molin, si que li espaule soit frouide; et remettet sor la brisure, un poultice d’uef et de lin, et estoupes legieres, et l’estraint a grant bende.
de la brisure dou pis	of the break in the stone
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc; mais il brise sovent au defuer. Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.
