The penis is sometimes broken in the middle, but this rarely happens; it more often breaks at the tip. And when it is broken in the middle, it hurts a lot, and there is bleeding, and swelling, and discomfort, and sometimes vomiting of blood, and the hair grows on the broken bone, and it feels painful to touch.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met .i. cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des .ij. costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient; puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en .i. drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve; et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint; et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures; puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the treatment is for the patient to lie on his back, and place a pillow between his shoulders, then press his shoulders together and bring the ribs closer together with his hands, making sure the bone is positioned correctly; then apply poultices and bandages over the fracture site, using a light pressure, and wrap it in a cloth, tying it so that it does not move; then wind the bandage around the waist tightly and comfortably, checking every hour to see if it needs tightening; and if there is corrosion or itching or pain or an abscess at the site, quickly remove the bandages and poultices and treat the area as needed; then re-apply the poultice and bandages, tightening them until it is healed.
de la brisure des costes	of the fracture of the ribs
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses; et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	You should know that broken ribs only occur on the large ones in the back and in the chest, and they only bend because they are slippery; this can be discovered through examination of the two areas.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient. Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	And the treatment is that you put it back in place, as it should be. And then apply the plaster, and hold it with a bandage if necessary.
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile; et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	And if the broken ribs are bent downward, the patient feels great pain and piercing, as with pleurisy, because the bone pierces the membrane; they also have a cough and vomit a large amount of blood, which is a serious illness, and the elders have given it great concern.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And there are those who say that one should administer foods that swell the belly, in order to push the broken ribs outward.
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not believe that hot abscesses will come to life unless they have first died down.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	And if it has come, then heal it.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison; toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	And some say that one should put cupping glasses over the area to draw out the excess fluids, and this seems reasonable; however, there is a risk that the cupping glass will draw out the vital fluids due to the weakness of the body.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And some say that one should cover the area with soft wool soaked in hot oil, and place tents between the ribs to apply even pressure all around, then it should be treated with a poultice of pleurisy, meat, and medicine.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz .i. estrument por warder lou syfac; et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les .ij. levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez. Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu; et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the patient feels great pain that he cannot endure due to the bone piercing through the flesh, and there is doubt in the patient, then one should split above the broken rib, and one should place a tool underneath to ward off the pain; and then one must cut the bone and pull gently, and then sew up the two lips of the wound if it is large, and treat it with plasters until it heals. And if a cold abscess comes, then moisten a cloth in rose oil and place it over the spot; and treat the area around the abscess as needed, and let the patient lie carefully on his side where he should, until it is healed.
de la brisure dou col	of the break in the neck
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie; et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	Sometimes there is a break in the bones of the neck, and it can be bent; and also in the spine of the back.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent. Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	And when this happens to someone, and you want to know if he will be healed or not, take note if his hands are soft, swollen, and lifeless, and if he cannot move or straighten them, and if he does not feel it when you poke him with a needle, know that it is a deadly condition in many cases. But if he can move his fingers and feels the pain when they are strained and poked, know that the joint of the bone is saved, and the patient will be healed if proper care is taken.
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit; et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit. Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet. Saiches qu’il est mortelz: si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	And if a similar thing happens to the spine in the back, and you want to know if it is broken or not, then take care whether his feet are swollen, and whether the symptoms are there which occur in paralysis, and in the back wind and involuntary evacuation; and when he is laid on his belly, there is involuntary evacuation. And when he is laid on his back and wants to sit up, he cannot. Know that it is fatal: do not labor over his treatment.
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	And if this accident does not occur, then the condition is lighter.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez; puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer; et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	And the treatment is that you apply a hot poultice to the spine if there is an abscess, and then apply one of the comforting and drying ointments, and bind it with a bandage; and instruct the patient to rest and not sleep on the painful part until he is healed.
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur; et oste l’os, puis assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier; puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if any bone is broken, you should cover it with a bandage; and remove the bone, then bring together the two lips of the wound, if it is large, with a single stitch, then treat it with ointment as needed until it is healed; and if the shoulder-bone is broken, which is called the "bone of the cow," grab your left little finger with your right hand, and apply the poultice and bandage evenly, if you need to; then bind it tightly, and if there is a broken bone, splint it and remove it, and treat the wound until it is healed.
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	of the fracture of the bone of the hip
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief; et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	It may happen that the bone of the hip is fractured, and if it does, there will be a slight lessening at the head; and it extends long and declines to the sides, and brings pain to the area, and puncturing, and swelling in the place that is broken.
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure; et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li; et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	And the restoration is that you extend your hand over it, as far as you can reach the fracture; and know which is the fractured part and its shape; and if the fracture is only at the head, then put it back into place so that it is in its natural shape.
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	And if the fracture extends long, or declines inward, then let the patient lie on his stomach, as far as the restoration of that fracture can be prepared.
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve; et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	And when you have made it even, then apply the plaster, and then put a splint of wood or of horn on top, and hold the fracture still so that it does not move; and treat the area beneath the rib cage until the color is even.
Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	And instruct the patient to sleep on his healthy side or on his back.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit; et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident; et c’est li maniere.	And if swollen abscesses arise, do not touch them until the swollen abscesses are resolved, and apply what we have said before; and then return to restoration, and treat it as appropriate, if there is no bad development; and that is the way to do it.
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	of the shoulder dislocation
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des .ij. manieres: dont l’une est que tu pren .i. fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	The shoulder is that which is between the neck and the head of the shoulder, and if it is broken, it must be restored according to one of two methods. The first method is to take a wooden staff of average thickness, in this shape:
Et lie as .ij. chiés .ij. liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus .i. siege; puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval; puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	Tie the two ends of a rope to the staff, and pull them upward, and let the patient sit on a chair; then have the patient swing his broken arm over the staff until he feels pain in the shoulder, and put a curve in the staff, then stretch him downward while a helper holds him steady; then have the patient hold the break in place with both hands together, until the break is set as it should be.
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a .ij. ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout .i. liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	The other method is to have the patient lean forward over his knees, and tie his hand to his neck; then have one minister hold the broken part in place with his hands, and the others pull on each end of the rope, stretching him apart.
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint .i. liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part. Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes .i. liien moien desoz l’assele, et .i. autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure; et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre .i. liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute; puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if you see that the extraction is too strong, then tie a rope under the break, and over the break, and have each minister pull in their own direction. And if the break is near the head of the shoulder, then you must put one rope gently underneath the shoulder joint, and another towards the neck, over the break; and likewise, if the break is towards the neck, then tie a rope lightly, without labor, so that the break is aligned with its proper location, and with the neck; then align the break as it should be, and hold it in place, unless an abscess forms.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a .vij. jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez; puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein; et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	And if a deep abscess comes, do not drain it until the seventh day, and put soft linen in vinegar and rose oil on the abscess, so that the deep abscess is soothed; then drain it, and the way to drain it is to put the ointment on the break, then assemble the arm above the shoulder, and put your hand on the shoulder or on the breast; and put the cloth, and drain above the shoulder, and above the arm, so that the arm is in place, if nothing moves it or if the bone is not moved.
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele .i. doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure .iij. dois de chescune part; puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	And if you doubt that the bone will move, use a splint, and put a larger and stronger splint over the break, with an inch of space between each splint, and let each splint be large enough that it extends 3 inches beyond the break on each side; then drain over the splints, as I said at the beginning of the chapter, more strongly and less slowly.
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit; puis regarde chescuns .iij. jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois. Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	And if you see the position of the splints and the draining, as we have said, in the hour that you restore the broken member, and you doubt the deep abscess, then leave it bound until the seventh day, as we have said; then examine the bandage every 3 days, so that itching or swelling does not come to the site, or the pus cannot come to the member because it is too tight. Then loosen it, as we have said.
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés .iij. jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac; et met desoz l’ajutoire .i. cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens; si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz; et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse. Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en .xl. jors dou tout; et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.  Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier .l. jors ou .ij. mois.	And if such accidents do not occur, then it should be dislocated no sooner than three days or more; and the patient should sleep on his back, and keep his hands on his stomach; and place underneath the shoulder a plain woolen cushion evenly, and watch every hour of the day or night that the figure of the broken limb does not move, or soften the ligament; then treat it with medicine, and give him the meat we have mentioned earlier, in such a way that the meat is at first subtle; and when he begins to recover, make it thicker. And it is customary for the shoulder and leg to be treated for forty days altogether; and then it should be dislocated and administered baths and medicines of ointments to heal the area. And if the dislocation is severe and swollen, it should remain dislocated for one or two months.
de la brisure du bras	of the fracture of the arm
Li bras est compos de .ij. os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet; et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi; par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	The arm is composed of two bones, which are called the "ulna" and the "radius". The ulna is smaller and is located near the armpit, while the radius is larger and is situated below the small finger. Sometimes only the large bone breaks, sometimes only the small one, and sometimes both together.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations; et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble. Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	When the small bones are broken, their restoration and healing is easy; but when the large bones are broken, healing is difficult, and more painful than when they are broken together. If only a small bone is broken, it should be extended slightly and set evenly.
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort; et l’estende sus .i. cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et .i. cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor; puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a .i. liien, et uns autres ministres a .i. autre au desus. Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	And if it is the large bone, it must be pulled harder; and he should extend himself on a cushion, and hold the pouch of his hand higher than the others, and the small fingers lower than the other fingers, and he should cross his arms over his chest, and there should be a cushion in front of him, so that the patient does not experience any pain; then the minister should extend his arm to the part below his hand, or to the elbow, and another minister above. Then he should set the splint evenly according to its best form.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	And if in the fracture there are pieces, place each one in its place, and if any stick in the heart, and you cannot restore it to its place, then make an incision through the skin and bone, as we have said before.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler; si pren la cure.	And if there is a wound with the fracture, I have spoken about it in the individual chapter; take the cure.
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue .i. drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz; et lie .i. drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez. Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres; et saiches que il doit avoir vj. esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions: soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en .ij.; et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre; et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres; et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit. Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	And if in the beginning of the restoration, there are hot abscesses, then apply .i. bandage of cerotic ointment made from rose oil and white wax, neither too hard nor too soft; and bind .i. bandage over it gently, until the hot abscess is soothed. And then remove the cerotic ointment, and apply the plaster of mill-powder with egg white, then put on the splints, and let the splint of the fracture be a little stronger and larger than the others; and understand that he must have six splints on his arm in various positions: whether the fracture is in one or two bones; and bind more tightly over the fracture than anywhere else, and every day looser as I said at the beginning of the chapter; and let the bandages over the fracture be soft and moist, neither hard nor rough; and let the thread with which he is bound be made of linen, neither too thick nor too fine, as we have said. And re-examine the limb and the binding after a few days.
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez; et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer. Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	And if any bad accident happens to the limb, as itching coming to it, then you must wash the limb with warm water until the itching is soothed; and let the limb not be bound tightly but rather loose. And then begin the binding again, and if the ligature becomes soft and the bone dislocated, and similar things, then treat it again.
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses .i. poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	And if you perceive that the nourishment cannot reach the limb because it is too tight, then you must loosen it a little and leave it like that for some days, until the nourishment reaches it; and then bind it again.
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a .xx. jors. ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos; et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en .xxx. jors ou en .xxxv., et par aventure en .xx. jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	And if none of the things we have said come to the patient, do not release him until twenty days have passed or until around that time; then he can wash his hands, and his neck should be even, and he should guard against movement and exertion, and sleep on his back; and know that this fracture is restored in 30 or 35 days, and perhaps in 20 days, according to the compositions and complexes of the virtues.
de la brisure de la main	of the fracture of the hand
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	Know that in the back of the hand and at the base of the fingers there are few fractures, and they only come from bending many times.
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement; puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint; et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu; et soit envoloupee en .i. drapeil de lin.	And when the palm of the hand is broken or bent, one should make the patient's arm straight, and have him extend his hand and straighten the broken bones as much as possible; then he should place an emetic on the skin, and if there is no abscess, then he should apply a poultice. Then the patient should rest for 24 hours in a comfortable position, with the affected area elevated above the heart, and keep the wound clean and dry to prevent infection.
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie; et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	And if the fracture is around the stomach of the plant, make a sphere of fabrics, and instruct the patient to hold it against their broken plant; then stretch it with a long strip of fabric, and hold the cloth in place with a hot candle as big as the palm of your hand, stretching it as needed.
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	And if the fracture is on the outside, you should place one cloth on top and another underneath the plant, so that the hand is open and straight; then bind it all around the hand, and stop the bleeding between the fingers.
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient; et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve; et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés; ou tu les lie toz en .i. tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet; et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	And if the fracture is on one of the fingers, if it's the thumb, set it straight as needed and hold it in place; and if the fracture is on another finger, like the index finger or another, straighten it and bind it to the adjacent healthy finger; or you can bind them all together, whichever is easier, or you can place a cloth on top, like a poultice; take care with the restoration and treatment of a hot abscess, and dry up any fluid that arises, as I have said.
de la cuixe brisie	of the broken thigh
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier; et li restauration si est c’on lie .i. liien desus la briseure, et .i. autre desoz.	The bones of the thigh are often broken, and one can see this when they move forward and backward; their restoration is by binding one above the fracture and another below.
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment; et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	And the patient lies on his face, then each assistant stretches their band to their side equally; and this is when the fracture is within the bone.
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure. Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval; puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses .ij. mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	And if the fracture is close to the root of the thigh, then one band should be towards the buttock, and the other band below the fracture. And likewise, if it is close to the knee, then the band should be beyond the knee, and the extension should be down; then the assistants should put the bone back into its natural position with their two hands, and then apply the poultice and bandage, unless an abscess forms there.
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure; li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	And if there is a hot abscess, let it subside and then return to your work and treatment; the bandage is done in the following way.
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure .i. bendeil dur doublé en .ij. ou .iij., et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute .i. fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus; puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe; puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment .iij. tors ou iiij. sus la briseure; et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint; puis enten as .ij. chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie .iij. esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet; et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	You should wrap a bandage around the fracture—a tough, doubled length of cloth two or three times—and leave the excess, then turn the leg so that the heel comes to the root of the shin, and thread a long strand between the thigh and the leg, below the knee, so that the end of the strand comes up above; then return to the leg and the thigh with the bandage, then place splints over the fracture, and put a splint on the bone of the leg; then fill the space between the leg and the thigh with soft rags to even out the pressure, then begin to tie tightly three or four times around the fracture; and when you go higher up over the fracture, lessen the pressure; then tie two strands of the thread that you have threaded between the leg and the thigh, and tie three splints that are above, then return below to the end of the thread, so that you come by the foot; and tighten it, so that it does not move from its place, then leave it thus until no swelling or inflammation or anything similar comes.
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois; et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet; et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	And if something happens there, then loosen it and address what is happening, as we have said many times; and if there are pieces of bone sticking out, they should be removed if possible; and if not, then the area should be split open and the wound cleaned, as we have said, until it is healed.
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras; toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	And sometimes the thigh is broken in this way when splints are placed on it, as in the shoulder and arm; nevertheless, with treatment made in this way, the patient is not healed.
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en .l. jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	And you shall know that the leg is restored in one day or a little less or more, according to the different complexions.
de la ruelle dou genoil	of the groove of the knee
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois. Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou .i. pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	You shall know that in the groove of the knee there is little bruising, but it bends many times. And if it breaks, it is only a single fracture, or a hole, and it happens with and without wound, and it feels good to everyone.
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet; puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant; si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is to put it back in place with the fingers, as long as it can be; then apply the plaster, and if necessary, put on a round splint, and bind it as it should be, then follow all the instructions we have given for other fractures, such as hot abscesses and similar conditions; then treat each incident as needed until it is healed.
de la brisure de la jambe	of the fracture of the leg
Saiches que en la jambe ait .ij. os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»; et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i.	You should know that in the leg there are two bones, one of which is properly called the "tibia," and the other is called the "fibula"; and all other breaks occur as they do in the arm, and therefore their treatment is the same, and the procedures are all alike.
Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	And if both bones are broken together, then the leg is turned completely inside out.
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	And if only the small bones are broken, then it turns forward.
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien; et torne desoz. Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement; mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere; et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	And if the large bone is broken, one feels great pain and sees it well; and it turns underneath. Therefore, administer extension, and make it even, and bind the splints evenly; but nonetheless, if the fracture is ugly, and there are several pieces, then the extension should be less and lighter; and adjust it according to your skill.
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren .ij. faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz; puis envoloupe en .ij. leus .i. bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien; et aucun i aministrent .i. bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie; et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident; si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have completed your work, take two wooden splints that reach from the top of the leg to below the knee on either side; then wrap two bandages around them, one above and one below, and tie it in the middle as well, and at this point the leg should not be able to bend to the right or left, and thus it is well; and some administer a wooden bar that extends from the top of the leg, and they place the leg upon it so as to prevent movement, and properly they apply it at the break where there is pain; and move the leg every day to check for any hot abscesses or other accidents; and treat until healed.
de la brisure des os dou piet	from the fracture of the bones of the foot
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	At the ankle there is no fracture, but at the foot there can be a fracture and in both feet, and there is only bruise in various positions.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus; puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a .ij. chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	If the leg bone is broken and you see the bones protruding above each other, then have the patient lie on his back as if he were walking, and then place your foot on top of his, where the bones are raised, and then press down until they return to their places; then apply the ointment and bandages, and put a small, flat stone under the arch of the foot, and then bind it firmly in place with bandages and other materials as needed.
Et quant .iij. jors ou .iiij. seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	And when three or four days have passed, loosen the bandage, for you will find the bones healed, whether broken or dislocated.
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main; puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment; et s’il en i a .ij. ou .iij., ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en .i. drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet; et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	And if any of the toes are broken, treat them as we have said for the fingers of the hand; then place a splint along the length of the toe, making it slightly larger, and place under the foot the stone that I have described, and bind it firmly in place; and if there are two or three, or more, broken, place a splint on each toe according to its size, wrapped in a linen cloth, and tighten the stone underneath the foot; and let the top of the stone press firmly against the sole of the foot.
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit; et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	And you must not forget the other things that I have said about other fractures, from what we have already discussed; and treat each case as it requires.
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	of the fracture of the bone of the finger
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier; puis emplisse li baile la nature de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com .i. sto; puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto; et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice .vij. jors ou entor: si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature; puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens: la nature si revenra li brisure; puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the bone of a woman's nature is fractured, have her sit up and lean forward, then bend her back backwards; next, fill the vagina with cotton, placing pieces as large as an egg inside; then help the woman to stand, lifting her back slightly, and the cotton will emerge with the egg when it reaches the opening of the vagina, taking the bone with it; after she urinates, remove the cotton, and repeat this process for seven days; the fracture will be healed. If you wish, take a goat's bladder, tie a string to its opening, fill the bladder with air by blowing through the string until it is inflated inside the vagina; the bone will be drawn back into place by the pressure; then fill the vagina with cotton and leave it there for several days until it heals.
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche; et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre. Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration: enten le donques.	And when the bone of a man's or a woman's finger is fractured, it is restored in the same way as we have described for the hip bone; these fractures are not hidden from those who devote themselves to studying and understanding my book. For the fractures teach us, through their various arrangements, the right path to restoration; listen, therefore, and learn.
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge; puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse .iij. jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	For a broken penis, take a goose's gullet and insert the penis into it; then wrap a cloth around it and leave it for three days, checking on it occasionally, and it will heal quickly.
de brisure avec plaie	of fracture with wound
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	It is necessary for one who has a fracture with a wound, especially if it is large, like the bone of the thigh or shoulder, or similar, to be bled immediately, in accordance with the bleeding we have described earlier.
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the wound heals, then remove the vitriol, if you don't have anything else, and then start to reset the fracture in that same hour, or that day, if no abscesses appear.Et si la brisure est en jointe de corps, ou il n’y a pas de plaie, s’il le peut demourer ains que il n’y ait pas de contusion ou de lesion, qu’il demoure assiez sans se muevre, si com nos avons dit avant.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	And if the fracture is in a joint of the body, or there is no wound, if it can remain without movement causing contusion or injury, it should remain seated and still as we have said before. And if abscesses appear, then leave the reset until the next day, as long as the abscesses are soothed, and don't touch them on the third or fourth day, because you would bring about a bad accident.Et si li membres sont contuziez ou les os briziez, et qu’il ne demourent pas adés, si covient que tu remettes le membre a son leu, et le repos par tuit le jor, et la nuit, et la matinee, et par tuit l’endit qu’il doit demourer asez.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	And if the broken bone is apparent on the uncovered heart, then you must gently put it in place with your hands, with a small extension.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a .vij. dois ou .viij. de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie; et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne .iii. ou iiij., selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure; et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	And if the extension is not apparent to you to make it equal with your hands, then reset it with this instrument which is made of iron and is seven or eight inches long, and the width is according to the amount of the injury; and for this reason, it is necessary for the surgeon to press into the wound three or four times, according to what he needs in each case of broken bone; and let it be round and somewhat thick so that it does not bend under pressure on the limb while you are working, and let it be pointed at the end, and thick from the middle forward, thus:
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent; et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre. Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	And it is called a "splint", because the curved shoulder should be placed over the visible head of the bone; and the bandage is wrapped around once, as tightly as possible, so that the bones are brought together and made even. And if the fracture is small, and the instrument cannot grip the bone well, then you must cut notches in the head of the bone so that the instrument can get a good hold.
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir; puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	And if you cannot reset the bone as we have said, then cut it with a suitable instrument, either an incision or a saw, according to your ability; then take out what remains in the bone of splintered pieces and small fragments.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil. Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille .i. drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit; et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption; puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure; et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois; et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	And when the bone is put back in place and the patient feels great pain afterward, know that it is not in its natural place. Do this until it is in its proper place, then wet a cloth with black wine vinegar and apply it carefully to the area; do not put any ointment or anything else on the wound that would cause pus and corruption. Then administer poultices once you have set the bone, leave the wound uncovered, and wrap the bandage all around according to the size of the wound; be very careful that the wound is not constricted by the binding. And many times fools have done this and have caused death or corrosion on the patient; the constriction should be looser than other bindings.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles; mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie. Et quant tu vois aprés .i. jor ou .ij. enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	And if the wound is large or deep, and you fear that harm may come to it as we have said, and you feel pain in the area, then do not put poultices on it; but wrap around it, instead of poultices, hard cloths tied tightly. And when you see after a day or two swelling at the wound, remove what you put over it completely, and apply ointment that heals wounds, such as tetrafarmaçon ointment and similar.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre .ij. fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	And you should loosen the limb twice a day, in the morning and evening, until it is healed and closed.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	And one must prepare the limbs in such a way that the bowstring runs smoothly downward.
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	And if they persist for many days, and it cannot heal but keeps dislocating the bowstring, know that there are tiny pieces of bone causing this, so you must probe the wound with a needle, and remove all the broken pieces causing the pain.
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant. Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse; par aventure cherra par lui aprés .xx. jors ou .xxx., puis cure la plaie, se tu pues; et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	And if a fistula or other form of corruption appears, then one must treat it according to what he says in his chapter above. And when the bone is broken and open on the limb, as with the bones of the thigh or shoulder, and similar large bones, do not split it, for many die from this, but leave it until it calluses over; perhaps it will fall off after 20 or 30 days, then cure the wound if you can, and if you cannot, then leave it.
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	of bruises that come upon the healing
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre; et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	There are many times after the healing of a fracture, especially when it is near a joint, that an ugly sight appears in the member; and by chance the member cannot perform its natural functions.
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres: si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil; et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors; et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee; ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite; car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres; et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent; ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Take care then that the patient is free of moisture: if the medic gives astringent remedies such as aloe, incense, myrrh, sarcocolla and similar, so that you grind one or all of these substances together and mix them with wine, vinegar, egg white, or garlic; and put it on the night-time as poultices, and hold it firmly in place and do not remove it for several days; then remove it and start again until the swelling is gone. Or press it onto a well-made piece of plaster; for the property of plaster is that it removes all swellings from the limbs; if the swelling has become as hard as stone, and there is a need to remove it, cut into it, and make the excess apparent; or have it cut by some surgeon so that it is removed and healed.
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	of the limb which is weak after healing
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes: de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit; ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre; ou por multitude d’arosement; ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre; ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	When the bone fracture is healed, and the limb remains weak and thin, this happens for many reasons: one is that it was bound too tightly, and not bound as it should have been; or because there were too many bandages, and the limb could not receive nourishment; or due to excessive swelling; or due to too much movement, and not at the right time; or because there is a lack of blood in the body, and so it is weak.
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui; et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce; puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre; et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	And the cure is that you should make the patient eat and drink to soften his body so that blood multiplies within him; and give him a bath, and joy and relaxation; then apply pitch to the affected member, so that the pitch attracts it to itself greatly, and often wash it with warm water until the pitch is drawn out to the member and it returns to its natural shape.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	and the limb straightens after health
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil: si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre; et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors; toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses; et li fai .i. emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus; ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	When the member is crooked after healing, and the broken bone opens, and the shape of the member is deformed, nonetheless it does not lose its natural function; yet one must not believe foolish people who say that the limb should be broken again completely anew, and many fools have done this in our land; and these actions are blamed, and great harm results, and sometimes death; nevertheless, if the dislocations and tortures are recent, one should wash them with warm water, or cook softening herbs such as marshmallow leaves, and roots, and mallow, and similar medicines that soften. And you make a soothing ointment, such as well-prepared diaquilon, and you take the mucilage of marshmallow, and confit it with goose fat or sesamen oil, and apply it as an ointment; or you take figs, and grind them with colon fodder, and similar medicines that soften.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes. Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	And sometimes the dislocation is opened by constantly rubbing and lengthening it with moist hands. And movement should be encouraged in the member every hour.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement; et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	And if the crookedness is awoken and hardened like stone, and it needs to be removed with iron, then one must cut it to the bone with a subtle incision; and apply poultice and care in the treatment.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	Here begins the book of dislocations.
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocation occurs when a joint moves out of its place, which prevents it from moving, and the limb is misaligned, causing the patient great pain and injury.
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When dislocation occurs in someone, one must now reset it without delay.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu; por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez: maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors;	For if one delays, the place will swell and by chance be reset to its place; therefore, one should not move it at all when it is swollen: many times this brings about phlegm and other pains.
toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez; puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	However, when this happens, let the patient bleed, then leave it until the abscesses are drained; then raise the member with warm water and oil, then reset it gently, and treat each member as the healing comes to its place.
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	And I have arranged the chapters on dislocations of the head down to the feet.
des mandibules	of the jaws
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc .ij. manieres: ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc; ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	Then the jaws become dislocated and the dislocations of both are in two ways: they are slightly displaced from their place and softened a little; or they are entirely dislocated and hang down towards the feet, and saliva flows from the mouth which he cannot hold back, nor can he close his mouth, and his tongue is enveloped with speech.
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	When the dislocation is small, it returns through various positions.
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie;	And if it is complete and accomplished, you must reset it quickly and not delay.
et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de .ij. pars; et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal; et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	And in such a way that the minister grabs the head of the patient, and pushes his fingers into the root of the dislocation of the jaw inside the mouth, if the dislocation is on both sides; and let the other two hands be relaxed, to apply pressure equally; and instruct the patient to soften his jaws and move them in all parts.
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	And she looks at it equally, until it returns to its place.
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les .ij. mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement; ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	And if it is stuck, especially if both jaws are together, then they should be soaked in warm water and oil, so that they are gently reset; do not pull hard on the jaw, as we have said.
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens;	And when they are reset equally, and the mouth of the patient is closed well without softening, then place damp cloths on it made from rose oil and wax, then tie it gently with soft bandages.
et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre .ij. cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules;	and let the patient sleep on his back, and let his shoulders be between two pillows, so that he does not move them to the right or left, nor effort to chew, but take soft food, until the pains are removed, and the jaws are bound;
et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	and then eat what he wants lightly, and do not bother to open his mouth to eat and drink as long as the jaw is well bound and healed.
Et se les .ij. mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	And if the two jaws cannot be reset in an hour and are not converted to their place, then come fever and usual sickness, and perhaps intestinal distress, and perhaps vomiting of pure bile.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions; et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en .viiij. jors.	And when you see this, then know that it is deadly; and many die from it within eight days.
de la forcelle	of the fork
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	The forceless cannot dislodge from the ribs within its continuance of the armpit, and it is dislodged sometimes to the outside, and they feel it well.
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras; et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra; puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint;	And the restoration is that the patient lies on his back and extends his arms; then he presses the area firmly with his palm, and it will return to place; then apply the ointment and bandage, and keep it tight.
et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer; se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit; puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez;	And the shoulder which is toward the armpit cannot be dislodged; if it can be moved at all, and if it does move, then put it back in place as we have said; then apply the ointment and bandage, and keep it tight, and instruct the patient to rest until he is healed.
et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	And in the same way, the shoulder blade is put back into place when it has been dislocated from its socket.
de la dislocation de l’espaule	of the dislocation of the shoulder
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc .iij. manieres: de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz; et li seconde est a la partie dou pis; et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc;	You know that the shoulder is dislocated in three ways: one way it dislocates at the part of the acromion below; and the second is at the part of the foot; and by chance it dislocates above, and this happens rarely.
et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners; et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment; a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	It never dislocates behind the shoulder, and it never dislocates inward for the nerves; and many times it dislocates below towards the acromion, especially in those who have little flesh, because in them it is forced out violently; but in those who have enough flesh, it slips out gently and goes back in gently.
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	And by chance it happens to some men that they get a concussion or a fracture, and the shoulder swells from a hot abscess, and they think it is dislocated because of this.
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains; et adonques encomence la cure.	Therefore you must test it until you are certain of its effectiveness; then begin the treatment.
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste;	And you will know there is a dislocation when it sinks towards the armpit, and there is a difference between the sick shoulder and the healthy one, and you will find a manifest difference between them.
et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes; et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens;	And you will find a pit at the head of the shoulder, and under the armpit at the top of the shoulder, as if it were an egg; and the patient cannot bring his hand to his nose, nor move in any way;
et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier;	and also, if it is dislocated upwards, it is not hidden, for you can clearly see it by touch;
et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	and this method of dislocation is not difficult to cure when it is new, or if the child is ill.
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu; et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz; si venra hastanment.	And the method is that the minister lifts the hand of the sick person up high, then places his fingers under the shoulder blade, and raises the joint with force to its place; and the minister lifts the hand and extends it upward, then lowers it; and it will come back into place quickly.
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude; et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree;	And if it does not come back into place as we have said within several days, then the sick person should be bathed in warm water; and he should be anointed with softening and soothing ointments, such as a decoction of aniseed and fenugreek and mullein in water, and he should be made comfortable.
puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide;	Then the minister should press on the sick person's back, and place a layer of wool under the shoulder blade, neither too soft nor too hard, then he should place his heel on the wool and lift the head of the shoulder gently, and pull the hand of the sick person.
et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval; celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere:	and other ministers dye the head of the patient so that it does not move downward; the shoulder will return right away, and if you see that it is reset according to this way:
et est que tu faices estre present .i. home qui soit plus grans que li malaides; et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar;	and it is that you have a man present who is larger than the patient; and let him stand straight towards the side of the patient, and press his shoulder under the armpit of the patient, and lift the armpit upward, so that the patient hangs in the air;
et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre. Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	and another minister pulls the arm of the patient downward towards the belly. And if the patient is too light, they can use something heavy with them, and the dislocation will return right away.
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere: et est c’on fiche .i. lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com .i. pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile;	And it is reset in another way as well: and one is to thrust a long stick into the ground, so that its head is as high as a palm, and not too thick nor too thin;
puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust; puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment;	then it should be placed under the patient, but with a soft cloth on top, and the patient should be upright and still; then his hand should be stretched out below on the other side, and the joint will return to its place gradually;
et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure: pren .i. tison de .ij. bras de grant et .iiij. dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	and if it does not want to return due to all these things that we have said, then perform this cure: take a stick 1 yard long and 2 inches wide, with a hooked end to fit into the joint, according to this form:
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide; et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus .i. eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part: li jointure reva ens maintenant.	then tie a soft cloth to the end of the stick so that the stick does not hurt the patient, then place it under the joint of the patient; stretch out his arm along the length of the stick, and tie the shoulder to the stick, and the arm to the head of the stick; then place the arm on top of a pillow, and stretch out the hand below, and let the body hang on the other side: the joint will return now.
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	And when it is in place, in whatever way it is, you should then place a woolen sphere under the joint, then apply the prepared plaster made from mill dust, incense, and egg white, all over the shoulder and around it; then tighten it under the joint gradually, and tie the string onto the plaster, and hold the hand to his chest, and let the hand remain like this.
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost; et puis menjuce plus aprés .v. jors ou .vij., et le mueve; et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	And he must eat little, as long as the limb is comfortable, for it will heal faster; and then eat more after five or seven days, and move it; and if it is stiff and not softened, it will be healed.
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a iij. pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	And if the joint is dislocated due to moisture that it has encountered, or for any other reason, then you should administer cautery to three openings, as described in the chapter on cautery.
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés .vij. jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis; et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	And if you do all this and it still dislocates after seven days, and the joint does not hold, and he cannot lift his arm upwards, then you should know that the nerves at the top of the shoulder are torn or stretched or relaxed; and you should know that the joint will never be fixed in its place.
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure; et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Dislocation that is towards the bottom, and the breasts, or behind, is done by pushing and stretching with the hands, and one should treat it in the same way until it is healed.And if there is dislocation of the jaw, one should not let the patient eat anything hard for as long as the joint is uncomfortable, so that it can heal quickly; and then he can eat more after five or seven days, and move his jaw; and if it is stiff and not softened, it will be healed.
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	And if after healing, there is pain in the limb, and with movement, the patient suffers many times, until that pain is relieved and returns to its original state.
de la dislocation dou coute	from the dislocation of the shoulder
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient; et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien; et desalue selonc chescune figure.	You know that the joint of the shoulder is dislocated by pins, and it returns with pins; and if it is dislocated everywhere, especially in front and behind, and the dislocation is not reduced, for one sees and feels it well, and it dislocates according to each figure.
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement. Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	And when you join the dislocated shoulder with the healthy one, you can see it clearly. For the joint is twisted, and cannot bend the arm or touch its shoulder at all.
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener; et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier; si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	And you must reset it so that the abscesses heal, for if the abscesses heal, then it will be painful to reset; and by chance it may not be able to be fully reset, especially when it is in the back; so it is worse than other dislocations, and causes more pain, and death may result.
Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes .ij. mains; et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.	And the restoration is, when it can be reset, that you extend its hand with your two hands; and its arms should be spread out, and the hands bent according to the elbow, around and underneath, and push the joint into its socket at its wrist, or at the root of its palm, until it returns to its place.
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	And if the dislocation is in front, it will return when he bends his hand towards his hand, and strain at the root of the palm where it is dislocated.
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension; et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension; puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large;	And if it does not want to return to its place, then give strong extension; and it is that two ministers extend the arm, and two ministers pull, so that he does not move with the extension; then turn the arm from each side, after you have wrapped a long and wide cloth around it;
et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne;	and when he looks at the joint in his hand, then he should anoint it with oil to soften the joint, and then bend the joint properly so that it recovers.
et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie.	and when it is in place, he should put a dry poultice on it with egg white, and hold the joint tightly, and bandage the arm to the neck of the dislocation, and leave it for some days, then loosen it.
Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse; et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis; puis le deslie.	And if the joint is firm in its place, then loosen the bandage and leave it; and if you see that the joint is not healing well, then reapply the poultice and the bandage, and leave it for some days until it is firmly in place; then loosen it.
